1401 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tibbetts


NO. 5-02-0822


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 921; 815 N.E.2d 409; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 975; 287 Ill. Dec. 6



August 17, 2004, Decided  
August 17, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to Publish Granted August 17, 2004. As Corrected September 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rule 23 Order filed July 8, 2004. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Wabash County. Nos. 02-CF-14, 02-CM-20, & 02-DT-12. Honorable James V. Hill, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.1 (2000), appellant motorist's license was summarily suspended for three years as a third-time driving under the influence (DUI) offender. He petitioned to rescind the suspension. The Circuit Court of Wabash County, Illinois, found that he had failed to establish a prima facie case and dismissed his petition. The motorist appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist claimed he did not refuse to submit to chemical testing because he agreed to a breath test and was physically and medically unable to submit to a blood test. The officer denied asking the motorist to take a breath test. The appellate court held that the trial court, in ruling on appellee State's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1110 (2002) motion, was not required to view the evidence in the light most favorable to the motorist, but properly judged the credibility of the motorist's evidence in finding that he failed to make a prima facie case under 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-118.1 (2002). The motorist failed to put on medical or other corroborating testimony regarding his fear of having blood drawn, or that it was physically or psychologically impossible for him to take a blood test. The officer was not required to articulate a need for a blood test before requesting one; moreover, as he found cannabis in the motorist's van, and blood test results were necessary to establish if a driver was under the influence of drugs, his decision was reasonable. 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501.1(c) and (d) (2000) were not unconstitutionally vague and did not deprive the motorist of due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1402 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Vill. of Chatham v. County of Sangamon


NO. 4-03-0878


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 889; 814 N.E.2d 216; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 952; 286 Ill. Dec. 566



August 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 7, 2004.
Appeal granted by Vill. of Chatham v. County of Sangamon, 212 Ill. 2d 529, 824 N.E.2d 283, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1872, 291 Ill. Dec. 707 (2004)
Affirmed by Vill. of Chatham v. County of Sangamon, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 967 (Ill., Sept. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 02MR161. Honorable Leslie J. Graves, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff village and found that Division 15.1, (65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-15.1-1 through 11-15.1-5 (2002)) of the Municipal Code, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-1-1 through 11-152-4 (2002), granted the village zoning and building-code jurisdiction over lands subject to annexation agreements.


OVERVIEW: The village filed a complaint against the county for declaratory judgment that it had zoning and building-code jurisdiction over certain lands that were subject to annexation agreements. The county filed a counterclaim for declaratory judgment that it, not the village, had legal jurisdiction over the lands for zoning and building code purposes. The court affirmed the trial court. Resolution of the case required the interpretation of 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-13-1, 11-15.1-2 (2002) and 55 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-1063 (2002). While the language of the three statutes was clear and unambiguous, the statutes were in direct conflict with one another. The court had previously held that an annexing municipality's subdivision and zoning jurisdiction overrode another municipality's statutory grant of planning jurisdiction. The same held true for the county's statutory zoning grant. Thus, the trial court properly ruled that Division 15.1 controlled the issue presented to it. On its affirmative defenses, the county failed to prove that the classification system in 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-15.1-2.1 (2002) was arbitrary or that it was an invalid use of legislative police power.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which granted summary judgment in favor of the village, was affirmed.

 

1403 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Spivey


No. 1-03-1810


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


351 Ill. App. 3d 763; 814 N.E.2d 925; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 929; 286 Ill. Dec. 699



August 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 20, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 23406. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of unlawful use of a weapon (UUW) by a felon in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1)(3)(A) (2002). He challenged the constitutionality of the statute and the sufficiency of the evidence. He also argued that he had not received all the admonishments required by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(a) and that there was an error in the mittimus.


OVERVIEW: Police investigating young people with apparent gang affiliations loitering at night in a city park pursued defendant as he fled on a bicycle. Each saw him remove an object from his waistband and fling it away. One officer never took his eyes off the object, which proved to be a gun. The appellate court upheld his UUW conviction, first finding that since the UUW statute rationally related to the legitimate government aim of preventing violence and, moreover, required scienter of knowledge, it did not violate substantive due process. Furthermore, the evidence of the two officers was ample to support conviction, despite slight discrepancies that naturally occurred when each saw the action from a different perspective. Defendant had stipulated to a previous felony conviction, so he could not complain of the State's failure to prove it. Although the trial court gave most of the required admonishments at sentencing, there was an apparently inadvertent omission of an admonishment regarding the right to move for reconsideration of sentence. That error was harmless, since defendant had not shown any resulting prejudice. Finally, a wording error in the mittimus was corrected.


OUTCOME: The court corrected the slight error in the mittimus, which the State had conceded, and affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

 

1404 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. Diener


NO. 4-03-0750


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


351 Ill. App. 3d 645; 814 N.E.2d 187; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 940; 286 Ill. Dec. 537



August 4, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 7, 2004.
Appeal denied by Thomas v. Diener, 824 N.E.2d 292, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1850, 291 Ill. Dec. 716 (Ill., Nov. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Douglas County. No. 01LM32. Honorable Frank W. Lincoln, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant former employer of a child support obligor appealed from a Douglas County Circuit Court (Illinois) judgment that imposed an enormous penalty on him, payable to plaintiff obligee, for allegedly knowingly failing to pay withheld child support within seven days, as required by 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 (2000). He argued that the trial court misinterpreted the statute and, in the alternative, that it was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: The employer, who did not handle payroll, knew little about when the support checks were paid; his son was the only witness regarding the manner in which the son, as bookkeeper, handled the checks. His practice was to mail everything out, pay and child support, the Saturday of the week after the pay period had ended. The appellate court held, first, that under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/15(b-5) (2002), the seven-day period did not run on Saturdays, so the mailings were timely, if otherwise proper. In a country town with no mailboxes, mailing occurred when the son followed his customary practice of putting the stamped letters out for the carrier to pick up that day. 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 28/35 made it clear that the employer was to be regarded as having made payment when mailing occurred, and so the trial court's finding that payment was made only upon arrival and date-stamping at the collection unit was manifestly erroneous, given that the son's evidence was uncontradicted. Although the employer's records of payment showed a few other irregularities, they could be attributed to oversight, and the finding that they were knowing was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1405 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nicholas


1-02-0828


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


351 Ill. App. 3d 433; 813 N.E.2d 1057; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 836; 286 Ill. Dec. 364



July 9, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 25, 2004.
Appeal granted by People v. Nicholas, 212 Ill. 2d 547, 824 N.E.2d 289, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1739, 291 Ill. Dec. 713 (2004)
Reversed by, Judgment entered by People v. Nicholas, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1629 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)
Reversed by People v. Nicholas, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 308 (Ill., Jan. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From The Circuit Court Of Cook County. Honorable Joseph G. Kazmierski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court reversed; cause remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after he was convicted in the Circuit Court Of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of first degree murder of his mother.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of shooting his mother. He was questioned by the police over an extended period of time. He was given food, drinks, and cigarettes and was otherwise treated fairly. Defendant gave two oral confessions before he spoke with an attorney and invoked his right to remain silent. Thereafter, defendant agreed to give the police a court-reported statement. Although defendant was placed under arrest after his first oral confession, he was not taken before a judge. He was kept "past call" while the police investigation continued. On appeal, defendant asserted three errors, including error in the failure to suppress his court-reported statement. The court reversed, holding that (1) the statement should have been suppressed because it was tainted by the failure to take defendant promptly before a judge for a 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/109-1(a) (1998) hearing and by the failure of the police to cease questioning defendant after he exercised his right to remain silent; (2) the trial court properly refused to give an involuntary manslaughter instruction; and (3) the prosecutor's repeated references to defendant as "pure evil" were improper and denied defendant a fair trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and his case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1406 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Winters


No. 1-02-2790


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 747; 812 N.E.2d 737; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 793; 285 Ill. Dec. 917



June 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Winters, 823 N.E.2d 978, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1546 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 12486. The Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder under a theory of accountability. He was sentenced to a mandatory life sentence under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (1998) because he had been convicted of the murders of more than one person. Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the appellate court's order remanding the case for resentencing implied that the sentence was discretionary. The appellate court's mandate unambiguously stated that defendant was to be resentenced under the prior version of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii). As defendant conceded, that version clearly required a mandatory life sentence for the murders of more than one person. Thus, defendant's natural life sentence was mandatory. Defendant alternatively argued that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) was unconstitutional as applied to him under the Illinois Supreme Court's decision in People v. Miller. However, the appellate court concluded that People v. Miller did not apply to defendant, a "young" adult, regardless of his allegedly passive participation in the murders because defendant was an adult at the time the murders were committed, making his life sentence mandatory and the degree of his participation in the murders irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. In addition, the appellate court granted the State's request that defendant be assessed $ 100 as costs for the State's defense of the appeal.

People v. Taylor


No. 2-03-0138


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 839; 812 N.E.2d 759; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 831; 285 Ill. Dec. 939



June 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 02-CM-3755. Honorable Joseph R. Waldeck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which convicted her of harassment by telephone under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 135/1-1(2) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant left a message on the victim's answering machine, which included a few vulgarities. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to allow the trial court to find that she had the requisite intent to harass. The appellate court concluded that a trier of fact could not infer an intent to harass in the required sense solely from the use of some vulgar language in a telephone call that otherwise had a legitimate purpose. For a call to be made with intent to harass, the caller had to have had the intent to produce emotional distress akin to that of a threat. Thus, the appellate court concluded that the evidence did not support the inference that defendant intended her call to harass the victim. Defendant might have intended her language to offend, as her admission that leaving the message was wrong suggested, but intent to offend was not sufficient to sustain her conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

1408 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Garvin


No. 2-03-0162


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 845; 812 N.E.2d 773; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 833; 285 Ill. Dec. 953



June 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Garvin, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 918 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 29, 2004)
Appeal granted by People v. Garvin, 212 Ill. 2d 541, 824 N.E.2d 287, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1792, 291 Ill. Dec. 711 (2004)
Affirmed by People v. Garvin, 219 Ill. 2d 104, 847 N.E.2d 82, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 328, 301 Ill. Dec. 423 (Ill., Mar. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01-CF-3683. Honorable Perry R. Thompson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of burglary in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-1(a) (2000) and theft in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/16-1(a)(1)(A) (2000). He was sentenced to concurrent terms of six and a half years' imprisonment, and was ordered to give a blood sample for genetic marker testing, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2002). Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his pretrial motion to suppress evidence and that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 was unconstitutional. The appellate court concluded that because the police lacked probable cause when they arrested defendant, the trial court should have suppressed any harmful statements made by him subsequent to his arrest. However, the trial court's admission of defendant's statements--his request for his wallet and his admission that he was in the area where a theft of computer equipment occurred--was harmless because there was sufficient and competent evidence presented at the trial that clearly established defendant's guilt. The statements were not material to the guilty finding where other competent evidence overwhelmingly established defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. In addition, the appellate court found that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 was not unconstitutional. The State's interest in deterring and prosecuting recidivist criminal acts strongly outweighed defendant's diminished right to privacy and the minimal intrusion caused by the submission of a blood, saliva, or tissue sample.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Arnold


No. 1-03-2213


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 668; 812 N.E.2d 696; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 816; 285 Ill. Dec. 876



June 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Arnold, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 885 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 20, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Arnold, 217 Ill. 2d 569, 844 N.E.2d 40, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1646, 300 Ill. Dec. 368 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Arnold v. Illinois, 547 U.S. 1075, 126 S. Ct. 1778, 164 L. Ed. 2d 525, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3181 (2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Arnold, 2013 IL App (1st) 112039-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1756 (2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Arnold v. Hutchinson, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 3260 (N.D. Ill., Jan. 10, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 20265. The Honorable Colleen McSweeney Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to 45 years' imprisonment, 25 years for murder with a mandatory 20-year add-on because the court found that defendant personally discharged a firearm during the commission of the murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after an informant identified him. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the warrantless arrest and suppress evidence because the police lacked probable cause for his arrest. Further, he asserted that the statute which mandated the addition of 20 years to his 25-year sentence for murder, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(ii) (2000), was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that probable cause to arrest defendant existed, as the information provided by the informant had an indicia of reliability because it independently corroborated information the police learned through their investigation. Further, the enhanced penalty provision for personally discharging a firearm as applied to first-degree murder did not violate the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution. Finally, the enhanced penalty provision, as applied to first-degree murder, did not violate due process as the increase in penalty was a reasonable means of deterring the targeted conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1410 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Austin


No. 1-03-1984


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 766; 812 N.E.2d 588; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 750; 285 Ill. Dec. 768



June 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Austin, 211 Ill. 2d 585, 823 N.E.2d 968, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1547, 291 Ill. Dec. 382 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Hon. Vincent M. Gaughan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after he was convicted in a bench trial conducted in Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1)(3)(A) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car stopped after a brief pursuit for a traffic violation. Defendant, who was seated in the car, was ordered to raise his hands. A police officer testified that as defendant raised his hands, the officer saw a gun in defendant's right hand. When defendant's hands were at chest level, he dropped the gun to the floor of the car. The loaded gun was recovered after defendant was ordered to exit the car. On appeal, defendant argued that the officer's testimony was incredible and was insufficient to support defendant's conviction. He also argued that the UUW statute violated due process and that the penalty for UUW violated the Illinois proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970). The court affirmed, holding that (1) the officer's testimony supported defendant's conviction and the trial court's finding of credibility would not be reversed; (2) the aggravated UUW statute was rationally related to the goal of protecting public safety; and (3) comparative proportionality review of the UUW statute and Illinois' reckless discharge of a firearm statute was inappropriate because the statutes were enacted for different legislative purposes.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1411 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Beurksen v. Graff


No. 1-03-2385


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


351 Ill. App. 3d 148; 813 N.E.2d 1018; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 745; 286 Ill. Dec. 325



June 24, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 25, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Beursken v. Graff, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1014 (Ill. App. Ct., July 30, 2004)
Appeal denied by Beursken v. Graff, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 37 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 D 18147. Honorable Drella C. Savage, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandmother sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which vacated a previous order providing her with visitation rights pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b) (1998), commonly called the "grandparent visitation statute."


OVERVIEW: The grandmother had been granted overnight and summer vacation visitation with her grandchild. After § 607(b) was found to be unconstitutional, appellee mother sought the order vacating the visitation order. The grandmother argued that even though the statute was unconstitutional, she had a common law right to visitation. The court disagreed. As § 607(b) had been found unconstitutional, the visitation order was void. The grandmother had no common law right to visitation as such a right would be in direct conflict with the fit mother's constitutionally protected right to make decisions regarding the best interest of her child.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

 

1412 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lisa Z. (In re Amanda D.)


No. 2-03-1360


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 941; 811 N.E.2d 1237; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 763; 285 Ill. Dec. 358



June 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 22, 2004.
Appeal granted by In re Amanda D., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1589 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)
Affirmed by People v. Lisa M. (In re D.W.), 2005 Ill. LEXIS 319 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 02--JA--15. Honorable Gordon E. Graham and John D. Bolger, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Finding of unfitness reversed; order of the trial court vacated; cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, McHenry County (Illinois), entered a series of orders that declared respondent mother to be an unfit parent and determined that it was in the best interests of her child that her parental rights be terminated. The unfitness finding was based solely on the Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2002), which allowed for that finding due to her prior conviction for aggravated battery of a child. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother was in an alcohol-induced blackout when she fractured the arm of a daughter. Thereafter, the mother pled guilty to a charge of aggravated battery. She then successfully completed an inpatient substance-abuse program. In the meantime, another daughter was born to the mother. The State soon petitioned for termination of parental rights. The sole allegation regarding unfitness was that the mother previously had been convicted of aggravated battery to a child. The Adoption Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (2002), permitted a finding of unfitness due to such a conviction alone. The trial court held a hearing and, thereafter, terminated the mother's parental rights in the younger daughter. On appeal, the appellate court found that § 50/1(D)(q) was unconstitutional, as it violated the mother's substantive due process rights because it mandated a finding of unfitness based on the conviction alone, without regard to consideration of other relevant factors. The appellate court added that while the State had a compelling interest in the welfare of children, the statute was not narrowly tailored to advance that interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held the statutory section unconstitutional. Accordingly, it reversed the finding of unfitness and vacated the trial court's order terminating the mother's parental rights. It also remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Cummings


No. 1-02-3290


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


351 Ill. App. 3d 343; 813 N.E.2d 1004; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 956; 286 Ill. Dec. 311



June 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 16, 2004. Released for Publication August 25, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Cummings, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1012 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 2, 2004)
Motion granted by People v. Cummings, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1639 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Cummings, 212 Ill. 2d 539, 824 N.E.2d 286, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1909, 291 Ill. Dec. 710 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cummings v. Illinois, 544 U.S. 1051, 125 S. Ct. 2298, 161 L. Ed. 2d 1093, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4234 (2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Cummings, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 677 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 25, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Claim dismissed by United States ex rel. Cummings v. Rednour, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 112671 (N.D. Ill., Oct. 22, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Cummings v. Atchison, 2012 IL App (5th) 120192-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3190 (2012)
Decision reached on appeal by, Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Cummings, 2016 IL App (1st) 141847-U, 2016 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 737 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 26997 (03). Honorable Joseph G. Kazmierski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery and sentenced him to natural life imprisonment as a habitual criminal pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 (2000).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his sentence was unconstitutional because the penalties for armed robbery and armed violence with a weapon were disproportionate, and the sentence was disproportionate to the sentences imposed on his codefendants. He also argued that the trial court failed to conduct an adequate inquiry into his posttrial pro se claims of ineffective assistance. The appellate court found that defendant's natural life sentence was constitutionally proportionate where defendant had no constitutional right to choose the offense with which he would be charged or his penalty--he was charged with the greater offense of armed robbery and not the lesser offense of armed violence. In addition, defendant's penalty was not based solely on the armed robbery offense, but also on his history of committing violent Class X offenses. Where defendant's background supported application of the Habitual Criminal Act and there was nothing to indicate that either codefendant had a similar criminal background, defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally disproportionate. Finally, the trial court adequately inquired into defendant's allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence of natural life imprisonment were affirmed.

Mermelstein v. Rothner


No. 1-03-2891


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 800; 812 N.E.2d 461; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 716; 285 Ill. Dec. 641



June 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.
Appeal denied by Mermelstein v. Rothner, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1540 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 91 CH 5470. Honorable Sophia H. Hall, Judge Presiding.
Mermelstein v. Rothner, 324 Ill. App. 3d 1126, 805 N.E.2d 750, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 4740, 282 Ill. Dec. 131 (Ill. App. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court granted a directed verdict in favor of defendant corporation in a breach of fiduciary duty action, the corporation dismissed its counterclaim against plaintiff. When that judgment was reversed and remanded, plaintiff filed an amended complaint, and the corporation raised its previously dismissed counterclaim. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the counterclaim as time barred. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-207 appeared to preserve a defendant's right to bring an otherwise time-barred counterclaim, while 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217 appeared to limit that right after one year if the counterclaim was voluntarily dismissed. Focusing on the waiver theory of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-207 allowed the court to harmonize the apparent conflict with 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217. If a defendant had previously voluntarily dismissed a claim that would otherwise be barred by the statute of limitation or the one-year period of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217, that claim would (as the result of waiver) nevertheless be "within the remaining period of limitation." Therefore, the court found defendant's counterclaim was not barred by the one-year limitation of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-217 because, as a result of plaintiff's waiver, it was not outside the period of limitation. Moreover, the court found judicial economy was not served by adopting a statutory interpretation forcing defendants to litigate counterclaims, when they would prefer not to, simply to preserve these claims against the possibility of an appeal favorable to the plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and remanded.

 

1415 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hayes Mech., Inc. v. First Indus., L.P.


No. 1-02-1191


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


351 Ill. App. 3d 1; 812 N.E.2d 419; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 693; 285 Ill. Dec. 599



June 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 CH 03036. Honorable Clifford Meacham, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), granted appellee landlord's summary judgment motion on that count of appellant contractor's complaint against the landlord that sought to have the landlord pay a lien amount for renovation work the contractor performed for defendant tenant in the building owned by the landlord. It then denied the contractor's motion for leave to file a proposed amended complaint. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tenant moved into the landlord's building. Thereafter, the tenant and the contractor executed an agreement obligating the contractor to perform office renovation work and obligating the tenant to make biweekly progress payments. The tenant paid for most, but not all, of the total cost of the project. The contractor then filed a claim for lien and a two-count complaint. The second count, directed at the landlord, sought recovery of the lien amount. Eventually, the contractor released its lien against the landlord and sought leave to file an amended pleading alleging quantum meruit and unjust enrichment claims. The landlord responded by stating it had no direct relationship with the contractor and had not been a party to the renovation contract. The trial court denied the motion for leave to amend and granted the landlord's summary judgment motion. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err in denying the motion for leave, as the contractor had not pled any facts showing that the landlord had engaged in conduct that merited quasi-contract relief against the landlord and in the contractor's favor for the tenant's renovation contract debt.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Garrido v. Cook County Sheriff's Merit Bd.


No. 1-03-1128


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 68; 811 N.E.2d 312; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 674; 285 Ill. Dec. 71; 21 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 716



June 9, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied a petition for administrative review of a decision of respondent Cook County Sheriffs Merit Board to discharge petitioner employee after it found that she was in violation of the sheriff's office drug-free workplace policy. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff's office had a drug-free workplace policy, which the parties agreed was a zero-tolerance policy. The employee, a deputy sheriff, was randomly selected to undergo drug testing. After the employee's urine sample tested positive for the presence of cocaine metabolites, the sheriff's office filed a complaint with the Merit Board. At a hearing, the employee testified and presented evidence that she tested positive for the presence of cocaine metabolites due to her innocent consumption of Mate de Coca tea that was purchased in Peru when she and her husband traveled there to adopt a child. After the hearing, the Merit Board discharged the employee, and the circuit court denied her petition for review. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that the application of the drug-free workplace policy by the Merit Board was not rationally related to the specified purpose of the policy and, therefore, violated the employee's substantive due process rights. The court stated that a review of the extensive factual findings led it to conclude that the Merit Board found that the employee tested positive for the presence of cocaine metabolites due to her innocent consumption of the tea.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Merit Board to dismiss the employee for cause and reversed the order of the circuit court affirming the Merit Board's decision. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court with instructions to enter an order reinstating the employee in her position as an employee of the sheriff's office.

 

1417 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mark W. (In re Mark W.)


NO. 5-02-0461


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


348 Ill. App. 3d 1065; 811 N.E.2d 767; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 658; 285 Ill. Dec. 280



June 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 02-MH-39. Honorable Daniel J. Stack, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a pretrial detainee, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which granted petitioner State of Illinois' petition to involuntarily administer psychotropic medication to the detainee.


OVERVIEW: The detainee was arrested on aggravated battery charges and was found unfit to stand trial. The use of psychotropic drugs rendered the detainee fit to stand trial but he discontinued the drugs after being released from a detention health center. As a result, he again became unfit to stand trial, leading to a 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-107.1 (2002) for involuntary treatment. The detainee filed a motion to dismiss, contending that § 2-107.1 was unconstitutional. The motion was denied and the order allowing the State to administer the psychotropic drugs was entered. The court affirmed in part, holding that § 2-107.1 was not unconstitutional and that the State could administer antipsychotic drugs to the detainee to render him competent to stand trial. However, the drugs could only be administered based on a showing that important governmental interests existed that would be furthered by administration of the drugs, that the involuntary medication was necessary to further those state interests, and that the administration of the drugs was medically appropriate. The parties' trial court stipulation allowing the involuntary administration of the drugs fell short of those requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial courts finding that the statute was constitutional as applied to pretrial detainees generally and to the detainee specifically. The court reversed the order granting the State's request to involuntarily administer the psychotropic medication.

People v. Dryden


No. 2-02-0999


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 115; 811 N.E.2d 302; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 687; 285 Ill. Dec. 61



June 8, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 8, 2004.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Dryden, 838 N.E.2d 1, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1644, 297 Ill. Dec. 514 (Ill., 2005)
On reconsideration by People v. Dryden, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 127 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Feb. 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 01--CF--2710. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which, following a jury trial, convicted defendant on two counts of home invasion and one count of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon. Defendant was acquitted on two counts of armed robbery. Defendant's 21-year sentence included a 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-11(c) (2000) 15-year sentence enhancement for possession of a firearm during a home invasion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was admitted into a dwelling where he threatened the occupants with a gun. Shortly after entering the dwelling, defendant opened the door and allowed two accomplices into the home. On appeal, defendant contended that he was not proven guilty of home invasion, that the § 12-11(c) sentence enhancement violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970), and that his conviction on two counts of home invasion violated the one-act, one-crime rule. The court agreed in part. While home invasion usually required entry of a dwelling "without authority," the evidence showed that defendant intended to rob the occupants of the dwelling when he was allowed to enter and thus, the limited-authority doctrine supported his home invasion convictions. Home invasion and aggravated battery with a firearm were similar crimes, with home invasion being the less serious crime. As such, the sentence enhancement for home invasion was a harsher penalty than the penalty for aggravated battery with a firearm and it violated the proportionate penalties clause. Finally, although there were multiple victims, defendant committed only one act of home invasion and his multiple convictions were improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed one of defendant's convictions for home invasion, but the second conviction was vacated. The court also vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case so that a new sentencing hearing could be held.

People v. Haycraft


NO. 5-02-0636


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 416; 811 N.E.2d 747; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 653; 285 Ill. Dec. 260



June 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Haycraft, 823 N.E.2d 972, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1543 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County. No. 01-CF-160. Honorable John P. Coady, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to suppress evidence was denied. Defendant stipulated to a bench trial, and was convicted of criminal drug conspiracy and unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms of 19 years for each conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the search of his home was unconstitutional because his parole agreement did not give the parole agent the authority to search his home without a warrant. The appellate court disagreed, noting that defendant signed a parole agreement permitting the agent to visit his home and that the need to remove persons from the home and to locate, dismantle, and take possession of the dangerous instrumentalities used in cooking the methamphetamine was an exigent circumstance that justified the warrantless search. Next, contrary to defendant's argument, the trial court's admonishments pursuant to the guilty plea procedure did not transform defendant's stipulated bench trial into a guilty plea. As for defendant's sufficiency claim, the appellate court concluded that the liquid mixture, containing the ingredients necessary to manufacture methamphetamine, constituted a substance containing methamphetamine despite the fact that it was not yet in marketable form. Finally, the appellate court vacated defendant's conspiracy conviction and sentence based on 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-5 (2002), prohibiting the conviction of both the inchoate offense and the principal offense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for criminal drug conspiracy were vacated. The case was remanded to the circuit court with directions to credit $ 1,875 against the defendant's drug assessment. In all other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Williams


No. 3-02-0456


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 273; 811 N.E.2d 1197; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 596; 285 Ill. Dec. 318



May 26, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 21, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Williams, 211 Ill. 2d 612, 823 N.E.2d 977, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1412, 291 Ill. Dec. 391 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit Peoria County, Illinois. No. 01-CF-1106. Honorable Thomas G. Ebel, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Williams, 347 Ill. App. 3d 1123, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 3820 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 10th Judicial Circuit Court, Peoria County (Illinois), of prostitution. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-14(a), criminalizing prostitution, prohibited conduct constitutionally protected under U.S. Const., amend XIV. The appellate court held the statute did not affect a fundamental right or suspect classification, so it was reviewed under the rational basis test. Under that test, it was a valid attempt to promote the legitimate purpose of protecting the safety, health, and welfare of the people by preventing venereal disease, cutting down prostitution-related crimes of violence and theft, and protecting the integrity and stability of family life. As the statute validly attempted to protect the public welfare, it did not violate defendant's constitutional rights. Acts of prostitution were excluded from the protection afforded private sexual activity between two consenting adults. The statute was carefully crafted to distinguish between the business of selling sex and private, noncommercial, acts.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Perlstein v. Wolk


No. 2-03-0003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


349 Ill. App. 3d 161; 810 N.E.2d 598; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 580; 284 Ill. Dec. 808



May 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 24, 2004. Counsel Amended September 20, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Perlstein v. Wolk, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 757 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., June 24, 2004)
Appeal granted by Perlstein v. Wolk, 211 Ill. 2d 614, 823 N.E.2d 978, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1600 (2004)
Affirmed by Perlstein v. Wolk, 218 Ill. 2d 448, 844 N.E.2d 923, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 315, 300 Ill. Dec. 480 (Ill., Feb. 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 02--L--297. Honorable Stephen E. Walter, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a widow and her son, filed an action against defendants, a law firm and an attorney who worked for the law firm, alleging malpractice. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) granted the attorney and law firm's motion, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619(a)(5) (2002), to dismiss the complaint, and denied the widow and son's motion for reconsideration. The widow and son appealed.


OVERVIEW: A widow and her son by a previous marriage sued an attorney and a law firm in January 1998, alleging that they were prevented from receiving money which the widow's deceased husband intended to transfer under a trust, will, and codicil he executed because the attorney improperly drafted the husband's will. The attorney and law firm filed a motion to dismiss the action, arguing that it was time-barred under § 13-214.3(d) of the Illinois Limitations Act, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3(d) (1994). The trial court agreed, and it dismissed the case. The appellate court (1) noted that § 13-214.3(d) was repealed by 1995 Ill. Laws 89-7 (Public Act 89-7), but was reinstated in December 1997 when the Supreme Court of Illinois declared that Public Act 89-7 was unconstitutional; (2) noted that the widow and son's action would not have been time-barred if Public Act 89-7 had not been declared unconstitutional; and (3) held that the widow and son had a reasonable period of time after the supreme court declared Public Act 89-7 to be unconstitutional to file their lawsuit, that they filed their lawsuit within a reasonable period of time, and that their lawsuit was not time-barred.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Davis


No. 1-03-0822


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


349 Ill. App. 3d 93; 810 N.E.2d 582; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 590; 284 Ill. Dec. 792



May 21, 2004 


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 25, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Davis, 212 Ill. 2d 590, 815 N.E.2d 407, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1464, 287 Ill. Dec. 4 (Ill., 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Davis, 211 Ill. 2d 590, 817 N.E.2d 534, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 2044, 288 Ill. Dec. 176 (Ill., 2004)
Vacated by People v. Davis, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1445 (Ill. App. Ct., Nov. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Hon. Frank Zelezinski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon and one count of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: The police officer responded to a report of two people sleeping in a car with the motor running. The officer observed defendant in the passenger seat, woke up the driver, and then opened the door of the car. In the armrest of the opened door, the officer observed cocaine. The officer woke up defendant, who was holding an unloaded .25-caliber revolver. Defendant was arrested. Later defendant, in a statement, admitted to owning the gun and drugs. Defense counsel was ineffective for failing to file a motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. By pursuing a motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence, defense counsel could have made a strong case that the circumstances surrounding defendant's arrest failed to demonstrate probable cause. The officer's seizure of defendant arguably amounted to an unconstitutional seizure. The officer woke up the driver prior to opening the door. The record reflected no further need to gain the driver's attention or to open the door. Defendant was prejudiced by counsel's failure to file the motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. Had the motion succeeded, the evidence needed for the prosecution would have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

People v. Deganutti


No. 1-02-2855


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


348 Ill. App. 3d 512; 810 N.E.2d 191; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 518; 284 Ill. Dec. 538; 5 A.L.R.6th 599



May 12, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook Coungy. Nos. 00 CR 23697 & 00 CR 23698. Honorable Thomas R. Sumner Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant on charges of unlawful observation of voting under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/29-9 (2000) and on charges of absentee ballot violations under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/29-20(4) (2000) in connection with the completion and mailing of the absentee ballots of two voters.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to the voters' homes and obtained their signatures on absentee ballot request forms. Once the ballots were mailed to the voters, defendant returned to the homes. With voter one, defendant sat on the couch with the voter and instructed which numbers to punch on the ballot. With voter two, defendant provided a list a numbers and stood nearby as voter two completed the ballots. Defendant then looked at the ballot and had voter two re-punch a number that had not punched cleanly. Defendant then put the ballots in the mail for the voters. On appeal, she argued insufficient evidence to sustain her convictions. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the circumstantial evidence surrounding defendant's presence as the voters completed their ballots supported the unlawful observation convictions; (2) the fact that defendant knowingly took the voters ballots and mailed them, a violation of 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-6 (2000) supported her conviction under 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/29-20(4) (2000), and (3) the fact that the statutes defendant was convicted under required only a knowing mental state rather than criminal intent did not violate substantive due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the trial court erred in several respects when it found her unfit as a parent. The court disagreed and affirmed. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/1-3(4.05) (2002).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), denied the State's motion to transfer defendant juvenile's first-degree murder case to an adult court for prosecution. The appellate court affirmed. Thereafter, the trial court granted the State's motion to have his case be designated as an extended jurisdiction juvenile proceeding and entered a final disposition after he was adjudicated by a jury to be delinquent. He was then sentenced. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A car full of people, including defendant, passed near three people. Defendant then got out, ran up to them, and fatally shot one. Witnesses identified defendant as the shooter. He was arrested. His mother went with him to the police station. Defendant was read his Miranda rights. He asked "Do I need a lawyer?" but nevertheless gave statements admitting he shot the victim. The trial court denied his motions to quash and suppress. It also denied the State's motion to transfer the case to adult court, which was affirmed on appeal. It granted the State's motion to designate the case as an extended jurisdiction juvenile (EJJ) matter. Defendant was adjudicated delinquent. He was given a juvenile sentence and a conditional adult sentence. On appeal, the appellate court found that the delinquency finding was proper because probable cause existed to arrest him, his confessions were voluntarily given, and he did not invoke the right to counsel. However, it also found that only the juvenile portion of his sentence was proper because the State was required to simultaneously file its motion to transfer and motion to designate the case as an EJJ matter and did not do so.


OUTCOME: The disposition was affirmed, and the sentence was modified by deleting the adult portion of defendant's sentence and retaining the juvenile portion of his sentence, which meant his sentence of incarceration would continue until his 21st birthday.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a street gang member. He held the rank of "chief enforcer." He saw the victim and mistakenly believed that the victim was a rival gang member. Defendant, accompanied by two fellow gang members, fired several shots at the victim. One bullet struck the victim and killed him. Coyne v. Milan Police Pension Bd.


No. 3-03-0066


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


347 Ill. App. 3d 713; 807 N.E.2d 1276; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 396; 283 Ill. Dec. 435


September 29, 2003, Assigned; November 13, 2003, Submitted  
April 13, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2004.
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Coyne v. Milan Police Pension Bd., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 92 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 99--MR--53. Honorable Lori R. Lefstein, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 14th Judicial Circuit Court, Rock Island County (Illinois), entered a judgment that affirmed appellee city police pension board's decision that denied appellant former police officer's requests that he be allowed to receive a line-of-duty disability pension or a non-duty disability pension. The former police officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former police officer, while working as a police officer, submitted to a psychological examination to determine his fitness for a promotion. He received it after a doctor determined that he was of sound mind and suffered no impediments that would hinder his performance. However, as time passed, things began to change. The former police officer's job performance allegedly declined after he was reprimanded by the police chief. Also, he appeared to become traumatized by several incidents at work, including injuries he sustained, the stress of trying to save a trapped motorist, and his knowledge of several suicides. He started seeing two treating physicians and took their advice to leave police work to do something else. He applied for a line-of-duty disability pension or a non-duty disability pension. The city police pension board denied both requests and the trial court affirmed. On appeal, the appellate court found a city police pension board member with an apparent conflict-of-interest was properly allowed to remain on the board to decided his case, but further proceedings were required because specified error occurred in weighing the evidence.


OUTCOME: The decision permitting the city police pension board's member to remain on the board to decide whether the former police officer was entitled to a disability pension despite an alleged conflict-of-interest was affirmed; however, the board's finding that the former police officer failed to prove he had a disability preventing him from performing police work was reversed, and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1428 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Rajcan v. Donald Garvey & Assocs.


No. 2-03-0270


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


347 Ill. App. 3d 403; 807 N.E.2d 725; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 366; 283 Ill. Dec. 120



April 5, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 7, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01-L-760. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, three trustees and two beneficiaries of a trust, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiffs' second amended complaint against defendants, an attorney and law firm one and an attorney and law firm two, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619(a)(5) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs asserted that as a result of legal malpractice, the beneficiaries of the trust, who were disabled, lost certain public assistance benefits when the trust went into operation. Proper drafting of the trust could have avoided the loss. The trial court dismissed based on a finding that the action was barred by the six-year statute of repose in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214.3 (2002). Plaintiffs asserted that the statute was tolled because attorney one fraudulently concealed plaintiffs' cause of action. The trial court disagreed, finding that none of the claims against that attorney were for fraudulent concealment. The court reversed. The issue was whether the allegations in the complaint established a fraudulent concealment sufficient to overcome the statute of repose. Allegations that the attorney falsely assured the maker of the trust that he would provide the maker with a copy, and then did not, were sufficient to overcome the statute. Plaintiffs also asserted that their action was in fact timely under § 13-214.3(d). The burden was on defendants to show that the time in § 13-214.3(d) had expired. Defendants failed to do so, making dismissal under that section error.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1429 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


DHR Int'l, Inc. v. Winston & Strawn


No. 1-03-0855


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 642; 807 N.E.2d 1094; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 322; 283 Ill. Dec. 253



March 31, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From The Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CH-3137. Honorable Bernetta D. Bush, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Case dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a corporation and its chief executive officer (CEO), appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied their motion for a preliminary injunction to prevent defendant law firm from representing its opponent in an arbitration, claiming the attorney in question had once represented the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had found that the corporation and CEO had failed to make any showing that the attorney or the firm had represented them in any way that would have affected the pending arbitration regarding an asset sale. The arbitration went forward, but the corporation and CEO appealed denial of the injunction. The appellate court held that while Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307 authorized interlocutory appeals from rulings on requests for injunctive relief in certain situations, case law applying that rule held it inapplicable to orders relating to disqualification of counsel. While an appeal might have been allowed under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 306, the corporation and CEO had failed to raise appropriate grounds for such a permissive appeal. Finally, appellate jurisdiction was absent because of mootness. The arbitration had gone forward and the challenged attorney had represented the opponent.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction.

Crusius v. Ill. Gaming Bd.


No. 1-02-2819


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


348 Ill. App. 3d 44; 807 N.E.2d 1207; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 333; 283 Ill. Dec. 366



March 31, 2004, Decided  
March 31, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2004.
Appeal granted by Crusius v. Ill. Gaming Bd., 211 Ill. 2d 573, 823 N.E.2d 964, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1173 (2004)
Affirmed by Crusius v. Ill. Gaming Bd., 2005 Ill. LEXIS 962 (Ill., Sept. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 02 CH 07412. Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), dismissed plaintiff taxpayer's action seeking a declaratory judgment that a statute allowing a licensee who was not conducting riverboat gambling before a specified date to apply to defendant state gaming board for license renewal and approval of relocation to a new home dock location. The taxpayer had contended the statute was unconstitutional special legislation. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state gaming board issued a riverboat gambling license to the licensee's corporate predecessor. Although it operated a riverboat in its designated location there for several years, it ceased operations when it found the location was not economically viable. The state legislature then revised its riverboat gambling law, under which it had granted 10 riverboat gambling licenses, to allow the licensee to apply to the state gaming board for a license renewal and approval of relocation to a new location. The licensee applied pursuant to that law. The taxpayer then filed suit and claimed that the revised law was unconstitutional because it was special legislation passed to benefit only the licensee. The trial court dismissed the taxpayer's lawsuit. On appeal, the appellate court first found that the taxpayer had standing. It then found that the revision did not amount to special legislation, even though only one party benefitted from it, because it was rationally related to the State's interest under the riverboat gambling law of producing revenue for the State and promoting its tourism by allowing the licensee to relocate its riverboat casino to a more economically viable area.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Zapata


No. 1-02-3733


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

Rehearing denied by People v. Zapata, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 623 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 12, 2004)
Related proceeding at People v. Negron, 347 Ill. App. 3d 1109, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 3995 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Zapata, 217 Ill. 2d 592, 844 N.E.2d 47, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1639, 300 Ill. Dec. 375 (2005)
Petition denied by People v. Zapada, 979 N.E.2d 888, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1215, 366 Ill. Dec. 87 (Ill., 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied United States ex rel. Zapada v. Lemke, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56858 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 23, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 16022(02). Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of first-degree murder for shooting a man to death. It then imposed a 50-year prison sentence on defendant, which consisted of a base sentence of 30 years plus a 20-year sentence permitted under a statute that allowed for adding a term where a defendant personally discharged a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim stopped his car in an alley next to his apartment building. Defendant came walking along. He banged on the victim's car. A van containing some of defendant's acquaintances entered the alley. Defendant then punched out a window of the victim's car. The victim struck defendant with the car door, and they struggled. Defendant then pulled out a gun and shot the victim at least twice. Defendant fled, but a detective eventually found him. Defendant allegedly told the detective that he had spent the night at his girlfriend's house. At trial, defendant denied telling the detective that he had been at his girlfriend's house. The trial court found defendant guilty of first-degree murder. It then imposed upon him a base sentence of 30 years and an extended sentence of 20 years for using a firearm to commit the crime. On appeal, the appellate court found that the State disproved defendant's self-defense claim and that the sentencing statute was neither unconstitutional nor violated his due process rights. However, it found the trial court's assumption that the shooting was gang-related required resentencing since the evidence did not support that conclusion.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction was affirmed, but his sentence was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing and correction of the mittimus.

People v. Barron


No. 1-03-0384


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


348 Ill. App. 3d 109; 808 N.E.2d 1051; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 312; 283 Ill. Dec. 763



March 30, 2004, Decided  
March 30, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of two counts of felony disorderly conduct, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/26-1(a)(3), for declaring to ticketing agents at an airport that he had a bomb in his shoe. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: During check-in for a flight, defendant told a ticket agent that he had a bomb in his shoe. The ticket agent detected alcohol on defendant's breath, and told defendant not to make such statements. After defendant made further statements and laughed at the agents, another agent called the police. The police searched defendant and found no explosives. On appeal, defendant contended that the State failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/26-1(a)(3) distinguished between comments which actually alarmed an individual and those which were understood as joking remarks. The appellate court held that an individual could be found guilty of felony disorderly conduct upon transmission of a false alarm, regardless of the intention of the speaker or the effect the words had upon the person receiving them. The appellate court therefore found that the evidence, when viewed in a light most favorable to the State, supported defendant's conviction. The appellate court also denied defendant's claim that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/26-1 was constitutionally overbroad and violated defendant's right to free speech under the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Smith


No. 3-03-0492


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


347 Ill. App. 3d 446; 806 N.E.2d 1262; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 339; 282 Ill. Dec. 674


December 8, 2003, Assigned; January 21, 2004, Submitted  
March 30, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 30, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Smith, 209 Ill. 2d 597, 813 N.E.2d 227, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 934, 286 Ill. Dec. 170 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 01-CF-1167. Honorable Jerelyn Maher, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty following a stipulated bench trial in the Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, on a charge of indecent solicitation of a child, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6(a). Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was over 17 years of age, solicited sex from a 15-year old boy he met in a chat room. In reality, the "boy" was a police detective. Defendant was arrested when he traveled to a prearranged location to engage in oral sex with the boy. Section 11-6(a) made it unlawful for someone over the age of 17 to solicit a child, or someone believed to be a child, for the purpose of engaging in sexual conduct. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute based on overbreadth and vagueness, although he did not complain that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court affirmed, holding that (1) any arguably impermissible applications of the § 11-6(a) were dwarfed by the statute's legitimate reach, so the statute was not overbroad and did not impinge on First Amendment rights; (2) defendant could not challenge the statute for vagueness because his actions fell squarely with the statutory proscription of § 11-6(a); and (3) as the statute did not impinge on First Amendment rights, defendant lacked standing to challenge its constitutionality because he was not directly affected by the unconstitutional aspects of the statute he asserted.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction on the solicitation charge was affirmed.

People v. Wolst

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 96 CR 15947. Hon. Gary L. Brownfield, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted his petition for an unsupervised on-grounds pass privilege but denied his request to be transferred to a nonsecure setting and his request for supervised off-grounds pass privileges under § 5-2-4(e) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-2-4(e) (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who suffered from paranoid schizophrenia, shot and killed a stranger while under a delusional belief. After being found not guilty by reason of insanity, he was confined to a mental health center. Affirming denial of defendant's requests, court held, (1) defendant failed to meet his burden of showing that the privileges should have been granted, and, thus, trial court's determination was not against the manifest weight of evidence; (2) amendment to § 5-2-4(g), which shifted the-burden of proof to defendant, had no retroactive effect where it did not attach new legal consequences to defendant's murder conviction, was triggered by the facility director's recommendations, and was amended more than a year before those recommendation were made, and did not violate § 4 of the Statute on Statutes, 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 70/4 (2000) because it was procedural in nature; (3) the amendment to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/ 5-2-4(g) did not violate the ex post facto clause of U.S. Constitution because it was civil in nature; and (4) the amendment to § 5-2-4(g) also did not violate defendant's rights to substantive or procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Palmer


No. 2-02-0592


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


346 Ill. App. 3d 942; 806 N.E.2d 734; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 304; 282 Ill. Dec. 437



March 26, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 22, 2004.
Appeal granted by People v. Palmer, 211 Ill. 2d 603, 823 N.E.2d 974, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1158 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by People v. Palmer, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 8 (Ill., Jan. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 99--CF--1800. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) on one count of attempted first degree murder, two counts of home invasion, one count of armed robbery, and four counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault. He was adjudged a habitual criminal and was sentenced to seven consecutive life sentences, one for each conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the home of a husband and wife under the ruse of selling newspapers. He sexually assaulted the wife through both oral and vaginal sex, and he attempted to kill the husband. One count of home invasion was charged relating to the husband and one was charged relating to the wife. The multiple life sentences were based on an interpretation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1(c) (2002). The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part, holding that (1) for purposes of § 33B-1(c), defendant could only be sentenced to one life sentence where his multiple convictions arose out of the same transaction; (2) as defendant was sentenced once under the habitual offender statute, the consecutive sentencing guidelines under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(a) (2002) did not apply; (3) the life sentences were vacated and reduced to one life sentence pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b); (4) as defendant only "invaded" one home, only one home invasion conviction could stand; and (5) defendant's two convictions for the same act of penile penetration violated the one-act, one-crime rule and one of the convictions was vacated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment imposing seven consecutive life sentences and sentenced defendant to one term of life imprisonment. The court vacated one of the home invasion convictions, and two of the sentences and convictions on two of the aggravated criminal sexual assault charges. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Robinson v. Johnson


1-02-2121


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


346 Ill. App. 3d 895; 809 N.E.2d 123; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 281; 284 Ill. Dec. 1



March 25, 2004, Decided  
March 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by Robinson v. Johnson, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1136 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Honorable Philip L. Bronstein, Judge Presiding.
Robinson v. Johnson, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1191 (Ill. App. Ct., Sept. 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action, defendant doctors appealed, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 183, granted two motions filed by plaintiff, administrator of her decedent husband's estate, to extend the six-month statutory period of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402 (1998) for converting the doctors from respondents in discovery to defendants.


OVERVIEW: The administrator filed a wrongful death action against defendant hospital and named the doctors as respondents in discovery. Reversing, the court held that the trial court could not extend the six-month period under § 2-402 because an action filed pursuant to the provisions of § 2-402 was a special statutory action that provided for broad discovery unknown to the common law and made the six-month time requirement an inherent element of the right. Moreover, Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 183's plain language indicated that it only applied to the time limits set forth by the Illinois supreme court rules, and it simply did not apply to a statutory time limit like 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402; thus, the trial court erred in granting the two extensions. However, after granting the administrator's petition for rehearing and allowing a lawyers association to file an amicus curiae petition in support of the rehearing, the court held that its decision should only apply to the present case and prospectively because it was an issue of first impression whose resolution was not clearly foreshadowed and the purpose of the court's decision would be promoted by prospective application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the extension orders and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.
