People v. Braddock


No. 1-03-0404


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


348 Ill. App. 3d 115; 809 N.E.2d 712; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 275; 284 Ill. Dec. 146



March 24, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 7, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable William P. O'Malley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant police officer of solicitation of a sex act in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-14.1(a) (2002) and sentenced him to six months' supervision. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial and motion in arrest of judgment. Defendant appealed the denial of his posttrial motions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his conviction should be reversed because 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-14.1(a) was overbroad, vague, and unconstitutional. The appellate court concluded that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-14.1(a) was neither overbroad nor vague as applied and was not unconstitutional. When defendant offered the undercover police officer $ 50 in exchange for sex, he was not engaged in a protected activity because he exercised his right to free speech in the commission of a criminal offense. Also, the statute was not vague as applied to defendant's conduct because it provided adequate and clearly understandable notice that the offer of money in exchange for sex was proscribed. In addition, defendant's offer for sex was proven beyond a reasonable doubt where the undercover officer testified that defendant asked her for "sex," requested her price for sex, agreed thereto, showed her the money, and moved his car to the location she suggested. Finally, a fatal variance did not exist between the charge that defendant solicited sexual intercourse, an act of sexual penetration, and the proof at trial where the commonly understood meaning of "sex" was sexual intercourse.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Torres


No. 1-02-2579


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 252; 807 N.E.2d 654; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 265; 283 Ill. Dec. 49

Appeal denied by People v. Torres, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1133 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ill. v. Torres, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2265 (U.S., Mar. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CR 5209. Honorable Catherine Haberkorn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the trial court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence and entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer and his partner were on a routine patrol. They saw a parked truck. One officer saw two people inside engaged in what appeared to be a domestic altercation. The two police officers approached the parked truck; one officer approached the driver's side while the other approached the passenger's side of the truck. The one officer asked the driver, the woman, if she was in any danger; she said she was not. The other officer then removed the passenger, defendant, from the vehicle, patted him down, and ran a warrant check on him. The pat down revealed he was carrying a gun and a gun clip, while the warrant check indicated that he had an outstanding DUI warrant. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence that was found. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant was then found guilty of two counts of aggravated unlawful use of weapon. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in denying the suppression motion, as once the police ascertained the woman was not in any danger, the officer's actions in removing defendant from the vehicle, patting him down, and checking for warrants were unreasonable and violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

People v. Walls


NO. 5-01-0771


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


346 Ill. App. 3d 1154; 806 N.E.2d 712; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 270; 282 Ill. Dec. 415



March 19, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Walls, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1134 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 00-CF-404. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Jefferson County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of aggravated criminal sexual assault. The trial court then found that, pursuant to statutory law, it was required to sentence defendant to a term of natural-life imprisonment because the conviction was defendant's second conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault and it imposed that sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the complaining witness went to defendant's trailer. While there, defendant hit her in the head with a hammer. Defendant then placed her on the bed, tied her hands and feet, raped her, and then drove her home. Prior to trial, the State filed a motion in limine to prevent defendant from introducing evidence that she had, on a prior occasion, falsely accused a person of an offense. The trial court granted the motion. At the trial, a special assistant State's Attorney helped the prosecuting attorney. The trial court overruled defendant's objection to the assistance. Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault. Pursuant to a statute, he received a mandatory term of natural life imprisonment because it was his second conviction for that offense. On appeal, the appellate court found that defendant was not entitled to impeach the witness with a collateral example of untruthfulness, defendant's argument that the special assistant was not authorized to appear was waived since he objected on another ground, and the statute requiring a mandatory natural life term did not create a disproportionate penalty and, thus, did not violate the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

New Heights Recovery & Power, LLC v. Bower


Docket Nos. 1-02-3557, 1-02-3688 and 1-02-3894, Consolidated Number


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 89; 806 N.E.2d 1156; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 219; 282 Ill. Dec. 568



March 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 4, 2004.
Appeal denied by New Heights Recovery & Power, LLC v. Bower, 209 Ill. 2d 583, 813 N.E.2d 223, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 956, 286 Ill. Dec. 166 (2004)
Appeal denied by New Heights Recovery & Power, LLC v. Bower, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1076 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 00 CH 3157, 96 CH 2560, 00 CH 3754. Honorable Robert Boharic, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; stay vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an electrical utility, commissioners of the Illinois Commerce Commission, and others, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ruled that plaintiff qualified solid waste energy facilities (QSWEF) continued to be eligible for certain benefits under the Retail Rate Law, 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-403.1 (1996). The QSWEF cross-appealed the dismissal of certain their claims.


OVERVIEW: Under the original enactment of the Retail Rate Law, the QWSEFs received special reimbursement rates for electricity they sold to the utility. A 1996 amendment to the Law disqualified them from receiving the rate. The QWSEFs asserted they had a constitutionally protected interest in the rates. The trial court agreed and granted summary judgment on some of the QWSEFs' claims. The trial court dismissed their claims alleging breach of contract by the State and challenging the constitutionality of the amendment. The court affirmed in part, holding that (1) the reach of the amendment was prospective only; (2) because the QWSEFs had no vested right in the continuation of the Law as originally enacted, the prospective application of the amendment of the Law was not constitutionally prohibited, and the amendment served to abolish the subsidies formerly available to the QWSEFs; (3) the Law did not create a contract between the QWSEFs and the State so the QWSEFs' claims of breach of contract failed; (4) the amendment did not violate the special legislation clause in Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970); and (5) the amendment did not violate the "single-subject" rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment. The court dismissed with prejudice the breach of contract claims filed against the utility. The court affirmed the dismissal of the breach of contract claims against the state defendants as well as those claims challenging the constitutionality of the 1996 amendment to the Retail Rate Law.

 

1442 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pizano


No. 1-01-4277


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 128; 806 N.E.2d 1100; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 202; 282 Ill. Dec. 512



March 4, 2004, Decided  
March 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 4, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Pizano, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 879 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 1178. Honorable Marcus R. Salone, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated, remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted on a charge of knowingly possessing a fraudulent resident alien identification card, a violation of 15 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 335/14(B) (1998). He appealed both his conviction and his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant obtained the fraudulent identification card after his wallet was stolen. He testified that he bought the fraudulent card so that he could get into clubs. He eventually obtained a replacement card for his properly issued resident alien card. Defendant asserted that he "forgot" the fraudulent card was in his wallet, but upon questioning by the trial court, admitted that he used the fraudulent card several times a month to enter nightclubs. The court vacated defendant's sentence, holding that (1) a common purpose ran through § 14B(b)(1)-(6); (2) the penalty for knowing possession of a fraudulent identification card under § 14B(b)(1) was harsher than the penalty imposed for § 14B(b)(2)-(6), which violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11; (3) there was no common purpose in the statutes governing the fraudulent possession of a resident alien identification card and possession of a false driver's license; (4) 15 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 335/14B (1998) had a legitimate goal of eradicating fraud, which was within the State's police power and did not violate substantive due process; and (5) defendant received effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed but his sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for sentencing in accordance with the court's opinion.

People v. Lyles


No. 1-01-3478


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 100; 807 N.E.2d 499; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 198; 282 Ill. Dec. 875



March 3, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Lyles, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 445 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 31, 2004)
Appeal granted by People v. Lyles, 211 Ill. 2d 600, 823 N.E.2d 973, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1177, 291 Ill. Dec. 387 (2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Lyles, 217 Ill. 2d 210, 840 N.E.2d 1187, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1627, 298 Ill. Dec. 752 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 78 CR 1191. The Honorable John A. Wasilewski, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lyles, 106 Ill. 2d 373, 478 N.E.2d 291, 1985 Ill. LEXIS 222, 87 Ill. Dec. 934 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Order entered 6/4/2003 vacated; appeal dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellant inmate's appeal from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissing his second pro se petition for relief under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq., the State asserted that the reviewing court erred in vacating its earlier dismissal of the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of, in part, first degree murder. The inmate's appeal from the denial of his second post-conviction petition was dismissed for want of prosecution on April 18, 2003. Under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 367(a), the inmate had 21 days, or until May 9, 2003, to file a motion to vacate the dismissal order and reinstate the appeal. The inmate's counsel did not file the motion until May 27, 2003. The State asserted that the reviewing court lacked jurisdiction to grant the inmate's motion to vacate after the 21-day limitations period had passed. The reviewing court agreed. Although a defendant's right to direct appeal could not be lost through appellate counsel's failure to comply with procedural court rules, the inmate's due process right to counsel did not extend to a post-conviction appeal. The inmate's right to counsel was derived from Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c). Because the inmate's due process rights were not implicated in the post-conviction appeal, the reviewing court properly dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction when appellate counsel failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 367(a).


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

People v. Perea


No. 1-02-0662 and 02-0871 (Cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


347 Ill. App. 3d 26; 807 N.E.2d 26; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 193; 282 Ill. Dec. 730



March 2, 2004, Decided  
March 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 15473. The Honorable Clayton J. Crane, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were minors, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which transferred them from the juvenile to the criminal court system pursuant to the Presumptive Transfer Statute, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-805(2)(a) (1999), based on a charge of attempted murder, convicted defendants of armed robbery and aggravated battery, denied defendants' posttrial motions, and sentenced them under the Criminal Code.


OVERVIEW: The victim was attacked by defendants and a co-defendant while walking home. Although defendants were transferred based on an attempted murder charge, they were convicted of armed robbery under 702 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/18-2(a) (1998), which was also a Class X felony qualifying defendants for transfer. The trial court denied defendants' post trial motions for a new trial or transfer back to the juvenile system, and it sentenced them as adults. Affirming, the court held, inter alia, that (1) the Presumptive Transfer Statute was unambiguous and mandated that defendants be sentenced as adults; (2) the armed robbery charge could have been used to transfer defendants; (3) defendants' rights to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. 1, § 2 were not violated because defendants were not similarly situated to those transferred under the extended juvenile jurisdiction statute, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-810(1)(b), and the Automatic Transfer Provision, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-130(2) (1999); and (4) the Presumptive Transfer Statute was not subject to an Apprendi analysis because it did not constitute any kind of punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent delinquent taxpayers appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the application for a tax deed filed by petitioner, the holder of a tax certificate, and denied the taxpayers' posttrial motions.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers' delinquent real estate taxes on a single-family home were sold at a public tax sale. Petitioner was the assignee of the tax certificate memorializing the sale of the delinquent taxes. The taxpayers failed to redeem the property and petitioner sought his tax deed. Ann. 200/22-45 (2000) did not violate the separation of powers clause of the Illinois Constitution; and (4) the taxpayers' appeal, filed more than 30 days after the tax deed order was entered, was untimely.


OUTCOME: The taxpayers' appeal was dismissed.

People v. Phillips

People v. Daniels


1-97-4354


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

February 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 25, 2004.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph J. Urso, Judge Presiding.
People v. Daniels, 204 Ill. 2d 667, 789 N.E.2d 766, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 793, 273 Ill. Dec. 594 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated, and remand for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted her on a jury's verdict of a charge of first degree murder and sentenced her to 80 years' imprisonment. The conviction came after defendant's second trial on the charge, her first conviction having been reversed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Prior to her first trial, defendant had filed a motion to suppress the statements she made to police. The motion was denied, and the denial was affirmed in defendant's first appeal. After her conviction was vacated, defendant renewed her motion to suppress. The trial court refused to hold an evidentiary hearing on the motion. In her second appeal, defendant contested that refusal and asserted error in the quashing of certain subpoenas, the refusal to allow the jury to review defendant's medical records, and the imposition of an enhanced sentence. The court affirmed in part and vacated in part, holding that (1) the first trial court's decision on the motion to suppress constituted the law of the case and the second trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to revisit the motion; (3) the subpoenas, which sought information about police misconduct in the precinct in which defendant was arrested, were properly quashed where defendant was not asserting that she was physically mistreated; (4) the medical records were not admissible because the defense failed to lay a proper foundation for them, but (5) defendant's enhanced sentence violated Apprendi.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. Defendant's sentence was vacated and her case was remanded for resentencing.

People v. J.W. (In re J.W.)


No. 1-01-2703

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by J. W. v. Illinois, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2124 (U.S., Feb. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 JD 5031. Honorable Edward N. Pietrucha, Judge Presiding.
In re J.W., 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 243 (Ill. App. Ct., Jan. 27, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a juvenile, appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, in a prosecution under the "extended jurisdiction juvenile prosecutions" provision of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987 (EJJ statute), 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-810 (2000), convicted her of first degree murder under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a) (2000) for stabbing her mother and sentenced her as a juvenile and an adult but stayed the adult sentence.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, who was 13 at the time, initially denied hurting her mother, but later confessed to both the police and a youth officer. Affirming but modifying, the court held that (1) the inculpatory statements that she made to the youth officer were properly admitted because, although her prior statements to the police were suppressed, the State met its burden of showing attenuation by clear and convincing evidence; (2) the EJJ statute was not unconstitutional under Apprendi; (3) respondent did not have standing to contest revocation of the stay of the adult sentence on vagueness grounds; (4) the proceeding was properly designated as an EJJ prosecution because there was no evidence that the trial court failed to consider her age or her lack of previous delinquency; (5) the voir dire proceedings did not violate her rights to an impartial jury and effective assistance of counsel; (6) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing her; but, (7) because two murder convictions were entered for the same act, the less culpable conviction under 720 Ill Comp. Stat. Ann. 55/9-1(a)(2) had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for first degree murder and sentence under the EJJ statute, and it ordered that the dispositional order and the mittimus be amended to reflect only one conviction for first degree murder.

Randich v. Pirtano Constr. Co.


No. 2-02-0816


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


346 Ill. App. 3d 414; 804 N.E.2d 581; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 146; 281 Ill. Dec. 616



February 9, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 12, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01--L--332. Honorable Kenneth Moy, Judge, Presiding.
Randich v. Pirtano Constr. Co., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 971 (Ill. App. Ct., July 29, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an emergency medical technician (EMT), brought an interlocutory appeal of Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) decision, granting defendant contractors' 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/ 2-619 (2000) motion and dismissing EMT's complaint. EMT alleged negligence and willful and wanton misconduct with regard to gas line rupture. Petition for rehearing filed subsequent to appellate court's decision.


OVERVIEW: Employees of the contractors were installing underground television cable along a public utility easement when they punctured a gas main. The EMT was among those responding to contend with the leak and to ensure safety. The leaking gas was ignited by an unknown source and the EMT was injured. The contractors based their § 2-619 motion on the Illinois fireman's rule. The trial court dismissed all of the claims against the contractors. The appellate court affirmed in part. The fireman's rule applied to the EMT's negligence action against the contractors but not to his action for willful and wanton misconduct. Thus, dismissal of the willful and wanton misconduct claim was error. The EMT sought a rehearing based on the newly enacted 425 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 25/9f (2003). The appellate court noted that the statute was unclear as to whether it was imposing a new duty on owner/occupiers or was simply codifying a portion of the fireman's rule. Regardless, the appellate court refused to apply the statute retroactively to the EMT's case, ruling that to do so would violate the contractors' due process rights.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the EMT's negligence claim against the contractors was affirmed but the dismissal of his willful and wanton misconduct claim was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings. The EMT's petition for rehearing was denied.

People v. M.T. (In re M.T.)


No. 1-01-2314


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


346 Ill. App. 3d 83; 804 N.E.2d 1075; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 94; 281 Ill. Dec. 780



February 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 15, 2004.
Rehearing denied by In re M.T., 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 244 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 5, 2004)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by In re M.T., 808 N.E.2d 1007, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 945, 283 Ill. Dec. 719 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart F. Lubin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile appealed from his adjudication of delinquency by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) after he was found guilty on a charge of indecent solicitation of an adult pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-6.5(a)(1)(ii) (2000). He also appealed from the dispositional order, which sentenced him to 30 days in a juvenile detention center and 18 months' probation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged after he arranged for an 18-year-old female to perform oral sex on a 16-year-old classmate. On appeal he made several constitutional challenges to § 11-6.5. He also asserted that the statute was not meant to apply to a juvenile. The court affirmed, holding that (1) § 11-6.5(a)(1)(ii) was clear and unambiguous on its face and was fully applicable to juveniles; (2) respondent lacked standing to challenge the statute on the basis that it made misdemeanor conduct a felony because he was not tried as an adult nor convicted of a felony; (3) respondent lacked standing to challenge the statute on the basis that it did not require a culpable mental state or criminal purpose because he could not show that he was in the class he asserted would be aggrieved by the unconstitutionality and furthermore, the statute on its face required both a culpable mental state and a criminal purpose; (4) the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to respondent; (5) respondent lacked standing to challenge the statute's sentencing scheme when it had not been applied to him; and (6) respondent was required to register as a sex offender.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Ragusa


No. 2-02-1131


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


346 Ill. App. 3d 176; 804 N.E.2d 692; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 107; 281 Ill. Dec. 727



February 6, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. No. 02--CF--58. Honorable Leonard J. Wojtecki, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kendall County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him on charges of unlawful possession with intent to deliver methylenadioxy-methamphetamine (MDMA) or ecstasy, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/401(a)(7.5)(A)(ii) (2002), and cannabis, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 550/5(d) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested when police officers executed a search warrant at his home. He was advised of his rights and was taken in for further questioning. Defendant agreed to cooperate with the police in hopes of having his charges reduced after his uncle, a police officer, encouraged cooperation. Defendant's attempts to assist the police failed and he was convicted in a bench trial. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 401(a)(7.5)(A)(ii). The court affirmed in part, holding that (1) § 401 did not violate equal protection or substantive due process because its distinctions between possession of ecstasy pills and possession of ecstasy in its powder form had a reasonable basis; (2) prosecutors were restricted to charging under § 401 based on the form of ecstasy defendant had in his possession; (3) the different sentences for violations of § 401(a) and § 401(d) did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970); but (4) statements defendant made regarding his intent to deliver the cannabis and the ecstasy were made as part of plea-related discussions and were improperly considered as evidence on the intent to deliver charges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions to the extent they were based on the possession of ecstasy and cannabis but reversed his convictions and sentences on the intent to deliver charges. The case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the intent to deliver charges.

People v. Bloomingburg


No. 1-02-2359


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


346 Ill. App. 3d 308; 804 N.E.2d 638; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 80; 281 Ill. Dec. 673



February 3, 2004, Decided  
February 3, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 15, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Bloomingburg, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1637 (Ill., Dec. 1, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bloomingburg v. Illinois, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 2754 (U.S., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; mittimus ordered corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of first degree murder and sentenced him to 35 years' imprisonment, plus 25 years pursuant to the firearm enhancement provision, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(d) (2000), for a total of 60 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised several issues. The appellate court concluded that defense counsel did not render ineffective assistance of counsel by conceding defendant's guilt and pursuing an unavailable theory of self-defense because the evidence against defendant was overwhelming where he confessed, both in a videotaped statement and in his testimony at trial, to shooting the victim, and two eyewitnesses positively identified defendant as the shooter. Defense counsel's conduct did not constitute a "total failure of legal representation." His conduct demonstrated an attempt to present a defense, albeit, unsuccessfully, and to test the State's case against defendant. In addition, the firearm enhancement provision, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(d) (2000), did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, the Proportionate Penalties Clause, because there was no basis to compare two offenses with identical elements where there was only one offense of murder in Illinois. Also, the firearm enhancement provision did not constitute a double enhancement because the firearm factor was not an inherent or essential element of murder and it was only used to impose a longer sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court ordered that the mittimus in the case be corrected to reflect a credit of 696 days for defendant's pretrial custody. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Rucker


No. 1-01-3617


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


346 Ill. App. 3d 873; 803 N.E.2d 31; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 76; 280 Ill. Dec. 801



February 2, 2004, Decided  
February 2, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004. Petition for Rehearing Denied January 27, 2004. As Modified.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 01 CR 7093. Honorable Lon William Shultz, Judge Presiding.
People v. Rucker, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1037 (Ill. App. Ct., Aug. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of a school and possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a directed finding in favor of defendant on the first count and, after a bench trial, convicted defendant of the second count and sentenced him to 12 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly failed to consider his posttrial pro se motion for reduction of sentence. The appellate court found that defendant's motion for reduction of sentence did not fall within the exception for pro se motions alleging ineffective assistance of counsel because his motion failed to raise any issue of ineffectiveness. Therefore, the appellate court had jurisdiction over the instant appeal. Defendant also argued that the trial court should have conducted an inquiry into his allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel based on counsel's failure to file a motion to quash the arrest and suppress the evidence. The appellate court found no error, as such motions would have been futile; defendant's arrest was based on probable cause, and therefore the search incident thereto was legal. As for defendant's challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, the appellate court held that the stipulated evidence was sufficient to support the finding that the substance possessed by defendant was cocaine. Finally, as for defendant's sentence, the appellate court held that imposition of sentence upon defendant as a Class X offender was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Normand


No. 2-02-0857


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


345 Ill. App. 3d 736; 803 N.E.2d 1099; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 86; 281 Ill. Dec. 478



January 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 26, 2004.
Appeal granted by People v. Normand, 209 Ill. 2d 595, 813 N.E.2d 227, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 793, 286 Ill. Dec. 170 (2004)
Affirmed by People v. Normand, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 951 (Ill., June 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. No. 00--CF--123. Honorable Stephen C. Pemberton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) convicting him, after a bench trial, of possessing child pornography in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-20.1 (2000). He argued that the statute was unconstitutional in its application. He also argued, and the State conceded, that he was entitled to a credit against his fines for time spent in custody before sentencing.


OVERVIEW: After the invalidation as overbroad of those portions of the federal child pornography statute that prohibited virtual images of children, the highest court in Illinois, in the Alexander case, similarly severed and invalidated a provision in § 11-20.1 that prohibited computer-generated pornographic images of children. That court had, however, specifically rejected constitutional attacks on those portions of the statute dealing with images of real children. Defendant argued that his convictions of violating the "real children" prohibitions of § 11-20.1 were unconstitutional because the prosecution had not proved that the images found in his possession were truly those of real children. The appellate court held that federal and Illinois case law did not place that heavy burden on the State. A finder of fact could still make a judgment as to whether images depicted real people, and the trial court's findings of fact made it clear that it had made such a judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter solely for determination of the amount of credit due against defendant's fines.

People v. Diestelhorst


NO. 5-02-0218


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 1172; 801 N.E.2d 1146; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 60; 280 Ill. Dec. 201



January 27, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 27, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Diestelhorst, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 760 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County. No. 01-CF-73. Honorable John W. McGuire, Judge, presiding.
People v. Diestelhorst, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1551 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 23, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois) convicting him, as a previously convicted sex offender against children, of three counts of improperly approaching, contacting, or communicating with a child in a public park in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-9.4(a) (2000). His primary argument, among many, challenged the statute as unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: The charges arose out of defendant's conduct when he approached a high school boys' baseball team as they practiced in a park and spoke with several players. The appellate court held that the statute and the charging instrument both defined the prohibited conduct with sufficient clarity, and that the State presented legally sufficient evidence of defendant's violation. It also held that the statute was a reasonable exercise of the police power to protect children from sex offenders. There was no need to hold separate preliminary hearings on each charge, where they were similar and arose out of the same incident. Counsel was not ineffective in failing to challenge the information or request a bill of particulars, since such challenges could not have succeeded. Finally, the appellate court declined to interfere with the trial court's sentencing decision, reasonably based as it was on defendant's long record and the dangers posed by offenders against children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Pulley


No. 1-02-2023


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 916; 803 N.E.2d 953; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 20; 281 Ill. Dec. 332



January 21, 2004, Decided  
January 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 27, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Pulley, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 449 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Ralph Reyna, Judge Presiding.
People v. Pulley, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1629 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 22, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The instant appeal arose from defendant's conviction for aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW), under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) (2000) following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: There was sufficient evidence to show defendant was not on his own land at the time of the crime, aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW) 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) (2000). An officer's testimony showed defendant was standing with a gun in his hand outside of a government housing project. Also, the penalty for aggravated UUW was not unconstitutionally disproportionate under Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The seriousness of the conduct to be deterred under the UUW statute justified a higher sentence than the sentence for conduct without a loaded weapon. The UUW statute required a mental state under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1) (2000) and was not unconstitutional. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1) (2000) and 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(3)(A) (2000) were constitutional in that they bore a rational relationship to the public interest served, and the means adopted were reasonably designed to accomplish the desired objective. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1) (2000) did not violate due process and equal protection. There was a rational basis for denying renters the right to possess guns in apartment buildings' common areas.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

People v. Rivera


1-01-2747


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


346 Ill. App. 3d 398; 803 N.E.2d 882; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 14; 281 Ill. Dec. 261



January 16, 2004, Decided  
January 16, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 85 C 2128. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.
People v. Rivera, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 996 (Ill. App. Ct., Nov. 1, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a final judgment and dismissed the inmate's post-conviction petition. The inmate challenged the propriety of the summary dismissal of the petition. The petition was filed pursuant to the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2000).


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed his post-conviction petition after his second conviction for a murder was affirmed on direct appeal. In that direct appeal, the Illinois Supreme Court had ruled that the enhancement of the inmate's second sentence based on a weapons violation occurring subsequent to the original conviction was proper. In his appeal of the post-conviction petition dismissal, the inmate asserted that the increase in sentence violated the rule in Apprendi, which was declared subsequent to the second sentencing. The court affirmed. The supreme court's ruling was the law of the case on the enhanced sentence. Further, the Apprendi rule did not apply retroactively, as it was a new constitutional rule that did not fall into one of the two non-retroactive application exceptions set out in Teague v. Lane. And, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4 (1985), the trial court could use the weapons violation to extend the inmate's sentence after his second conviction on the murder charge. The conviction operated independently, making the extended-term sentence rule one of the recognized Apprendi exceptions.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the inmate's petition was affirmed.

People v. Lee


No. 3-02-0303


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


345 Ill. App. 3d 782; 803 N.E.2d 640; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 16; 281 Ill. Dec. 236



January 16, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 20, 2004.
Appeal granted by People v. Lee, 209 Ill. 2d 592, 813 N.E.2d 226, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 763, 286 Ill. Dec. 169 (2004)
Vacated by, Judgment entered by People v. Lee, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 618 (Ill., Apr. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 00-CF-1614. Honorable Barbara Badger, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; sentence vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a controlled substance and unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver as a result of cocaine found on his person when he was arrested for violation of Joliet, Ill., Mun. Code § 21-10.1 (1990) outlawing loitering for the purpose of engaging in drug-related activity.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the ordinance defining the criminal offense of loitering for the purpose of engaging in a drug-related activity was unconstitutionally vague because the phrase "circumstances manifesting the purpose to engage in drug-related activity" and the ordinance section listing circumstances which might be considered in determining whether such purpose was manifested did not provide adequate notice of the prohibited conduct nor establish minimal guidelines for enforcement. The appellate court concluded that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it failed to provide adequate notice of prohibited conduct and did not delineate adequate enforcement standards. A person reading the ordinance could not know what specific acts would manifest a drug-related purpose. The nine criteria listed in the ordinance for the police to use in determining whether a drug-related purpose had been manifested were not the only circumstances that could be considered. The police were given unfettered discretion to determine whether a person's conduct manifested drug activity. Because the cocaine found on defendant was seized in an unlawful arrest, it had to be suppressed.


OUTCOME: Because the State could not prevail on remand without the suppressed evidence, defendant's convictions had to be reversed and the sentence vacated.

People v. Smith


No. 2-02-0966


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


345 Ill. App. 3d 742; 803 N.E.2d 570; 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 8; 281 Ill. Dec. 166



January 14, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 19, 2004.
Vacated without op. by, Remanded by People v. Smith, 216 Ill. 2d 725, 834 N.E.2d 903, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1007, 296 Ill. Dec. 98 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 99--CF--1708. Honorable Joseph G. McGraw, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Smith, 326 Ill. App. 3d 1172, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 5762 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that dismissed his postconviction petition; defendant claimed that he was denied pretrial notice that the State intended to seek a Class X sentence and that his equal protection rights were violated.


OVERVIEW: The trial court imposed a 24-year, Class X prison term partially based on his criminal history. The appellate court held that pretrial notice under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/111-3(c) (1998) was not required since defendant was to be sentenced as Class X offender under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (1998). Defendant's right to equal protection was not violated. The age classification was not irrational because the attainment of the age of 21 was a well-recognized significant milestone in society. The goal of rehabilitating repeat offenders who were less than 21 years old provided a rational basis and reasonable method for punishing older repeat offenders more severely. Therefore, the trial court did not err in dismissing defendant's claim under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-2.1(a)(2) (2002) as frivolous and patently without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Priest


1-01-4126


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 660; 803 N.E.2d 181; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1585; 280 Ill. Dec. 951



December 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 8815. Honorable Thomas M. Davy, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), denied defendant's motion for a new sentencing hearing after it had previously sentenced him in absentia following entry of his guilty plea to a charge of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and his failure to appear on two separate dates for sentencing. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. When he did not appear at his sentencing hearing, he was sentenced in absentia to 15 years in prison. While he was missing, his attorney filed motions to withdraw his guilty plea and to reconsider his sentence. The trial court never ruled on either motion. He was taken into custody. His motion for a new sentencing hearing was denied. On appeal, the appellate court found that it did not have jurisdiction over his appeal. It so concluded because it found he did not strictly comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d); the failure to obtain rulings on the two motions required dismissal of his appeal under that rule. It also found 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-4.1(g) (2000), regarding new trial or new sentencing hearing motions, did not affect the allotted time for appealing in a criminal case. It explained that his direct appeal rights were not concurrent with his motion for a new sentencing hearing; thus, he could not use the denial of that motion to stall the time limit for filing a direct appeal. Also, since he did not appeal the denial of his new sentencing motion, no issues remained on appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal of defendant's conviction and sentence were dismissed.

People v. Rials


No. 1-02-2073


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 636; 802 N.E.2d 1240; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1590; 280 Ill. Dec. 719



December 31, 2003, Decided  
December 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Rials, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 628 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CR 2796. Honorable Vincent M. Gaughan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (2000) at the second stage without granting an evidentiary hearing. The inmate had been convicted and sentenced on a charge of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's conviction was affirmed on direct appeal after his appellate counsel filed an Anders motion and was allowed to withdraw from the case. During the pendency of the appeal, the inmate filed his post-conviction petition, attacking the constitutionality of his sentence and generally citing to several constitutional amendments. Post-trial counsel was appointed. The State moved to dismiss the petition. Appointed counsel did not amend the inmate's pro se petition but filed an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) certificate of compliance, indicating that the petition adequately represented the inmate's constitutional claims. The motion to dismiss was granted. On appeal, the inmate asserted ineffective assistance of appellate counsel and of post-conviction counsel. The court affirmed. The inmate waived any issue as to effective assistance of appellate counsel by failing to include the claim in his petition. Post-conviction counsel's obligations were governed by Rule 651(c), not the Strickland test. She was not required to search the record for additional constitutional claims the inmate might have asserted and her failure to do so was not a breach of any of her Rule 651(c) obligations.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the inmate's post-conviction petition was affirmed.

Schmid v. Fairmont Hotel Company-Chicago


No. 1-02-3614


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 475; 803 N.E.2d 166; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1591; 280 Ill. Dec. 936



December 31, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by Schmid v. Fairmont Hotel Co., 209 Ill. 2d 601, 813 N.E.2d 229, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 705, 286 Ill. Dec. 172 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 L 5607. Honorable James M. Varga, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hotel sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment against the hotel, denied its motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV), or in the alternative, for a new trial, and granted summary judgment to defendant electric company on an indemnity crossclaim. The judgment was entered in plaintiff guest's negligence action against the hotel and the electric company.


OVERVIEW: The guest was injured when he received an electric shock from a switch that turned on lights over a vanity in his hotel room. The shock caused him to jump back and strike his shoulder on a door frame. Testimony from maintenance personnel at the hotel established that while they were aware that short circuits did occurr in the vanity lights, they had never heard of such a short circuit causing a shock at the light switch. The guest did not present any expert evidence on the issue. The jury returned a general verdict against the hotel, finding it solely liable for the guest's injury. On appeal, the hotel argued that its JNOV motion should have been granted because it did not owe any duty to the guest. The court agreed. The existence of duty, including the element of whether an injury was reasonably foreseeable, was an initial question of law for the trial court to answer before a negligence case could be submitted to a jury. The presence of a short in the vanity light fixture was not a sufficient predicate for the hotel to anticipate the danger of an electric shock at the light switch because, under the facts of the case, the risk of such a shock was not reasonably foreseeable.


OUTCOME: The judgment against the hotel and in favor of the guest was reversed. The appeal of the grant of summary judgment to the electric company was dismissed as moot.

People v. Rozela


No. 2-02-1282


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


345 Ill. App. 3d 217; 802 N.E.2d 372; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1570; 280 Ill. Dec. 447



December 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 30, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Rozela, 209 Ill. 2d 597, 813 N.E.2d 227, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 706, 286 Ill. Dec. 170 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 02--DT--4298. Honorable Mark W. Dwyer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Du Page County (Illinois), entered a judgment that denied defendant's petition to rescind the statutory summary suspension of her driver's license for driving under the influence of alcohol. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw defendant's car speed past him. The officer then determined she was speeding and pulled over her car after observing it weave twice across a lane dividing line. The officer approached, and saw that defendant's eyes were glassy and bloodshot. The officer also smelled a strong odor of alcohol on her breath. The officer then administered certain sobriety tests. Defendant failed the horizontal gaze nystagmus test, but passed three other tests. The officer then asked her to submit to a portable breath test (PBT) and she agreed to do so. The result indicated defendant was intoxicated. Defendant was arrested and her driving privileges were suspended for three months. At a statutory summary suspension proceeding, the trial court admitted the result over defendant's objection. At the end of the hearing, the trial court found the officer's testimony credible and denied her petition to rescind the suspension. On appeal, the appellate court found that the statute authorizing the PBT was constitutional, the officer had reasonable suspicion to ask her to submit to the PBT, and the State was not required to show an adequate foundation to introduce the test results.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

DMS Pharm. Group v. County of Cook


Nos. 1-02-1347 & 1-02-3436


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 430; 803 N.E.2d 151; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1565; 280 Ill. Dec. 921



December 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004. As Corrected February 11, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 02 CH 1619 & 02 CR 11229. Honorable Nancy J. Arnold, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pharmaceutical group sued appellee county in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court granted the county's motion to dismiss. The pharmaceutical group filed a separate suit in the court for declaratory and injunctive relief against the county. The trial court granted summary judgment to the county. The pharmaceutical group appealed both judgments.


OVERVIEW: The pharmaceutical group alleged that the county violated state law and its own competitive bidding ordinance by using requests for information and requests for proposals to award a contract to supply prescription medication and other pharmaceuticals to the county. The pharmaceutical group also claimed that the county's board of commissioners improperly delegated its power to expend taxpayer funds for the purchase of pharmaceuticals to the county's comptroller. The county argued that it was not subject to the competitive bidding laws due to its status as a home rule entity under the Illinois Constitution and that the contract at issue was not adapted to competitive bidding. On appeal, the court found that the trial court properly granted the county's motion to dismiss as the county did not violate state law as it was not acting administratively, or its own ordinance as the ordinance, and the contract was not adaptable to competitive bidding. Further, the trial court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the county and against the pharmaceutical group in the other suit as the county did not improperly transfer power from one branch of government to another.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Hill


No. 1-02-1387


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 620; 803 N.E.2d 138; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1566; 280 Ill. Dec. 908



December 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Hill, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1681 (Ill., Nov. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 13448. Honorable Diane Cannon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and possession of a controlled substance. Because of his prior convictions, the trial court sentenced defendant to eight years' imprisonment for possession of a stolen motor vehicle under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2000), concurrent to his one-year sentence for possession of a controlled substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, the trial court granted defense counsel's request to order a clinical examination of defendant. On its own motion, the court ordered a second examination. The examiners did not find defendant unfit for trial. On appeal, the court found that, considering defendant's behavior, his demeanor at trial, and the prior medical opinion on his competence to stand trial, no bona fide doubt of defendant's fitness to stand trial existed and thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to conduct a fitness hearing. Defendant was able to understand the nature of the proceedings, assist in his own defense, and did not establish a bona fide doubt as to his fitness. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to sua sponte order a fitness hearing. Further, by consenting to the admission of the stipulation of a forensic chemist's opinion at trial, defendant could not object to the admission of that stipulation for the first time on appeal. Furthermore, the court declined to review the issue as plain error. Finally, the mandatory Class X offender provision was constitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment and the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Defendant, a gang member, beat a rival gang member to death with a tire jack after the victim rammed the car defendant was in. After the jury found defendant guilty of murder, the trial court found that the crime was committed with exceptional brutality. On that basis, an extended term sentence was imposed. People v. Johns


No. 3-01-0629


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


345 Ill. App. 3d 237; 802 N.E.2d 305; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1548; 280 Ill. Dec. 380



December 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 26, 2004.
Appeal denied by People v. Johns, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 510 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 01--CF--17. Honorable Donald C. Courson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, which entered judgment on a jury determination that defendant was guilty of two felony murders under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(3) (2000) and sentenced defendant to natural life imprisonment under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(c)(ii) (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant went with two accomplices to rob victim one in his home. Once there, victim one stated that he kept his money at his mother's home. The actual shooter accompanied victim one to his mother's home but left defendant, and a gun the shooter provided to defendant, with victim two, victim one's girlfriend. The shooter returned alone and told defendant to leave. Defendant left and then heard a shot. The three conspirators then fled the scene. On appeal, defendant questioned the sufficiency of the evidence to convict him of the two murders and argued that his sentence was unconstitutional as applied. The court affirmed. Defendant was accountable for felony murder of victim one because he willingly accompanied the others to victim one's home with the intent to rob him, he continued to participate in the enterprise by staying at that location with victim two, and he did not report the incident to police. As to victim two, the robbery was not over simply because defendant left the apartment. The threat of force against her continued until she was killed, making defendant accountable for her death. Finally, the natural life sentence did not violate defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Sawczenko-Dub


No. 1-02-2156


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


345 Ill. App. 3d 522; 803 N.E.2d 62; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1517; 280 Ill. Dec. 832



December 16, 2003, Decided  
December 16, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 13, 2004. Petition for Rehearing Denied January 12, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Sawczenko-Dub, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 141 (Ill. App. Ct., Jan. 12, 2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Sawczenko-Dub, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 601 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable THOMAS M. TUCKER, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of the first-degree murder of her husband. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim, her husband, began to argue. The victim went to his mother's house nearby. Defendant succeeded in luring him back to their apartment. The victim was soon found dead of a gunshot wound. Defendant later gave a statement. In it, she said she fully loaded a shotgun with shotgun shells. Defendant then lured the victim back to their apartment, picked up the gun, and shot him to death. At trial, she changed her story and said she accidentally fired the gun, killing the victim. In a bench trial, the trial court found the statement to be more credible and convicted her of first-degree murder. It then enhanced her sentence with an additional sentence for discharging a firearm and causing a death during an offense. On appeal, the appellate court found that the additional sentence did not violate the Illinois Constitution's Proportionate Penalties Clause, its separation of powers principles, or its Double Jeopardy Clause, and did not constitute an impermissible double enhancement of the offense of first-degree murder or her sentence. Also, it found that evidence was sufficient to convict her of first-degree murder and that she personally discharged a firearm.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Taylor


No. 1-02-1319


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


344 Ill. App. 3d 929; 801 N.E.2d 1005; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1407; 280 Ill. Dec. 60



December 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 23, 2004.
Rehearing denied by People v. Taylor, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1657 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 18, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Taylor, 208 Ill. 2d 553, 809 N.E.2d 1292, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 482, 284 Ill. Dec. 346 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Rodolfo Garcia, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of aggravated battery of a merchant and retail theft of merchandise valued at less than $ 150. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/16A-4 (2000) of the retail theft statute was unconstitutional because it contained a mandatory presumption that relieved the State of its burden to prove the element of intent. The appellate court agreed that the presumption contained in § 16-4 was constitutionally infirm but concluded that it could be severed from the remainder of the retail theft statute and intent could be inferred by surrounding circumstances and proved by circumstantial evidence. It assumed the trial judge found the defendant guilty of retail theft without relying on the constitutionally infirm presumption, but rather, inferred the requisite intent from the surrounding circumstances. The appellate court also found the merchant's uncontradicted testimony that he identified himself to the defendant, if believed, was sufficient to establish that the defendant knew that he was a merchant. Because defense counsel did not entirely fail to subject the State's case to meaningful adversarial testing, prejudice was not presumed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Johnson v. Duncan (In re M.M.D.)


No. 3-03-0231


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 345; 800 N.E.2d 831; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1373; 279 Ill. Dec. 543


April 17, 2003, Assigned; October 02, 2003, Submitted  
November 20, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 18, 2003. Certificate of Importance Denied December 18, 2003.
Appeal granted by Johnson v. Duncan (In re M.M.D), 207 Ill. 2d 604, 807 N.E.2d 975, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 20, 283 Ill. Dec. 134 (2004)
Affirmed by Johnson v. Duncan (In re M.M.D.), 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1674 (Ill., Nov. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Peoria County, Illinois. Nos. 96--F--543 & 96--P--617. Honorable Chris L. Fredericksen Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father filed a petition in the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois), seeking termination (or alternatively, modification) of an order granting visitation rights to appellees, his child's maternal grandparents. The judge denied his petition and a subsequent motion to reconsider. He filed an appeal claiming the judge erred because the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to enforce the visitation order.


OVERVIEW: After the mother died in childbirth, the father's child resided in foster care with the grandparents for almost five years. In 2002, in Wickham v. Byrne, the Illinois Supreme Court held that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b)(1), (3) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, authorizing courts to order grandparent visitation upon a finding that such visitation was in the best interests and welfare of the child, were unconstitutional. The father claimed that the holding declaring the grandparent visitation statute unconstitutional voided appellee grandparents' visitation order as a matter of law. The appellate court found that, although § 607(b)(1), (3) were intended to supersede the common law, such intent was never realized because the statute was invalid from its inception, and the unconstitutionality of § 607(b)(1), (3) did not void the grandparents' visitation rights as a matter of law. However, as a matter of fact, a visitation order had to pass scrutiny under the principles articulated in Wickham.


OUTCOME: The judgement was affirmed.

People v. Willis


No. 1-01-4170


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


344 Ill. App. 3d 868; 801 N.E.2d 47; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1363; 279 Ill. Dec. 755



November 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 8, 2004.
Appeal granted by People v. Willis, 207 Ill. 2d 627, 807 N.E.2d 981, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 19, 283 Ill. Dec. 140 (2004)
Reversed by People v. Willis, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 944 (Ill., June 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James L. Rhodes, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of criminal damage to property exceeding $ 300. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended the police lacked probable cause to justify his arrest and his confession should be suppressed because the police failed to take him before a judge for a probable cause determination before he confessed. While the appellate court found that the initial arrest was based on probable cause, it concluded the lengthy detention before any judicial intervention violated the Fourth Amendment and that suppression of the confession was the proper remedy. Defendant's confession occurred 73 hours after his custodial detention began; police made no attempt to present him to a judge for a probable cause hearing during those 73 hours. Presentment did not come for another l4 1/2 hours. The 73-hour detention before defendant made his confession far exceeded the 48-hour period for a presumably reasonable delay. Accordingly, the burden fell on the State to show an emergency or extraordinary circumstance was to blame. The State never attempted to make such a showing. Defendant's lawful detention became unlawful in violation of the Fourth Amendment after 48 hours. No intervening circumstances explained defendant's decision to confess after twice denying involvement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1473 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miles


No. 2-02-0760


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 315; 800 N.E.2d 122; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1385; 279 Ill. Dec. 280



November 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 11, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 02--CF--967. Honorable Kathryn E. Creswell Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicting defendant of possession of a counterfeit credit card in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/16 (2002) and sentencing defendant to five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant place a bag of six counterfeit credit cards in a door panel of the van. The trial court found that defendant's possession of more than two counterfeit credit cards constituted prima facie evidence that defendant intended to defraud pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 250/16 (2002). The appellate court found that the second sentence of § 16, which allowed the presumption made by the trial court, constituted an impermissible mandatory rebuttable presumption. Defendant's intent to defraud was established only by the State's evidence showing that defendant possessed six counterfeit credit cards. As such, the State was effectively relieved of its burden of proving defendant's intent to defraud beyond a reasonable doubt. This burden shifted to defendant to prove that she was merely holding the bag and had no knowledge of its contents. This was an unconstitutional shift of the evidentiary burden. The second sentence of § 16 was severable under 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 70/1.31 (2002), because the excision of the second sentence, which operated only to ease the State's burden of proof, did not impair the meaning or operation of the remainder of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

People v. Bolton (In re Bolton)


NO. 4-02-0515


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 1223; 800 N.E.2d 128; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1387; 279 Ill. Dec. 286



November 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 12, 2003.
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Bolton (In re Bolton), 214 Ill. 2d 532, 824 N.E.2d 278, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 332, 291 Ill. Dec. 702 (2005)
Different results reached on reconsideration by In re Det. of Bolton, 357 Ill. App. 3d 1099, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 3314 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 01MR134. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which entered judgment on a jury verdict that found defendant to be a sexually violent person pursuant to the Illinois Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 through 99 (2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to criminal sexual assault on his six-year old stepsister, which began when defendant was 12 years old. He was sentenced to intensive probation, which was revoked after defendant was found trying to lure another young girl to a secluded area for a sexual offense. He was sentenced to 12 years of imprisonment. Prior to his scheduled mandatory supervised release, a petition was filed seeking to have defendant civilly committed to the State's sex offender treatment program. The evidence at trial was conflicting as to whether defendant was at high risk for repeat offenses. The State's witnesses relied extensively on psychological testing and actuarial data to predict the potential for recidivism. The court reversed because the actuarial instruments used by the State's experts did not satisfy the Frye test for admissibility. The actuarial instruments, which added a quality of mathematical or objective certainty to what was otherwise the subjective opinion of the experts, instilled a false sense of confidence in the expert's opinions. Further, the instruments were of recent development, were controversial, and had not been subjected to empirical testing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Forcum


NO. 5-01-0692


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 427; 800 N.E.2d 499; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1352; 279 Ill. Dec. 431



November 7, 2003, Decided  
November 7, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Forcum, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 330 (Ill., Jan. 28, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Forcum v. Illinois, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3939 (U.S., June 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 00-CF-277. Honorable E. Dan Kimmel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, armed violence, and home invasion. He was sentenced to natural-life imprisonment for first-degree murder, 30 years imprisonment for attempted first-degree murder, 30 years imprisonment for armed violence, and 30 years imprisonment for home invasion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his ex-girlfriend and tried to kill her boyfriend. The appellate court held the trial court's use of a special interrogatory asking if the murder was exceptionally brutal or heinous, under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b) (2000), allowing an extended sentence, was not error. It did not add an element to the crime, contrary to ex post facto prohibitions, as it was a sentencing factor. Photographs of the murder victim's injuries, corroborating testimony of crime scene technicians, and helping the jury understand a pathologist's testimony, were admissible. Erroneously admitted hearsay about defendant's prior threats did not require a new trial given overwhelming evidence of his guilt. Testimony of defendant's tumultuous relationship with the murder victim was not hearsay, and any error in admitting it was harmless. The prosecutor could play a tape and read from a letter admitted into evidence during his closing. Defendant's armed violence conviction was based on the same act as the attempted murder and had to be vacated, but he could be convicted of home invasion and murder, despite the interrelationship of the acts those convictions were based on.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and home invasion were affirmed, and his armed violence conviction was vacated.
