People v. Jones


NO. 5-02-0398


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 413; 800 N.E.2d 97; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1353; 279 Ill. Dec. 255



November 7, 2003, Decided  
November 7, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Jones, 208 Ill. 2d 547, 809 N.E.2d 1289, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 519, 284 Ill. Dec. 343 (2004)
Reversed by People v. Jones, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 632 (Ill., May 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 01-CF-218. Honorable Robert P. LeChien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order denying the suppression of evidence reversed; defendant's conviction and sentence reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. Prior to the trial, defendant moved to suppress the seized evidence. Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied his motion.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motions to suppress. Specifically, defendant argued that the police officer did not have probable cause to seize and search the box the officer observed during the traffic stop, and, as a result, the weapons located during the officer's subsequent search of the vehicle were tainted fruit that should have been suppressed. The appellate court concluded that the officer did not have probable cause to search either the box in defendant's front shirt pocket or the remainder of the vehicle's contents because the only reason offered by the officer justifying his search of the box was the officer's conclusion that the box was "drug paraphernalia." However, the officer testified that this was only a suspicion that was confirmed after he had opened the box. Further, the officer conceded that the box could contain a variety of non-illicit items and that it did not have only one purpose. In addition, the State did not demonstrate beyond a preponderance of the evidence that the officer's discovery of either or both of the weapons observed in defendant's vehicle would have been inevitable.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court denying the suppression of the evidence was reversed. Defendant's conviction and sentence were also reversed.

Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Sanchez, 222 Ill. 2d 594, 861 N.E.2d 662, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1786, 308 Ill. Dec. 331 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by United States ex rel. Sanchez v. Jones, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 42427 (N.D. Ill., May 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Henry R. Simmons, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a charge of aggravated sexual assault. He appealed his sentence to a term of natural life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a prior conviction for aggravated sexual assault. The prior conviction was used to enhance his sentence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(d)(2) (2000). On appeal, defendant asserted that his sentence violated the Proportionate Penalties Clause in Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970), that it was imposed in violation of his Apprendi rights, and that the sentence violated his right to a trial by jury. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-14(d)(2) (2000) not violate his Ill. Const. art. I, § 13 (1970) right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: Both defendant's conviction and his sentence were affirmed.

Serpico v. Vill. of Elmwood Park


No. 1-02-1762


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


344 Ill. App. 3d 203; 799 N.E.2d 961; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1329; 279 Ill. Dec. 158



October 31, 2003, Decided  
October 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CH 17896. The Honorable Sophia H. Hall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a sports bar and its owner (the bar), appealed from a summary judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declaring that an ordinance enacted by defendant village banning simulated video gaming devices was not unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Elmwood Park, Ill., Ordinance 2001-08 (2001) banned video gaming devices throughout the village, although officials admitted that they only enforced the ban against public places. The bar removed its slot machines and similar games, but challenged the ordinance's constitutionality. The appellate court held that the bar had not met the heavy burden of showing unconstitutionality. First, gambling games devoid of narrative or intellectual content were not protected expression under the First Amendment as some sophisticated games were. The appeals court examined the claims of substantive due process and equal protection violation solely to ascertain whether the ordinance bore a rational relationship to controlling illegal gambling, and found that it did. The village was within its powers in determining that electronic gambling in public posed the greatest threat to public welfare. Finally, the bar could not challenge the ordinance as vague when it admitted that it knew that its machines had violated it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment.

LaSalle Nat'l Bank v. City of Highland Park


No. 2-02-1012


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 259; 799 N.E.2d 781; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1336; 278 Ill. Dec. 916



October 31, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing.
Appeal denied by LaSalle Nat'l Bank v. City of Highland Park, 208 Ill. 2d 539, 809 N.E.2d 1287, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 403, 284 Ill. Dec. 341 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Emmerman v. City of Highland Park, 160 L. Ed. 2d 365, 125 S. Ct. 477, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7492 (U.S., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 01--MR--703. Honorable Barbara Gilleran Johnson, Judge, Presiding.
LaSalle Nat'l Bank v. City of Highland Park, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1230 (Ill. App. Ct., Sept. 29, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) dismissing a complaint against defendants, the city, its zoning board, and various officials, seeking review of the board's denial of a variance allowing them to build on the second of two contiguous, undersized lots. They also challenged the constitutionality of the zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: When the landowners bought their two lots, only one of which had been built on, each lot was too small for a single-family dwelling under an ordinance then in effect, as well as the ordinance in effect many years later when they sought a variance to build on the second lot. The appellate court first reviewed the board's decision, deferentially, to assure that it was not against the manifest weight of the evidence, which it was not. The appellate court then addressed the constitutional challenges. It found no federal due process violation, amounting to an uncompensated taking, because there was no showing that the landowners had not done well off their long-term investment, with or without development. Furthermore, although it was not conclusive, it was significant that the landowners had known of the limitation when they bought the property. It was not an unreasonable exercise of the police power for the city to seek to maintain low density in certain areas. Finally, zoning ordinance application was inevitably fact intensive, so it was not necessarily unreasonable, arbitrary, or violative of equal protection to deny the variance even though others' requests had been granted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Powell


NO. 4-02-0567


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 699; 798 N.E.2d 1252; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1330; 278 Ill. Dec. 495



October 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 29, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Douglas County. No. 00CF34. Honorable Frank W. Lincoln, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois) convicting defendant of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 550/5(f) (2000) after denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The police officer pulled defendant over for tailgating. A criminal history inquiry indicated that defendant had been arrested for drug possession. There was an outstanding warrant for defendant's arrest in another county. Defendant told the officer that he and the passenger were going to Mississippi. The officer completed the warning ticket and gave it to defendant. The officer kept defendant's driver's license and spoke to the passenger. The passenger said they were going to a destination in Illinois. The officer asked for permission to search the vehicle, which defendant initially granted but then revoked. A canine unit indicated the presence of drugs. The officer searched the vehicle and found cannabis. The trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress. The traffic stop was complete when the officer issued defendant a warning ticket. At that time, the officer knew that the interior of the car smelled like air freshener that he suspected was used to mask the smell of cannabis, and he knew of the warrant, defendant's criminal record, and that defendant was going to Mississippi. This did not constitute a reasonable and articulable suspicion to extend the stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for proceedings consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

People v. Culbreath


NO. 4-02-0163


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 998; 798 N.E.2d 1268; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1333; 278 Ill. Dec. 511



October 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 29, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 01CF622. Honorable Donald D. Bernardi, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of aggravated battery, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-4(b)(1) (Supp. 2001). The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) sentenced him to an extended term of six years in prison, based on a prior conviction, and ordered that within two years of his release from prison, defendant pay $ 10,026 in restitution to the hospital that treated the victim. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court violated his rights to due process and effective assistance of counsel when it conducted voir dire without a court reporter present. The appellate court found no error, since, inter alia, defendant made no claim of error; as such, lack of the record deprived him of nothing. Defendant next argued that trial counsel did not have the authority to waive the court reporter's presence because that decision belonged to defendant. The appellate court held that in a criminal case, the decision whether to waive a court reporter's presence during voir dire remained with defense counsel. As for the restitution order, the appellate court noted that the trial court could order restitution regardless of the term of incarceration or defendant's financial resources. Finally, the appellate court found no error in defendant's extended term sentence since 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann.5/5-8-2(a) (2000) did not require the State to prove to the jury beyond a reasonable doubt defendant's prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Harris


NO. 4-02-0481


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 1014; 798 N.E.2d 1259; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1334; 278 Ill. Dec. 502



October 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 29, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Harris, 211 Ill. 2d 595, 823 N.E.2d 972, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1055 (Ill., Oct. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 01CF355. Honorable Donald D. Bernardi, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (2000). Defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict or for new trial was denied. The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a five-year prison term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(a) (2000) was unconstitutional because it required no culpable mental state and permitted a felony conviction based on innocent conduct. The appellate court disagreed, finding that § 24-1.1 was reasonably designed to remedy the evils the legislature found to be a threat to public safety. Defendant also contended that the trial court erroneously refused his request to stipulate his prior convictions, in violation of the holding in People v. Peete. Defendant acknowledged the error was not raised in his posttrial motion but contended that it could be reviewed under the plain-error doctrine. The appellate court found plain error under both prongs of the plain error rule, since the evidence was closely balanced and the error was fundamental. The jury should have known defendant was a felon and could not possess a firearm. This jury should not have been informed of defendant's four felony convictions by name and reminded several times by the prosecution that defendant was a four-time convicted felon.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the action was remanded for a new trial.

People v. Jennings


NO. 5-00-0482


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 717; 798 N.E.2d 1211; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1263; 278 Ill. Dec. 454



October 16, 2003, Decided  
October 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Jennings, 208 Ill. 2d 546, 809 N.E.2d 1289, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 444, 284 Ill. Dec. 343 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Shelby County. No. 99-CF-55. Honorable Michael P. Kiley, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Shelby County (Illinois) convicting defendant of second-degree murder in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-2 and concealment of a homicidal death in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3.1(a) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant stated that in response to witnessing his wife in the process of committing an extra-marital affair with the victim, defendant attacked the victim. Defendant got on top of the victim, who was facedown on the ground. Defendant hit the victim in the head with a rock. He passed the rock to his wife and stayed on top of the victim while she hit the victim. Defendant sat on top of the victim for at least 15 minutes before the victim quit struggling. The victim's body was found wrapped with chains and cans filled with concrete in a lake. The prosecuting attorney was from the State's attorney appellate prosecutor's office, and he was appointed as a special prosecutor. The prosecutor was improperly appointed as a special prosecutor. Defendant, however, waived his right to challenge the prosecutor's defective commission to prosecute. Defendant did not object to the prosecutor, nor was defendant harmed by participation of the special prosecutor, who was a licensed attorney. Defendant was not entitled to an involuntary manslaughter jury instruction, because the length of the struggle, at least 15 minutes, precluded an involuntary manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1484 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Muldrow v. Muldrow (In re Estate of Muldrow)


No. 1-02-1825


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 1148; 799 N.E.2d 497; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1255; 278 Ill. Dec. 779



October 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 P 1165. Honorable Henry A. Budzinski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The decedent died in 2001. She left a will which nominated her two sons, appellee and appellant, as co-executors. Appellant sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied appellant's petition to name him the sole executor and disqualify appellee from serving as executor.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court erred when it refused to disqualify appellee from serving as executor pursuant to 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-13(a) (2002) because he was a convicted felon. Specifically, the issue was whether the limitation on felons serving as executors contained in 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-13 violated equal protection. The appellate court concluded that an executor was entrusted with property to which others had claims and had to safeguard that property and ultimately distribute it in accordance with the law. A convicted felon had demonstrated an inability to act within the confines of the law. This provided a more than adequate basis for the legislative determination that felons were not qualified to act as executors. Therefore, the appellate court concluded that 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/6-13 did not violate equal protection because it disqualified felons from acting as executors. The statute was constitutional on its face. Because appellee's status as a felon was not disputed at the trial level, the trial court was not required to make additional determinations of fact or to consider any additional factors.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order denying appellant's motion to disqualify appellee, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1485 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Wauconda Fire Prot. Dist. v. Stonewall Orchards


No. 2-02-1116


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 374; 797 N.E.2d 1130; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1248; 278 Ill. Dec. 212



October 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 2003.
Subsequent appeal at Wauconda Fire Prot. Dist. v. Stonewall Orchards, LLP, 207 Ill. 2d 631, 807 N.E.2d 983, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2623, 283 Ill. Dec. 142 (2003)
Affirmed by Wauconda Fire Prot. Dist. v. Stonewall Orchards, LLP, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 318 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 02--CH--1033. Honorable Margaret J. Mullen, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff fire protection district appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a golf club and the county, in the district's action seeking an injunction against defendants to enforce a district ordinance regarding the installation of fire sprinklers. The ordinance was enacted pursuant to authority in the Illinois Fire Protection District Act.


OVERVIEW: Based on a building permit issued by the county, the club built a clubhouse that did not contain sprinklers, even though the district had advised the club that a district ordinance required sprinklers. The clubhouse sat within both the district and an unincorporated area of the county. The district sought an injunction to prevent the county from issuing an occupancy permit and to prevent the club from using the clubhouse. It also sought a declaration that it had authority pursuant to 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 705/11 (2002) to enact and enforce ordinances within the unincorporated portions of the county. Section 11 precluded the district from enacting ordinances where a municipality had adopted fire protection laws. The county asserted it was such a municipality. The court disagreed, holding that (1) based on the definition of municipalities in the Illinois Constitution, the county was not a municipality; (2) the district had concurrent jurisdiction with the county with regard to fire prevention laws; (3) as their ordinances were not in conflict, the club had to comply with both entities ordinances; but (4) the district could not seek enforcement of its ordinances by the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal as to the injunctive relief against the county. The court reversed and remanded the cause for further proceedings, consistent with its opinion, with respect to the injunctive relief sought against the club and the declaratory relief sought against both defendants.

 

1486 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carmichael


No. 1-02-1106


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 855; 799 N.E.2d 401; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1231; 278 Ill. Dec. 683



September 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis J. Porter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, as modified, and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon and sentenced to five years in prison. Defendant appealed his sentence based on an improper enhancement, the Apprendi doctrine, and a violation of the proportional penalties clause in Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The trial court enhanced defendant's sentence under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.1(e) based upon a finding that defendant had previously been convicted of armed violence. The armed violence conviction was based on defendant's commission of the predicate felony of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. The appellate court affirmed but modified defendant's conviction. Armed violence was not an inherently violent offense, and there was insufficient evidence to show that defendant had contemplated the use of force or violence in committing the possession of a controlled substance felony. Therefore, it could not be considered a forcible felony under the catch-all category for forcible felonies in 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-8 (2000), and the armed violence conviction could not be used to enhance defendant's sentence. Resentencing was required. And while armed violence was similar to the charge of unlawful discharge of a weapon, which carried a lesser sentence, the sentencing range for armed violence did not violate the proportionality clause. The two crimes were enacted for different purposes, making a comparative proportionality analysis inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but modified it to reflect that it was for a Class 3 rather than a Class 2 felony. The court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case for defendant's resentencing. The court did not reach the Apprendi argument.

 

1487 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Ceres One Corp. v. Naperville Twp. Rd. Dist.


No. 2-02-1250


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 382; 797 N.E.2d 1097; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1239; 278 Ill. Dec. 179



September 30, 2003, Decdied


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 97--TO--0004. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township road district sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment to appellee tax objectors on one of nine tax objections that challenged a 1996 property tax levy.


OVERVIEW: The objection asserted that a portion of the 1996 tax levy that was designated for a "permanent road fund" was invalid. The district asserted that the road fund was authorized by a special hard road tax levy that was approved in a 1979 referendum pursuant to provisions of the Illinois Highway Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 1-101 et seq. (1977). On appeal, the objectors asserted that the referendum had expired by force of law five years after it was approved. At issue was whether the repeal of the five-year limitation shortly after the 1979 referendum was approved applied retroactively. The court ruled that it did not. The five-year limit was found in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, paras. 6-601, 6-602 (1977). It was removed by Ill. Pub. Acts 81-779, 81-821. The effect of the public acts was made retroactive by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 6-602.1 (1979). But para. 6-602.1 was eliminated in 1980 by Ill. Pub. Act 81-1509 (1980). That same Act left intact the prospective application of the elimination of the five-year period and the procedures outlined in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 6-617 (1979). As the district failed to renew the referendum, it expired by law after five years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1488 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. L.M. (In re D.W.)


No. 1-02-1606


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


344 Ill. App. 3d 30; 799 N.E.2d 410; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1238; 278 Ill. Dec. 692



September 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 2003.
Appeal granted by People v. L.M. (In re D.W.), 207 Ill. 2d 603, 807 N.E.2d 975, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 17, 283 Ill. Dec. 134 (2004)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Lisa M. (In re D.W.), 2005 Ill. LEXIS 319 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard A. Stevens, Judge Presiding.
In re D.W., 294 Ill. App. 3d 1089, 721 N.E.2d 847, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 1202, 242 Ill. Dec. 568 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted a petition by the State and terminated the parental rights of respondent, a mother, with respect to her minor son pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-29(2) (1998) and 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (1998). The mother appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(q) (1998) violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions. Under that section, a parent was presumed unfit if the parent had been criminally convicted of aggravated battery, heinous battery, or attempted murder of any child. The mother had been convicted of the attempted murder of another her children by poisoning the child with a cleaning solution. The appellate court found no basis supporting an argument that the statute violated a party's due process rights merely because the statute required a finding of unfitness as a matter of law based on a prior conviction involving the attempted murder of a child. The appellate court further held that the statute did not violate the equal protection clause. The statute created a method for the State to have a parent declared unfit for the protection of children because of a prior conviction, and did not create classifications for administering direct punishment for convictions. The appellate court finally held that the trial court properly determined that termination was in the best interests of the child.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Colin


1-00-2755


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


344 Ill. App. 3d 119; 799 N.E.2d 451; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1232; 278 Ill. Dec. 733



September 30, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 3, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Colin, 207 Ill. 2d 609, 807 N.E.2d 977, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 208, 283 Ill. Dec. 136 (2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Colin, 368 Ill. App. 3d 1216, 931 N.E.2d 365, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 4289, 341 Ill. Dec. 757 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Claim dismissed by Colin v. McCann, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 34092 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 21, 2009)
Related proceeding at People v. Colin, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 789 (2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Colin v. Pfister, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 159137 (N.D. Ill., Nov. 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CR 6687. Honorable John J. Moran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on two counts of aggravated criminal assault and was sentenced to two consecutive 60-year terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed, arguing that (1) the circuit court erred in admitting other-crimes evidence involving him in a prior sexual assault, and (2) his sentence was unconstitutional under the Apprendi doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant assaulted a young neighbor on numerous occasions. The prior crime evidence also involved a neighbor child. Defendant's wife took part in both sets of assaults by procuring the children for defendant, "preparing" them for the assaults, and then physically aiding defendant in accomplishing the assaults. The court affirmed both defendant's conviction and his sentence. The assistance given by the wife to defendant in the commission of both crimes was a distinctive common feature sufficient to support the trial court's admission of the other crimes evidence to show defendant's modus operandi. As both the trial court and the prosecution went to great lengths to be sure that the jury understood the limited evidentiary value of the other-crimes evidence, there was no abuse of discretion in the ruling that the evidence's probative value outweighed any prejudice to defendant. Finally, although defendant's extended term sentence, based on a trial court finding that defendant's crime was particularly brutal and heinous, violated Apprendi, the error did not warrant reversal because it did not affect the fairness, integrity, or public reputation of the judicial proceeding.


OUTCOME: Both defendant's conviction and his sentence were affirmed.

People v. Briseno


No. 1-02-1995


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 953; 799 N.E.2d 359; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1192; 278 Ill. Dec. 641



September 26, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Jesse G. Reyes, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of cannabis in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(6) (2000). He was sentenced to two years of court supervision and a $ 200 fine. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied defendant's motion to suppress and defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, (2) 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(6) (2000) was unconstitutionally vague, and (3) the State failed to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court concluded that the statement made by defendant in which he admitted smoking marijuana in his vehicle just before driving was not the result of custodial interrogation, and therefore Miranda warnings were not required as a prerequisite for admitting the statement into evidence. Also, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-501(a)(6) was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant was not found guilty based on whim or caprice but, rather, based on evidence that proved defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of driving under the influence of cannabis, including: (1) the officer's testimony that he smelled a strong odor of cannabis in defendant's vehicle and on defendant's breath, (2) defendant's admission that he smoked cannabis in his vehicle just before driving his vehicle, (3) defendant's slurred speech, (4) defendant's dilated pupils, and (5) defendant's motor skills being slower than average.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Henderson


1-99-1277 & 1-99-3220 (consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 1108; 799 N.E.2d 682; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1188; 278 Ill. Dec. 817



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As modified upon Denial of Rehearing.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph Kazmierski, Judge Presiding.
People v. Henderson, 799 N.E.2d 682, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 814, 278 Ill. Dec. 817 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's prior opinion was modified upon denial of rehearing. Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order and judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying his motion to compel deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) testing pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/116-3 (1998) and dismissing a petition for post-conviction relief sought on grounds of an illegal life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man were both convicted of kidnapping and rape, on strong evidence. DNA testing was not available at the time of defendant's trial, and many years later he moved for such testing pursuant to § 116-3. The trial court held that because of the overwhelming evidence of guilt, DNA results could not possibly have constituted new evidence materially relevant to the question of actual innocence, but the appellate court held that under the statute, the trial court should not have made that call, because even though the possibility was not great, a complete non-match between defendant's DNA and genetic material found on clothing items and on the victim's vaginal swabs would still have been significant, even though by no means conclusive, on his claim of actual innocence. Although defendant's post-conviction challenge to his sentence failed, because the rule of Apprendi did not apply retroactively, nor was it violated by life sentences for habitual offenders, favorable DNA test results might support a future post-conviction relief petition based on a claim of actual innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the petition for post-conviction relief but reversed the denial of defendant's motion to compel DNA testing. It remanded the matter to the court below with directions to order DNA testing of certain items of evidence and to order dissemination of results to both sides.

Robinson v. Johnson


1-02-2121


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1191



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication March 25, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. Robinson, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 297 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 22, 2004)
Supplemental opinion at, Rehearing denied by Robinson v. Johnson, 346 Ill. App. 3d 895, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 281 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Honorable Philip L. Bronstein, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question was answered in the negative, trial court's extension orders were vacated, and cause was remanded with directions..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents in discovery, two doctors, sought review from orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motions of plaintiff, an administrator of a deceased patient, in her medical malpractice action. The matter was before the court on a certified question as to whether the six-month statutory period of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402 (1998) could be extended under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 183.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's complaint alleged that her husband's wrongful death was caused by the hospital while he was a patient there. She also joined the doctors as respondents in discovery. The trial court granted two motions to extend the administrator's time to convert the doctors to defendants pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402, and thereafter, it granted the extension. The doctors appealed by certified question as to whether the trial court had the discretion under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 183 to grant the extension. The court reviewed the meaning and purpose of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-402 and concluded that it was not ambiguous. It further found that § 2-402 was a special statutory action and as such, the time limitations contained therein were not subject to extension under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 183. Further, Rule 183 only applied to time limits set forth in Illinois Supreme Court Rules and was therefore inapplicable to a statutory time limit. The court dismissed arguments that custom and practice or an unjust result required that the extensions be allowed, and noted that the doctors were not engaged in delay or evasive tactics to squander the six-month period.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative. The extension orders were vacated and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Montalbano v. Ill. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


NO. 4-03-0075


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 471; 797 N.E.2d 1078; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1220; 278 Ill. Dec. 160



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 2003.
Appeal denied by Montalbano v. Ill. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 692 (Ill., May 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 01MR186. Honorable Elizabeth A. Robb, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which upheld a final administrative decision of defendant Illinois Department of Children and Family Services. That decision denied plaintiff's request to expunge an indicated finding of sexual penetration, molestation, and substantial risk of harm.


OVERVIEW: The Department's initial "indicated" finding was issued based on "credible evidence" in support of a report that plaintiff had sexually abused an 11-year-old girl. Plaintiff sought a hearing on the indicated finding and asked that the indicated report be expunged. A hearing was held before an administrative law judge (ALJ). The ALJ issued an opinion denying the expungement request. The Department adopted the ALJ's decision. Plaintiff filed his court action, and the trial court upheld the Department's decision. The appellate court reversed, holding that (1) plaintiff had a liberty interest in keeping his name off the State's suspected child abuser register; (2) the Department violated plaintiff's due process rights when it failed to comply with time limitations regarding hearings and final decisions found in Ill. Admin. Code ch. 89, § 336.220(a) (2001) and 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7.16 (2000); (3) the ALJ properly considered hearsay evidence and his findings were supported by the evidence; and (4) the fact that the mandated reporter did not testify at the hearing did not require expungement of the indicated finding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

People v. John J. (In re John Paul J.)


1-02-1205


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 865; 799 N.E.2d 769; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1185; 278 Ill. Dec. 904



September 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Rehearing denied by In re J.P.J., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1486 (Ill. App. Ct., Oct. 22, 2003)
Appeal denied by In re John Paul J., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 194 (Ill., Jan. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sandra R. Otaka, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents sought review of orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that their infant son was a neglected minor and which adjudicated him a ward of the court.


OVERVIEW: The son was taken into temporary custody shortly after his birth. Four older siblings were already in the State's custody due to the parents' problems. The father had drug problems, and the mother had a personality disorder that impaired her ability to parent. Both parents claimed to have been receiving help with their problems, but no actual evidence was presented to prove their contentions. A psychologist testified that without intensive psychotherapy, the mother would not be a good parenting candidate. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the failure to hold a temporary custody hearing within the time limit in 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-9(1) (2000) did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction in the matter but would only have required the son's release from custody on proper motion; (2) the parents waived their 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-14(d) (2000) "timely adjudication" argument; (3) the allegations of the State's petition reasonably informed the parents as to the nature of the neglect charge; and (4) the parents' past history, the psychological testimony offered, and the mother's failure to follow through with counseling, all supported the trial court's orders.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. McClain


No. 1-01-1936


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 1122; 799 N.E.2d 322; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1163; 278 Ill. Dec. 604



September 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied September 11, 2003. Released for Publication December 3, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. McClain, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2611 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CR 33433. Honorable Frank Zelezinski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a third jury trial, defendant was convicted of first degree murder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to an extended term of 80 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion for a 24-hour continuance to secure a witness because the witness would have exculpated defendant. The appellate court found that defense counsel made diligent efforts to call the witness, but declined to find any error since defendant failed to demonstrate that the witness's testimony would have been material to the case and thus, failed to prove prejudice. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him to an extended-term sentence because it improperly retroactively utilized a recently amended version of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-2 (2000). The appellate court concluded that defendant could be sentenced in accordance with the statutory scheme as long as the procedures utilized comported with Apprendi and because the amended version of § 5-8-2 only addressed procedural aspects for complying with Apprendi, there was nothing to prohibit its application. Finally, the appellate court disagreed with defendant that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11 1-3(c-5) (2000) was unconstitutional because it allowed the State to add elements of an offense by only giving written notification to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Moore


No. 2-02-0367


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 331; 797 N.E.2d 217; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1165; 277 Ill. Dec. 870



September 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 16, 2003. Released for Publication October 16, 2003.
Rehearing denied by People v. Moore, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1283 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Oct. 16, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Moore, 207 Ill. 2d 621, 807 N.E.2d 980, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 235, 283 Ill. Dec. 139 (2004)
Appeal denied by People v. Moore, 217 Ill. 2d 584, 844 N.E.2d 44, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 1632, 300 Ill. Dec. 372 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Moore v. Gaetz, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46735 (N.D. Ill., May 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 01--CF--2150. Honorable Mary S. Schostok, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9- 1(a)(1) (2000)). The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) imposed a 50-year sentence after concluding that defendant was eligible for a 25-year sentence enhancement based on his use of a firearm during the offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erroneously declined his tendered jury instructions on second-degree murder based on the provocation of mutual combat and on self-defense. The appellate court concluded that the totality of evidence indicated that defendant was the aggressor, he used excessive force under the circumstances, and he and the victim did not fight on equal terms. In addition, there was no evidence that defendant acted under an objectively reasonable belief that the threat presented required use of a handgun. Defendant also argued that the trial court's failure to consider the jury's request for transcripts was reversible error. The appellate court concluded that even if such were an error, it was harmless in light of defendant's objection at the time of the jury's request. Finally, the appellate court concluded that defendant failed to meet his burden of proving that he received an unconstitutional sentence when the trial court imposed the 25-year sentence enhancement mandated by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(d)(iii); the appellate court found no violation of the Proportionate Penalties Clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, or improper double enhancement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Burks


No. 1-01-4472


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


343 Ill. App. 3d 765; 799 N.E.2d 745; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1136; 278 Ill. Dec. 880

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 01 CR 14256. Honorable Ronald A. Himel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and sentenced him to seven years' imprisonment following a bench trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a police officer observed two separate drug transactions. The evidence showed that in each instance, a buyer approached defendant and handed him money. Defendant then pointed to another individual who proceeded down an alley, retrieved a bag from behind a garbage can, and handed the buyer something out of the bag. The bag was confiscated and small packets of cocaine were found inside. On appeal, defendant made several arguments including insufficient evidence, unconstitutional sentencing, and improper consideration of his ineffective assistance of counsel claims. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the evidence was sufficient to show defendant had constructive possession of the cocaine and that the totality of the circumstances showed an intent to deliver the drugs; (2) defendant failed to raise any colorable claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because he failed to show that he was prejudiced by any of his counsel's alleged deficiencies; and (3) defendant's sentence under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) as a Class X offender did not violate the Illinois constitution or federal decisional law.


OUTCOME: The court modified the mittimus to show the correct number of days defendant had served before he was sentenced, and as modified, affirmed both defendant's conviction and his sentence.

People v. Dent


NO. 5-02-0389


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 567; 797 N.E.2d 200; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1156; 277 Ill. Dec. 853



September 11, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 01-CF-2343. Honorable James Hackett, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/114-11, 114-12 (2000) in defendant's marijuana possession prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was confronted by seven to nine armed, uniformed police officers after he exited his vehicle and walked toward a house. The officers had gathered to take part in a "knock and talk" program meant to garner information that might be useful in drug investigations. While surrounded by the officers on three sides, defendant was asked if he had any drugs on him and he was also asked to consent to a search. The arresting officer testified that defendant consented to a search, which yielded fourteen small bags of what was believed to be cannabis. Defendant's vehicle was then searched, yielding two more bags of cannabis. Defendant asserted that he was illegally detained. The court agreed and affirmed. The State admitted that the officers had no probable cause to stop defendant with regard to any crime, thus the encounter was not a Terry stop. Under the totality of the circumstances, it was reasonable for defendant to believe he was being detained. As the detention was unlawful under the Fourth Amendment, defendant's consent to the search was ineffective. The evidence obtained as a result of the illegal detention was properly excluded as "fruit of the poisonous tree."


OUTCOME: The order granting the motion to suppress evidence was affirmed.

Harrisonville Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n


NO. 5-02-0199


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 517; 797 N.E.2d 183; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1157; 277 Ill. Dec. 836



September 11, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Harrisonville Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n, 207 Ill. 2d 601, 807 N.E.2d 974, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 13, 283 Ill. Dec. 133 (2004)
Affirmed by Harrisonville Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n, 212 Ill. 2d 237, 817 N.E.2d 479, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1020, 288 Ill. Dec. 121 (Ill., Sept. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an Order of the Illinois Commerce Commission. Nos. 00-0233 & 00-0335 Consolidated.
Harrisonville Tel. Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 639 (Ill. App. Ct., May 23, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a telephone association and several individual rural telephone companies, appealed an order of respondent Illinois Commerce Commission, which established a state universal service fund for small rural telephone companies pursuant to the Illinois Public Utilities Act, 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-101 et seq. (2000).


OVERVIEW: In establishing the universal fund, the Commission determined both an "affordable rate" for rural services and that the fund would apply only to primary access lines for homes and businesses. Petitioners sought a rehearing, which produced an order that changed the affordable rate by lowering it, but did not change the Commission's decision regarding lines that would be covered by the fund. The court first ruled that it had jurisdiction to hear the appeal under the Act because nothing in the Act required petitioners to seek a second rehearing on the issues and in fact, 220 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-113(a) (2000) limited petitioners to one rehearing. The court reversed the Commission's order regarding the lines to be covered by the fund. The state's fund was to mirror the federal universal support fund and 47 C.F.R. § 54.101(a)(1) (1998) did not limit the federal fund to primary access lines. The court affirmed the affordable rate set by the Commission. Setting the rate was within the Commission's power and the court was unwilling to find that the rate set by the Commission was not supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commission's order regarding funding for primary access lines only but affirmed the remainder of the Commission's order. The court remanded the case for further proceedings relative to the inclusion of all access lines in the funding amounts.

 

1500 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henry


No. 2-02-0089


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 133; 796 N.E.2d 718; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1114; 277 Ill. Dec. 632



September 4, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00--CF--2045. Honorable Kathryn E. Creswell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which entered judgment on a jury's verdict of guilty against defendant on a charge of reckless homicide and a charge of driving with a revoked license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the reckless homicide statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3 (2000), and the jury instructions based on the statute were unconstitutional because they contained mandatory irrebuttable presumptions that relieved the State of its burden to prove recklessness and intoxication beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. Section 9-3(b) did contain an unconstitutional presumption that being under the influence of alcohol or drugs was presumed to be evidence of a reckless act unless disproved by other evidence. However, the trial court had granted defendant's motion that the jury not be instructed on § 9-3(b) so no error occurred. Section 9-3(c)(1), which provided that a person was under the influence of alcohol for purposes of reckless homicide where the person's blood-alcohol level exceeded 0.08, did not require a jury to find a person guilty of reckless homicide based on that presumption. Thus, § 9-3(c)(1) was constitutional and its application was not effected by the status of § 9-3(b). Finally, it was not improper to give both Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions, Crim. No. 7.09X and 23.30 (4th ed.).


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions on both charges were affirmed.

 

1501 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. DeBord


No. 2-02-0226


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


344 Ill. App. 3d 321; 800 N.E.2d 809; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1112; 279 Ill. Dec. 521



September 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 31, 2003. As Corrected.
Rehearing denied by People v. DeBord, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1596 (Ill. App. Ct., Sept. 3, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. DeBord, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2592 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County. No. 00--CF--21. Honorable William A. Kelly, Judge, Presiding.
People v. DeBord, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 972 (Ill. App. Ct., July 29, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of involuntary manslaughter, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(a) (2000), of a victim less than 12 years old. At the sentencing hearing, the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County (Illinois) found that the victim was a family or household member and ruled that the offense was elevated from a Class 3 felony to a Class 2 felony. The trial court imposed a 10-year prison term and a $ 100 domestic violence fine.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that he could not be convicted of the involuntary manslaughter of a family or household member because it was not a lesser-included offense of first-degree murder. Specifically, defendant argued that his due process rights were violated because the charging instrument did not allege the family-or-household-member element and the jury did not find the element beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court concluded that in cases involving the conviction of a lesser-included offense, the family-or-household-member fact was an element of the offense of involuntary manslaughter, and the element had to be identified in an instrument charging the greater offense. The offense of involuntary manslaughter of a family or household member was not a lesser-included offense of first-degree murder as charged in the superceding indictment because the murder charge did not allege that the victim was a "family or household member" as defined by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/112A-3 (2000). Also, the State conceded that the trial court erred in ordering defendant's fine to be drawn from defendant's bond.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded for the entry of a new judgment of conviction pursuant to the jury's verdict.

People v. Grochocki


No. 3-02-0196


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


343 Ill. App. 3d 664; 796 N.E.2d 153; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1237; 277 Ill. Dec. 438



August 26, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 1, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit. Will County, Illinois. No. 00--CM--4047. Honorable Robert C. Lorz, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Grochocki, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1083 (Ill. App. Ct., Aug. 26, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), convicting defendant of sexual exploitation of a child in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-9.1(a)(1) (2000), sentencing defendant to 12 months of conditional discharge, and requiring defendant to register under the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq., required sex offenders to register with certain specified government officials, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/3 (2000). The Illinois Sex Offender and Child Murderer Community Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/101 et seq., required officials to disclose a sex offender's registration information to school boards, school principals, and child care facilities in the county where the offender resided, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/120(a) (1998). The information was available for public inspection at police departments and sheriff's offices. Amendments to the notification law under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/115(b) (2002) and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/120(c) (2002) provided for a website to post names and pictures of sex offenders. This did not violate defendant's right to privacy under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. Defendant's criminal record was already public, so he could not claim a privacy interest in it. The amendments did not violate the Proportionate Penalties Clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The dissemination of defendant's sex offender status was not a punishment or penalty.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Morales


No. 1-02-1566


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 815; 795 N.E.2d 1006; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1035; 277 Ill. Dec. 338



August 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 24, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of aggravated battery with a firearm and was sentenced to 11 years' imprisonment. Defendant subsequently filed a pro se postconviction petition to vacate his plea, which the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissed as frivolous and patently without merit. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in dismissing his petition because Ill. Pub. Act 86-980, which created the offense of aggravated battery with a firearm and under which defendant pled guilty, violated the single subject rule of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), and, therefore, his guilty plea was void. In affirming the trial court's dismissal of defendant's postconviction petition, the appellate court noted first that, contrary to defendant's argument, there was no requirement for courts to look beyond the face of the public act itself. In addition, defendant's contention that the provisions of an enactment must relate to each other was repeatedly rejected by the supreme court. Finally, the appellate court noted that the subject provisions did all relate to a single subject - crime, specifically, the prevention of same.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Baker


NO. 4-01-0597


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


341 Ill. App. 3d 1083; 794 N.E.2d 353; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1077; 276 Ill. Dec. 458



August 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. Nos. 01CF165, 99CF2047. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.
People v. Baker, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 532 (Ill. App. Ct., Apr. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's probation was revoked, a jury found him guilty of aggravated kidnapping, armed violence, and unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) sentenced him to, inter alia, 40 years in prison for aggravated kidnapping, which included an automatic 15-year firearm enhancement, and also resentenced defendant to 10 years in prison for attempt. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the 15-year enhancement for aggravated kidnapping violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. Defendant contended that the offenses of aggravated kidnapping and armed violence predicated on the offense of kidnapping while carrying a category I weapon had identical elements, but carried difference sentences. The appellate court held that the 15-year enhancement for aggravated kidnapping violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution and was unenforceable. Defendant also argued that the trial court considered an improper factor, the presence of a firearm, as an aggravating factor in sentencing him. As defendant failed to include this issue in his post-trial motion, the appellate court considered it under plain error review. The appellate court concluded that defendant's argument did not satisfy either requirement of the plain error rule. The appellate court noted that the trial court's comment that defendant had escalated his choice of weapons in that he armed himself with a firearm was not so egregious as to deprive defendant of a fair sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The 15-year enhancement for defendant's aggravated kidnapping conviction was vacated and the case was remanded with directions that the trial court issue an amended written judgment to reflect that defendant's sentence for aggravated kidnapping was 25 years. In all other respects the judgment was affirmed.

People v. Marin


No. 1-01-1080


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 716; 795 N.E.2d 953; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1024; 277 Ill. Dec. 285



August 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 24, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Marin, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2495 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CR 20536. Honorable Dennis A. Dernbach, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted at a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. The trial court sentenced defendant to 24 months of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers stopped defendant when they saw him carrying a gun while standing in a group of young men. The officers recovered the gun from where defendant had dropped it. Defendant waived his Miranda rights and gave a confession at the police station, which confession he recanted at trial. On appeal, defendant contended that the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6 (2002), was unconstitutional on the grounds that the statute required no culpable mental state and thereby punished innocent conduct, resulting in the contravention of the due process provisions of both the state and federal constitutions. Defendant further contended that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. On appeal, the court found that the statute, in requiring only a knowing mental state rather than criminal intent, bore a rational relationship to the statute's objective of protecting the general public and law enforcement from those who possessed loaded weapons in public places, and did not otherwise reach beyond its valid scope and purpose. Further, the evidence was not so improbable or unreasonable as to create a reasonable doubt of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Johns


NO. 4-02-0748


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


342 Ill. App. 3d 297; 795 N.E.2d 433; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1027; 277 Ill. Dec. 66



August 8, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 5, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Johns, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2482 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Clark County. No. 02CF12. Honorable Tracy W. Resch, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a stipulated bench trial, the Circuit Court of Clark County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of possession of a controlled substance. The court sentenced her to 24 months' probation. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred by denying her motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: At the time of her arrest, defendant was on probation as the result of having been bound guilty of two misdemeanor driving related charges. The probation order provided that defendant was to submit to warrantless searches of among other things, her residence. The police conducted a random "probation check" of defendant's home and in a dresser drawer in her room, they found three used pipes, one of which contained cocaine residue. Defendant was not home at the time of the search but her teenage son consented to the search. Defendant's motion to suppress was based on the argument that the search was not based upon suspicion or evidence of illegal activity. The court reversed, holding that (1) the State failed to establish that defendant's son possessed the common authority over the dresser such that he could give consent to a search of the dresser; (2) the Fourth Amendment required all searches to be reasonable and the State failed to present any evidence on the reasonableness issue; (3) defendant had a diminished, but not extinguished, expectation of privacy in her home; and (4) reasonable suspicion of illegal activity was required to justify the search of the dresser.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

In re Marriage of Sullivan


No. 2-03-0080


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


342 Ill. App. 3d 560; 795 N.E.2d 392; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1012; 277 Ill. Dec. 25



August 6, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94--D--79. Honorable Brian R. McKillip, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that dismissed for lack of jurisdiction his petition (submitted in the course of petitioner mother's contempt proceeding relating to child support) to modify the parties' custody arrangement to permit the father's family to exercise visitation according to the father's schedule while the father was on active military duty.


OVERVIEW: The father exercised regular visitation with the parties' child. When he was called to active military duty, he sought a modification of the custody order to allow his immediate family members to exercise visitation instead, arguing that the mother would otherwise prevent such contact. The appellate court held that the trial court had erred in holding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the petition. When 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/607(b)(1) (2000), the grandparent visitation statute, had been held unconstitutional, Illinois law returned to the common law rule that allowed a court to award visitation to family members when special circumstances were present. In harmony with the policy of the Soldiers' and Sailors' Civil Relief Act of 1940, 50 U.S.C.S. app. § 501 et seq., of empowering civil courts to remove inhibitions that might interfere with a soldier's full devotion to his task, setting the father's mind at rest about his child appeared to present a special circumstance, empowering the trial court to proceed with a best interests analysis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal and remanded for additional proceedings.

People v. Ruiz


No. 1-00-2509


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 750; 795 N.E.2d 912; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1003; 277 Ill. Dec. 244



August 5, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 24, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Ruiz, 206 Ill. 2d 640, 806 N.E.2d 1071, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2460, 282 Ill. Dec. 483 (2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Ruiz, 2014 IL App (1st) 112993-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 440 (2014)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Ruiz v. Butler, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 106175 (N.D. Ill., Aug. 12, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 31306. Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on charges of first-degree murder, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-1(a)(2) (1998), and aggravated discharge of a firearm, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.2(a)(2) (1998). Under the Truth in Sentencing Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(i) (1998), he was required to serve the entire 40-year sentence he received on the murder charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges stemmed from a drive-by shooting in which defendant shot at and killed a father who was holding his three-year-old son. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on felony murder, that there was insufficient evidence to support the firearm charge, that the trial court erred in not compelling the presence of a defense witness, and that § 3-6-3(a)(2)(i) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that (1) the firearms charge, which was based on the discharge of a firearm in the direction of the child and not his father, provided the appropriate predicate for the felony murder charge and the jury instruction was proper; (2) where three theories on first-degree murder were presented to the jury, which returned a general verdict, any error in instructing on felony murder was harmless; (3) the evidence was overwhelming that defendant knew the father was in the area where he shot his firearm and was sufficient to support the firearm conviction even if defendant was not specifically aware of the child's presence; (4) no error was committed regarding the defense witness; and (5) § 3-6-3(a)(2)(i) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Clifton


1-98-2126 and 1-98-2384 (consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 696; 795 N.E.2d 887; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 980; 277 Ill. Dec. 219



August 4, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 11, 2003. Released for Publication September 24, 2003.
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Clifton, 365 Ill. App. 3d 1097, 927 N.E.2d 332, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 2670 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Clifton v. Bartley, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 67309 (N.D. Ill., May 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Marcus Salone, Judge Presiding.
People v. Clifton, 321 Ill. App. 3d 707, 750 N.E.2d 686, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 305, 255 Ill. Dec. 769 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's prior opinion was replaced. Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and case was remanded, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two co-defendants appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Following simultaneous but severed jury trials, both co-defendants were found guilty of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and aggravated battery with a firearm. Both defendants received consecutive sentences for the murder and attempted murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged the admission of gang-related testimony and alleged a speedy trial violation, ineffective counsel, and insufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed in part and remanded in part. Testimony by a gang crimes specialist was properly admitted because it qualified as an expert opinion; the specialist drew on a variety of sources, including talks with gang members, information from confidential informants, and contacts with outside agencies. The testimony was relevant to show the State's gang-related motive; without the gang-related evidence, the crimes would have been inexplicable. Even if the testimony were inadmissible, any error was harmless because of the overwhelming, nonhearsay evidence against the first defendant, including his identification by the surviving victim. The second defendant was not denied a speedy trial because many of the disputed delays were attributable to the defense, and the cumulative evidence was more than enough to establish the second defendant's accountability for any of the acts attributed to the first defendant. The court remanded for clarification of the extended-term sentences received by the first defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences of the second defendant, and the court affirmed the convictions of the first defendant and remanded for the trial court to clarify what factors were used in imposing his extended-term sentences.

People v. Youngerman


No. 1-01-3723


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 518; 800 N.E.2d 799; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 923; 279 Ill. Dec. 511



July 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 2003.
Appeal after remand at People v. Youngerman, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 1037 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 88 CR 6136. Honorable Timothy J. Chambers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and case was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from two orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which denied his motion for discharge or conditional release from the custody of the Illinois Department of Human Services, and granted the State's motion to amend his "Thiem date." Defendant was committed to the Department after being found not guilty by reason of insanity on charges of attempted murder, aggravated battery and armed violence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's Thiem date was modified after he absented himself from the treatment facility for nearly four years. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred in extending his Thiem date because 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-2-4(b) (2002) provided no basis for amending a Thiem date, and the State's motion, filed seven years after defendant's return to the facility, should have been denied. The resolution of defendant's claim depended upon whether a defendant's "period of confinement" included those period during which he had eloped or absented himself from the treatment facility without authorization. The appellate court held that the period of defendant's unauthorized absence, or elopement, from the facility did not constitute a period of commitment. Accordingly, the trial court was authorized to amend defendant's Thiem date. Doing so did not change the "maximum period of commitment" authorized by the statute. Defendant also argued that the State's motion should have been denied under the doctrine of laches. The appellate court noted that even if the State's delay amounted to a lack of diligence, defendant failed to show how he was prejudiced by the State's request.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order granting the State's motion to amend defendant's Thiem date was affirmed, but the order establishing the date was reversed. The trial court's order denying defendant's petition for discharge or conditional release was reversed. The case was remanded with directions for the trial court the trial court to set defendant's Thiem date as October 2, 2006 and order an independent examination and conduct a hearing.
