People v. Lucas


No. 1-99-2623


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 58; 795 N.E.2d 767; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 905; 277 Ill. Dec. 99



July 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Lucas, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2412 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lucas, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 342 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 26, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's prior opinion was vacated and different results were reached on rehearing. Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of attempted first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated kidnapping. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) using extended-term and consecutive-sentence statutes, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(2), 5-8-4(a) (1998), sentenced defendant to a total of 120 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the statutes authorizing the trial court to impose extended term and consecutive sentences, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(2) (1998), and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(a) (1998), were unconstitutional in light of Apprendi. The State argued that any error made in imposing the extended-term sentences was not plain error because defendant could not show prejudice, and the sentences must be affirmed. The appellate court agreed with the State, noting that Apprendi did not apply to consecutive sentences. In addition, the evidence presented to the trial court overwhelmingly supported a finding that the crime was committed in a brutal and heinous manner, indicative of wanton cruelty. Defendant also contended § 5-8-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, codified at 730 ILCS 5/5-8-4(a) (1998), was unconstitutional. Since none of defendant's separate sentences exceeded the maximum sentence for each offense, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the consecutive sentences imposed pursuant to § 5-8-4(a) were unconstitutional under Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Rosenberg


No. 3-02-0759


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


341 Ill. App. 3d 893; 793 N.E.2d 939; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 886; 276 Ill. Dec. 180



July 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.
Appeal granted by People v. Rosenberg, 206 Ill. 2d 639, 806 N.E.2d 1071, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2284, 282 Ill. Dec. 483 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Rosenberg, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1671 (Ill., Nov. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit LaSalle County, Illinois. No. 00-CF-172. Honorable H. Chris Ryan, Jr., Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with controlled substance trafficking. He was convicted in the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit LaSalle County, Illinois after his motion to suppress evidence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant hired an accomplice to drive a rental car containing ketamine cross-country. The accomplice was stopped in Illinois and consented to a search of the car. The accomplice was arrested and began cooperating with the authorities. He was granted use immunity before the grand jury. Defendant wanted the accomplice to testify at defendant's hearing to suppress the search, but the State refused to grant the accomplice immunity for that hearing. The State then granted the accomplice use immunity during defendant's trial, and defendant was convicted. Defendant's appeal asserted several errors but the main assertion was that he was denied due process by the State refusal to grant the accomplice immunity to testify at the suppression hearing. The court agreed. The State's refusal to grant immunity for the suppression hearing was a discriminatory application of its powers that frustrated defendant's attempt to garner necessary facts that could have established defendant's standing to challenge the search. The State's actions impermissibly distorted the fact finding process, and the fact that the motion to suppress could have been renewed at trial did not cure the due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order on the motion to suppress and remanded for a new hearing on the motion. The court retained jurisdiction to determine the remaining issues presented in the appeal in the event the State prevailed on the motion to suppress.

De Bates v. Bates


Nos. 2-02-0488, 2-02-0516, 2-02-0597 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


342 Ill. App. 3d 207; 794 N.E.2d 868; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 879; 276 Ill. Dec. 618



July 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 26, 2003.
Affirmed by In re Marriage of De Bates, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1619 (Ill., Oct. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99--D--958. Honorable John W. Demling and James J. Konetski, Judges, Presiding.
In re Marriage DeBates, 309 Ill. App. 3d 1087, 764 N.E.2d 606, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1187, 261 Ill. Dec. 991 (Ill. App. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed from that portion of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) that granted respondent father's request for a change of custody and transferred residential custody of the parties' child to him. The father cross-appealed from that part of the judgment that denied his petition to terminate unallocated family support.


OVERVIEW: The father and mother had joint legal custody, but the child resided with her mother. The father sought a change in residential custody based on the mother's persistent efforts to interfere with the child's relationship with him. The trial court appointed a child representative pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. OUTCOME: The court granted and denied various parts of the mother's motion to strike certain matters in one of the father's briefs, denied the father's motion to dismiss the mother's appeal, and proceeded to affirm the trial court's judgment on the main issues of custody and family support.

People v. McGee


No. 1-02-2637


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


341 Ill. App. 3d 1029; 794 N.E.2d 855; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 818; 276 Ill. Dec. 605



June 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. McGee, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2188 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of the six weapons charges in the information and, because defendant had a felony record, sentenced him to a mandatory Class X term of seven years' imprisonment on one of them. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (UUW) statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6 (2000), was unconstitutional because it violated the proportionate penalty provision of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. Defendant argued that aggravated UUW and misdemeanor UUW were identical offenses given different sentences. The appellate court concluded that there was not disproportionality. The appellate court found aggravated UUW required a finding of at least one of seven aggravating factors, none of which were required under the misdemeanor statute; thus, the felony charge applied to more serious conduct. Defendant also contended that the aggravated UUW provision he was convicted of violated substantive due process. The appellate court found that the purpose of the aggravated UUW statute was rationally related to a legitimate goal, making communities in Illinois safer and more secure. The appellate court concluded that each of the aggravating factors was a circumstance that belied indecent conduct.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Johnson


No. 1-02-0969


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


341 Ill. App. 3d 583; 793 N.E.2d 774; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 823; 276 Ill. Dec. 15



June 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 13615. Honorable William G. Lacy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial conducted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), on charges of aggravated domestic battery and aggravated battery. The charges were merged and defendant was sentenced to four years in prison. He appealed his conviction asserting that the domestic violence statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3.2(a), 3.3(a) (2000), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his victim had both been drinking when they were involved in a dispute wherein the victim smashed the windshield of defendant's vehicle and defendant then "ran over" the victim. Testimony from both defendant and his victim indicated that they had been in a dating relationship for at least one year prior to the incident and that the couple intended on living together after defendant's release. On appeal, defendant contended that the domestic battery statute was unconstitutionally vague due to the inclusion of persons in a "dating or engagement relationship" in its definition of "family or household members." The court disagreed and affirmed. Neither 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12-3.2(a) nor § 12-3.3(a) dealt with First Amendment rights. Therefore, defendant only had standing to contest their constitutionality as the statutes were applied to him in his case. Defendant's own testimony established the type of "dating relationship" that brought defendant within the definition of a "family or household member," providing defendant a reasonable opportunity to determine that his conduct was prohibited under the domestic violence statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Canel v. Topinka


No. 1-01-2069


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 65; 793 N.E.2d 845; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 844; 276 Ill. Dec. 86



June 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.
Appeal granted by Canel v. Topinka, 206 Ill. 2d 619, 806 N.E.2d 1064, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2307, 282 Ill. Dec. 476 (2003)
Affirmed by Canel v. Topinka, 212 Ill. 2d 311, 818 N.E.2d 311, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1036, 288 Ill. Dec. 623 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CH 13279. Honorable Stephen Schiller, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of defendants, the Illinois State Treasurer, and the Director of the Unclaimed Property Division of the office of the Treasurer of the State of Illinois, to dismiss the property owner's class action complaint. The complaint asserted that 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 1025/15 (2000) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed his action after the State retained dividends on stock it held for the owner as abandoned property. Section 15 was part of the Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act, 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 1025/1 et seq. (2000). Under 765 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 1025/15 (2000), the State was allowed to keep income or other increments that accrued on property while in the State's possession. The State claimed a right to such income based on its "escheat" powers. Although the constitutionality issue was not reached by the trial court, the court reviewed the question of law de novo. The court reversed. Section 15 was not an "escheat" law, and the State could not rely on its escheat powers as a basis for retaining the dividends. Both the stock and dividends remained the private property of the owner. A "taking" occurred for Fifth and Fourteenth Amendment purposes when the Treasurer kept the dividends pursuant to § 15. But, if no compensation was due, there was no constitutional violation. On the record, the issue of whether the owner was due any compensation could not be resolved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case for determination of the issue of compensation in accordance with the views expressed in the opinion.

People v. J.R. (In re J.R.)


No. 1-01-2318


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


341 Ill. App. 3d 784; 793 N.E.2d 687; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 831; 275 Ill. Dec. 916



June 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard F. Walsh, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile appealed from a Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) order that he register as a sex offender and submit a blood sample. He challenged the application of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 150/1 et seq. (2000), the Illinois Sex Offender and Child Murderer Notification Law, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 152/101 et seq. (2000), and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-4-3 (2000) to juveniles.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile, a teen-ager, was adjudicated delinquent for nonconsensual sexual activity with a 12-year-old girl. He argued that application of the registration and notification statutes to him violated his substantive and procedural due process rights, but the appellate court found no constitutional violations. The registration provisions were rationally related to the critical public interest in avoiding sex offender recidivism, and although juvenile offenders fell within the notification provisions, there were appropriately stringent limitations on dissemination of information about juveniles. The juvenile also challenged the fact that a blood sample submitted upon adjudication as a sex offender could never be expunged, but the appellate court held that such an argument would be premature until the juvenile actually reached a point at which he would otherwise be eligible for expungement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

People ex rel. Devine v. Tiara W. (In re Tiona W.)

OVERVIEW: On October 1, 2001, the father was served with a copy of a petition for adjudication of wardship and a summons via registered mail while in jail. On January 8, 2002, the father appeared in court. On that date, the mother appeared and was personally served with the petition for adjudication of wardship. The case was continued several times until May 8, 2002. On May 3, 2002, the father filed a motion to dismiss the petition for adjudication of wardship pursuant to former 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. People v. Strickland


No. 3-01-0775


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


342 Ill. App. 3d 566; 795 N.E.2d 793; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1019; 277 Ill. Dec. 125


February 24, 2003, Submitted  
June 25, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified August 6, 2003. Released for Publication September 12, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Strickland, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2423 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 99-CF-790. Honorable Clark E. Erickson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was an appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois). Defendant was convicted of bringing contraband into a penal institution and aiding escape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was affirmed where he was properly convicted, under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/31A-1.1, for bringing contraband into a prison and aiding escape. Defendant, by acquiring a gun, repackaging it, and giving it to a correctional officer, played a key role in the delivery of the gun to the prison. Since the statute prohibited defendant's actions, defendant's vagueness claim failed. The statute was not unconstitutional. As to the contraband charge, the defendant's guilt was clear and convincing. The inclusion of the improper accountability instruction was harmless error. As the defendant was accountable for his accomplices' actions and their actions aided a convict's escape, defendant was also guilty of aiding the escape. The accountability instruction was properly given under that circumstance. The evidence established guilt. Defendant was not convicted in violation of the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). Although 1984 Ill. Laws 1041 may have violated the single subject clause, the passage of 1986 Ill. Laws 866 remedied any constitutional infirmity. As defendant's conduct occurred in 1999, he was unaffected by the 1984 act.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

Evans v. Page


NO. 5-02-0126


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


341 Ill. App. 3d 486; 792 N.E.2d 805; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 759; 275 Ill. Dec. 330



June 18, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Evans v. Page, 206 Ill. 2d 620, 806 N.E.2d 1065, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2443, 282 Ill. Dec. 477 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County. No. 98-MR-102. Honorable William A. Schuwerk, Jr., Judge, presiding.
Evans v. Page, 324 Ill. App. 3d 241, 755 N.E.2d 105, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 638, 258 Ill. Dec. 24 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) dismissing the inmate's action against defendant Warden of the Menard Correctional Center, alleging violation of Title II of the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990 (Title II), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12131 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, who was a paraplegic, was a prisoner at a state correctional facility. The inmate alleged that he was denied transportation to and from court in a wheelchair-accessible vehicle, was denied wheelchair-accessible recreation and exercise, and was denied wheelchair access to the health care unit and library. The warden filed a motion to dismiss pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-619 (2000) on the ground that the inmate's claim was barred by sovereign immunity. The appellate court found that sovereign immunity barred the inmate's Title II claim. Illinois never consented to be sued in a circuit court by prisoners based on Title II violations. Almost every federal circuit court held that Title II did not constitute a valid abrogation of state sovereign immunity under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, because Congress had not identified a history and pattern of unconstitutional discrimination by the states against the disabled.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Brewer v. Bd. of Trs.


NO. 4-02-0885


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 1074; 791 N.E.2d 657; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 765; 274 Ill. Dec. 565



June 17, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 18, 2003.
Appeal denied by Brewer v. Bd. of Trs., 205 Ill. 2d 576, 803 N.E.2d 479, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2153, 281 Ill. Dec. 75 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brewer v. Bd. of Trs., 541 U.S. 987, 124 S. Ct. 2015, 158 L. Ed. 2d 491, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2761 (2004)
Related proceeding at Brewer v. Bd. of Trs. of the Univ. of Ill., 407 F. Supp. 2d 946, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 38056 (C.D. Ill., Dec. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 02L128. Honorable John R. DeLaMar, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff research assistant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) which dismissed his complaint alleging violations of federal antidiscrimination statutes filed against defendants, the Board of Trustees of the University of Illinois and four employees of the Board in their official and individual capacities.


OVERVIEW: The assistant alleged that he was an African-American with a learning disability. He was fired from his job as a research assistant and his enrollment in a master's-degree program was terminated. He claimed race discrimination, disability discrimination, and equal protection violations. The trial court dismissed based on sovereign immunity and lack of subject-matter jurisdiction. The court affirmed. While the Illinois Constitution of 1970 abolished sovereign immunity, the state legislature reinstated it with two narrow qualifications that did not apply to the assistant's case. Subject-matter jurisdiction over human rights violations similar to those asserted by the assistant was vested in the Illinois Human Rights Commission under 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8-111(C) (2000). As the state courts did not have jurisdiction over state discrimination claims, they had no jurisdiction over the assistant's federal claims. The fact that there was a presumption of concurrent jurisdiction with federal courts for federal civil rights violations could not overcome the specific limitation on circuit courts' jurisdiction over such matters.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Askew


1-01-2920


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


341 Ill. App. 3d 548; 793 N.E.2d 56; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 749; 275 Ill. Dec. 576



June 16, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 18, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Askew, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1853 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 01 CR 7090. Honorable Evelyn B. Clay, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of possession of a controlled substance. At the sentencing hearing, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to an extended-term sentence of four years in prison, based on defendant's prior convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly imposed an extended term sentence based on his prior convictions, because: (1) the trial court did not find the existence of his prior convictions beyond a reasonable doubt, as required by 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-2(a) (2000) of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections, and (2) the extended-term sentencing provision found in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2001) was unconstitutional under Apprendi because it did not require that his prior convictions be pled in the charging instrument or proven at trial. After examining the legislative history of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-2(a) (2000), the appellate court concluded that the legislature intended to include language exempting prior convictions from the proof beyond a reasonable doubt requirement. Thus, § 5-8-2(a) should have been read to include such an exception. Finally, the appellate court declined to hold 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (2001) unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Burdunice


No. 3-01-0776


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 986; 791 N.E.2d 1148; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 656; 274 Ill. Dec. 737



May 29, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 22, 2003.
Affirmed by People v. Burdunice, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 679 (Ill., May 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--788. Honorable Clark E. Erickson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois), convicting her of supplying electronic contraband to an inmate; defendant claimed that the act creating the offense violated the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a correctional officer for a sheriff's department, delivered cellular telephone batteries and a sealed package to an inmate. The package contained a handgun that was used by another inmate to shoot another correctional officer while escaping. The public act at issue, 1996 Ill. Laws 688, was titled "An act in relation to criminal law" and consisted of five sections amending various statutes including the statute under which defendant was convicted: 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/31A-1.2(c)(1), (4)(xi) (1998). Because one section of the public act concerned an amendment to a civil statute, the public act violated the single subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). Without curative legislation that facially exhibited the legislature's intent to cure the single subject violation, the statute under which defendant was convicted was void ab initio.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

People ex rel. Shockley v. Hoyle


No. 2-02-0795


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


338 Ill. App. 3d 1046; 789 N.E.2d 1282; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 687; 273 Ill. Dec. 850



May 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 19, 2003. Rehearing Denied June 19, 2003.
Rehearing denied by People ex rel. Shockley v. Hoyle, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 771 (Ill. App. Ct., June 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. No. 99--F--50. Honorable Michael T. Mallon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Illinois Department of Public Aid (State) filed a petition in the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) on behalf of plaintiff mother seeking a judicial determination that defendant putative father was the father of the mother's child, and an order to provide child support. The trial court granted the State's summary judgment motion and ordered the father to provide support. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the subject child was born, the mother named another as the child's father on the child's birth certificate. The father claimed the law of California, where the child was born, established the named individual as the child's father, as he must have signed a voluntary paternity declaration to appear on the birth certificate, and the trial court had to give this full faith and credit. The appellate court held there was no evidence of a declaration of paternity signed or filed with California authorities. The statutes defendant relied on were not in effect when the child was born. Under the law in effect then, an alleged father did not have to sign a declaration of paternity to be listed on a birth certificate, and the person named on the certificate could not be presumed to be the child's father. Under the circumstances, defendant was not estopped to deny the person she named on the birth certificate was the child's father, as it was not presumed he was the father, the mother consistently said the father was the child's parent, a blood test found the father's paternity was likely, and the father threatened to take custody of the child if the mother told anyone he was the father.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1525 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grant


No. 1-01-1134


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


339 Ill. App. 3d 792; 791 N.E.2d 100; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 633; 274 Ill. Dec. 304



May 22, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 10, 2003.
Rehearing denied by People v. Grant, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 917 (Ill. App. Ct., June 19, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Grant, 205 Ill. 2d 608, 803 N.E.2d 490, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2167, 281 Ill. Dec. 86 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James M. Schreier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1)(3)(A) (2000), and sentenced him to one year of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to prove that he had knowledge that the weapon was in the vehicle. The appellate court's review revealed that the State presented sufficient evidence to establish that defendant had constructive possession of the weapon. Defendant next asserted that counsel was ineffective when he failed to call a codefendant to testify that defendant did not know that the gun was in the vehicle, and that had counsel done so the result of the proceedings would have been different. The appellate court found no prejudice as a result of such failure, since the officer's testimony tended to show defendant knew the gun was in the car; thus, defendant failed to show how counsel's strategic decision prejudiced his case. Finally, defendant contended that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/24-1.6(a)(1)(3)(A) (2000) violated state and federal substantive due process guarantees because it required only a mental state of knowing, without further requiring a culpable mental state. The appellate court concluded that § 24-1.6(a)(1)(3)(A) was reasonably designed to achieve its purpose of protecting officers and the public against persons carrying loaded weapons in their vehicle.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1526 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Natural Res. v. Brauer


No. 3-02-0098


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 723; 791 N.E.2d 120; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 640; 274 Ill. Dec. 324



May 22, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 91-ED-1 and 92-ED-2. Consolidated under 99-ED-1. Honorable Ludwig J. Kuhar, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State initiated condemnation proceedings in the 12th Judicial Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), during which appellant property owners sold easements over the subject property. The State moved for a setoff against the condemnation award for amounts the owners received from the sale of these easements. The trial court granted the motion, and the owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed the trial court had no jurisdiction to grant the State's motion, as it modified the condemnation judgment and was filed more than 30 days after that judgment. The appellate court held the State's motion was timely filed before the judgment was filed. No law showed the State's right to its requested setoff. As the State was trying to reduce the jury's award, it had the burden of proving a decrease in the land's value due to the easement sales, and did not meet this burden. Nor did it show the existence of the easements was relevant to the property's valuation. The trial court improperly granted the setoff. It was not shown that the property's value, which was the basis of the condemnation award, decreased by the amount the owners received from the sale of the easements. The plain language of 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-121 (2002) measured the owners' compensation in terms of the land's value. A rule giving the State superior rights to those of the easement purchasers described the relationship between the State and the purchasers and did not concern the relationship between the State and the owners.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

Taylor v. Cowan


NO. 5-01-0670


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 406; 790 N.E.2d 897; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 684; 274 Ill. Dec. 124



May 22, 2003, Decided  
May 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Taylor v. Cowan, 205 Ill. 2d 649, 803 N.E.2d 502, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2073, 281 Ill. Dec. 98 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County. No. 00-MR-113. Honorable William A. Schuwerk, Jr., Judge, presiding.
People v. Taylor, 164 Ill. App. 3d 938, 518 N.E.2d 409, 1987 Ill. App. LEXIS 3671, 115 Ill. Dec. 884 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1987)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed an action against respondent warden, seeking a writ of habeas corpus ordering his release from the Illinois Department of Corrections. The Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) dismissed the inmate's action, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: An inmate was convicted of murder and robbery in 1979, and he was sentenced to death. However, the state supreme court reversed the robbery conviction, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the case for resentencing. On remand, the trial court determined that although the inmate was not charged with burglary, the evidence presented at trial was sufficient to prove burglary, and the court used that as an aggravating circumstance to impose a sentence of life imprisonment, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1) (1979) (now 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(b) (2000)). After the United States Supreme Court issued is Apprendi decision, the inmate filed a habeas corpus action, arguing that he was resentenced in violation of principals announced in Apprendi. The appellate court held that (1) because evidence of the burglary which the trial court used as an aggravating factor to sentence the inmate to life imprisonment was presented to the court as the trier of fact and proven beyond a reasonable doubt, the court did not violate Apprendi by using that information; and (2) the inmate did not meet the requirements for release.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Dupree


No. 1-98-3931


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


339 Ill. App. 3d 512; 793 N.E.2d 31; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 600; 275 Ill. Dec. 551



May 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 10, 2003.
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Dupree v. Mote, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11034 (N.D. Ill., June 26, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. DuPree, 205 Ill. 2d 603, 803 N.E.2d 488, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2099, 281 Ill. Dec. 84 (2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Dupree, 384 Ill. App. 3d 1086, 973 N.E.2d 1087, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 4515, 362 Ill. Dec. 691 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Dupree, 394 Ill. App. 3d 1101, 985 N.E.2d 1079, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 5367, 369 Ill. Dec. 93 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Dupree, 2012 IL App (1st) 100120-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1582 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 4800. Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: State's motion to dismiss was denied and defendant-appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, in absentia, in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of theft by deception and was sentenced, in absentia, to 10 years in prison. He appealed his conviction and his sentence. The State moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was told he could be tried and sentenced in absentia if he did not appear. The appellate court held defendant, though absent, had a right to a fair trial free from procedural defects, and 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-4.1(g) (2000), allowing him to collaterally attack his conviction, did not conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 606, as the attack was a collateral proceeding, but the grant of an appeal was not required unless procedural issues implicating fundamental fairness and due process were raised. The jury's consideration of other crimes evidence was harmless. Lay witnesses could give opinions, the trial court did not have to instruct the jury not to consider defendant's absence, and the State could refer to it. Sufficient evidence supported defendant's theft by deception conviction, as he posed as an attorney, accepted money as a retainer and to bond a person out of jail, and neither performed services for nor returned the money. His sentence was not excessive, given earlier convictions. A disparity between a returned fugitive and a defendant present for trial was based on a policy decision to give trials in absentia heightened scrutiny.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, and the State's motion to dismiss was denied.

People v. O'Quinn


NO. 5-01-0666


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 347; 791 N.E.2d 1066; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 630; 274 Ill. Dec. 655



May 19, 2003, Decided  
May 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. O'Quinn, 205 Ill. 2d 624, 803 N.E.2d 494, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2020, 281 Ill. Dec. 90 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by O'Quinn v. Illinois, 541 U.S. 943, 124 S. Ct. 1669, 158 L. Ed. 2d 368, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2142 (2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. O'Quinn, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 221 (2011)
Habeas corpus proceeding at O'Quinn v. Atchison, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121629 (S.D. Ill., Aug. 27, 2012)
Petition denied by, Motion granted by People v. O'Quinn, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2937, 2012 IL App (5th) 100583U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 97-CF-2278. Honorable Charles V. Romani, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to an extended term of 70 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to a speedy trial when defense counsel continued his trial for more than three and one-half years over his express objection. The appellate court concluded that defendant was not denied his constitutional right to a speedy trial, noting that the delays were all caused by defense counsel and defendant failed to show that the length of time caused his defense to be impaired. Defendant next argued that he was denied his right to a fair trial when the judge removed him from the courtroom. The appellate court found no error since defendant was not removed until just prior to closing arguments and his interests were adequately represented by counsel; thus, defendant was present at all material stages. Finally, defendant argued that the use of a special interrogatory to determine the victim's age deprived him of due process and violated the doctrines of separation of powers and ex post facto application of laws. The appellate court concluded that the trial court was acting within its express authority when it allowed the use of the special interrogatory and that the interrogatory caused no harm or prejudice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Beck


NO. 5-01-0722


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 413; 790 N.E.2d 429; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 583; 274 Ill. Dec. 53



May 14, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. Nos. 87-CF-150 & 00-MR-235. Honorable James K. Donovan, Judge, presiding.
People v. Beck, 190 Ill. App. 3d 748, 546 N.E.2d 1127, 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1687, 138 Ill. Dec. 72 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 1989)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, St. Clair County (Illinois), denied petitioner's motion to reconsider his sentence and found that Apprendi did not apply to the juvenile transfer proceedings used to transfer his case from juvenile court to adult criminal court, where the trial court later imposed six consecutive 20-year terms in prison after he pled guilty to six armed violence counts. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A petition alleging that petitioner was a delinquent minor was filed in the trial court. The petition alleged that petitioner had committed various violent crimes. The prosecution of the case was later transferred from juvenile court to adult criminal court pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(3)(a) (1985) (now codified at 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-130). Petitioner later pled guilty and was sentenced to six consecutive 20-year terms in prison. Several years later, petitioner filed a petition alleging that the consecutive sentences imposed by the court violated Apprendi. His petition was denied. Petitioner then filed a motion to reconsider alleging that Ill. Rev. Stat. Stat. para. 702-7(3)(a) (1985) was unconstitutional under Apprendi. After the trial court denied the motion by finding that Apprendi did not apply to juvenile transfer proceedings, petitioner appealed. The appellate court found that the statute was not unconstitutional because Apprendi applied only to statutes that were adjudicatory and not statutes, such as the one used to transfer petitioner's case, which were dispositional in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Traynoff (In re Traynoff)


No. 2-01-0880


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 6, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Traynoff (In re Det. of Traynoff), 206 Ill. 2d 622, 806 N.E.2d 1066, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2329, 282 Ill. Dec. 478 (2003)
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Traynoff (In re Traynoff), 214 Ill. 2d 533, 824 N.E.2d 277, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 329, 291 Ill. Dec. 701 (Ill., 2005)
On remand at, Substituted opinion at People v. Traynoff (In re Traynoff), 358 Ill. App. 3d 430, 831 N.E.2d 709, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 638, 294 Ill. Dec. 759 (Ill. App. Ct., June 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 98--MR--456. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order was affirmed, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition to commit defendant pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/40 (1998) of the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (1998). After defendant refused to participate in the evaluation process, the State moved to compel his submission. The motion was granted. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) found defendant to be a sexually violent person. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Act was unconstitutional because it was contrary to the due process standard established in Crane in that it allowed the civil commitment of a person as sexually violent without a finding that the person lacked control over his or her behavior. The appellate court found the Act constitutional as applied to defendant since the trial court made an explicit finding that defendant was not able to control his sexually violent behavior. The trial court also found sufficient evidence to support that finding. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred when it ordered him to submit to an evaluation by the department of human services. The appellate court found that plain error occurred. The appellate court concluded that defendant satisfied his burden of showing that he was prejudiced by the experts' testimony predicated upon certain tests or tools. All three experts relied, in part, on the actuarial tools to predict defendant's likelihood of reoffense. However, on the basis of the record, it was unclear whether these tools were still in the experimental stages or whether their validity had been established.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court compelling defendant to submit to an evaluation was affirmed and the cause was remanded with directions to conduct a hearing to determine the admissibility of the actuarial tools and for further proceedings.

Boxdorfer v. DaimlerChrysler Corp.


NO. 5-01-0273


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 335; 790 N.E.2d 391; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 553; 274 Ill. Dec. 15



May 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Boxdorfer v. Daimlerchrysler Corp., 396 F. Supp. 2d 946, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33076 (C.D. Ill., Oct. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 00-L-492. Honorable Phillip J. Kardis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order was reversed and order transferring cause to Sangamon County was entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car buyers filed a complaint against defendant automobile corporation, alleging common law fraud and consumer fraud. The corporation filed a motion to transfer venue. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) issued an order denying the defendant's motion to transfer venue. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The buyers complained that the paint on vehicles made by the corporation was defective in that it would delaminate and that the corporation failed to disclose that to the consuming public. The appellate court held that venue was not proper under the residence prong or the transaction prong. The facts did not support the residence prong, as the corporation did not design, manufacture, or produce its products in Madison County, and the corporation maintained no offices there. Although the corporation sold its vehicles to dealers from Madison County, those sales were conducted and completed in Michigan, and the corporation retained no ownership interest in the products after they had been sold. Additionally, the circuit court erred in ruling that venue was proper under the transaction prong of the venue statute, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-101 (2000). The cause of action did not spring into existence in Madison County, nor did some part of the transaction in which the cause of action arose occur in Madison County. Nor did the buyers' purchasing the cars in Madison County or the paint allegedly delaminating in Madison County sufficiently constitute some part of the transaction.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court was reversed, and an order was entered transferring the cause.

People v. Vida


No. 1-99-2922


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


339 Ill. App. 3d 115; 790 N.E.2d 64; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 555; 273 Ill. Dec. 922



May 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 20, 2003.
Opinion withdrawn by People v. Vida, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 595 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Frank De Boni, Judge Presiding.
People v. Vida, 323 Ill. App. 3d 554, 752 N.E.2d 614, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 491, 256 Ill. Dec. 734 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 22, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appellate court's order of March 28, 2003 was modified and defendant-appellant's sentence was reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to 100 years in prison, finding that his acts were exceptionally brutal, heinous, and indicative of wanton cruelty.


OVERVIEW: As a result of the brutality of the murder committed by defendant, he was sentenced to 100 years in prison. Although first degree murder carried a sentence of 20 to 60 years in prison under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(a) (1998), a court was permitted to sentence a defendant to 60 to 100 years in prison if the offense was exceptionally brutal or heinous indicative of wanton cruelty. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2(a)(1), 5-5-3.2(b) (1998). Defendant claimed that his 100 year sentence was unconstitutional, because the sentence was beyond the statutory maximum, requiring the trial court to submit to the jury the question of whether the murder was exceptionally brutal. The trial court was not required to submit the exceptionally brutal question to the jury, because the maximum sentence in a first degree murder case was natural life in prison. In addition, the statute used to impose an extended-term sentence upon defendant involved a consideration of the evidence regarding the particular offense in question after he was tried on the elements of that offense. Therefore, no new evidence was considered by the trial court in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Wilburn


No. 3-02-0297


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


338 Ill. App. 3d 1075; 789 N.E.2d 797; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 511; 273 Ill. Dec. 623



April 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 4, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Wilburn, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1917 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 95-CF-781. Honorable James T. Teros Judge, Presiding.
People v. Wilburn, 174 Ill. 2d 591, 686 N.E.2d 1172, 1997 Ill. LEXIS 623, 227 Ill. Dec. 16 (1997)
People v. Wilburn, 289 Ill. App. 3d 1148, 713 N.E.2d 837, 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 3891, 239 Ill. Dec. 306 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; sentence vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County (Illinois), dismissed petitioner's amended postconviction petition as untimely after petitioner was convicted of aggravated battery with a firearm and armed violence, the trial court sentenced him to consecutive 25 years in prison on each offense, and he filed an amended petition for postconviction relief. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A petitioner was convicted of aggravated battery with a firearm and armed violence based on an incident in which he shot the victim with a handgun and robbed him of cash. At that time, armed violence with a handgun was punishable by 15 to 30 years in prison. The petitioner was sentenced under the sentencing statutes to consecutive 25-year terms of imprisonment. His convictions were affirmed on appeal and his petition for leave to appeal to the state supreme court was denied. Thereafter, the state supreme court filed an opinion in another case that found the law that enacted amendments to the sentencing provisions for armed violence was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule of the Illinois Constitution. Petitioner did not file his petition for postconviction relief for approximately 16 months after the opinion in that other case had been filed. After the trial court dismissed his petition as untimely, the appellate court found that the petitioner was entitled to file his petition beyond the normal statutory time limits for doing so, as the facts did not show that the delay in filing the petition was due to his culpable negligence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, petitioner's sentence on his armed violence conviction was vacated, and petitioner's case was remanded to resentence petitioner under a prior version of the armed violence sentencing statute.

Puffer-Hefty Sch. Dist. No. 69 v. Du Page Reg'l Bd. of Sch. Trs.


No. 2-02-0196


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


339 Ill. App. 3d 194; 789 N.E.2d 800; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 528; 273 Ill. Dec. 626



April 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rule 23 Order Redesignated Opinion and Ordered Published in part May 1, 2003. Released for Publication June 3, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Puffer-Hefty Sch. Dist. No. 69 v. DuPage Reg'l Bd. of Sch. Trs., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 791 (Ill. App. Ct., Apr. 25, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by PUFFER-HEFTY SCH. DIST., ET AL. v. DU PAGE REG'L. BD. SCH., 540 U.S. 1219, 124 S. Ct. 1509, 158 L. Ed. 2d 155, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1669 (U.S., Mar. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01-MR-149. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.
Holbrook v. Regional Bd. of Sch. Trustees, 305 Ill. App. 3d 744, 713 N.E.2d 228, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 460, 238 Ill. Dec. 982 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of the decision of appellee regional board of school trustees to dissolve the school district and annex its territory to appellee neighboring school district, pursuant to 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2a(b) (1996) and 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-11 (1996).


OVERVIEW: 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-2a(b) (1996) let voters in a school district of less than 5,000 residents petition to dissolve the district. The appellate court held the equal protection challenge to the statute was subject to the rational basis test as it did not infringe the right to vote but affected the manner of exercising the right. The statute's purpose was rationally related to a legitimate state goal of promoting local control of education efficiently, and its population-based distinction was not arbitrary. The statute was not special legislation contrary to Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13, as it applied to all districts of the indicated size. The regional school board complied with statutory requirements, and a majority of the district's registered voters signed the petition. When the board's dismissal of the petition was reversed on appeal, the date to decide the petition's sufficiency was its filing, before dismissal, and it was sufficient as of that date. The subsequent withdrawal of signatures should not have been allowed. The regional board properly applied 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-11 (1996) to decide the district to which the dissolved district was annexed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Roberts


No. 2-01-0680


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


338 Ill. App. 3d 245; 788 N.E.2d 782; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 485; 273 Ill. Dec. 191



April 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. 00-CF-3112. Honorable K. Craig Peterson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of one count of possession of a look-alike substance with the intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of public housing property. Defendant was sentenced to 10 years and 10 months in prison and ordered to pay $ 20 as a street value fine and $ 100 as a trauma center fine. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) denied defendant's posttrial motions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that § 407(b)(3) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, codified at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/407(b)(3) (2000), punishing possession with intent to deliver a look-alike substance more severely than the statute governing possession with intent to deliver actual controlled substances, violated due process under the Illinois Constitution. The appellate court held that the potential for increased penalties for the offense of possession with intent to deliver look-alike substances did not violate due process under the Illinois Constitution. Defendant also contended that the trial court lacked statutory authority to impose a street value fine and a trauma center fine because § 5-9-1.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-9-1.1 (2000), expressly referred to cannabis and controlled substances and did not mention look-alike substances. The appellate court held that the failure of § 5-9-1.1 to mention look-alike substances led to the conclusion that the imposition of fines for such possession was not authorized.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence of 10 years and 10 months in prison was affirmed. That part of defendant's sentence imposing the $ 20 street value fine and the $ 100 trauma center fine was reversed.

People v. Smith


No. 1-01-4468


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


338 Ill. App. 3d 555; 788 N.E.2d 1204; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 482; 273 Ill. Dec. 328



April 18, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Smith, 205 Ill. 2d 633, 803 N.E.2d 497, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1750, 281 Ill. Dec. 93 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Shelley Sutker-Dermer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of attempted aggravated robbery. The trial court sentenced defendant to a nine-year prison term, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted aggravated robbery after he entered a convenience store wearing a mask, indicated he had a gun, and ordered the clerk to open the cash register. When police appeared in the parking lot of the store, defendant removed the mask and purchased a pack of cigarettes. Although defendant testified that he wore the mask because it was cold outside and never asked the clerk to open the register, the trial court convicted defendant of the charge, considered his prior convictions, and sentenced him, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2000), to nine years in prison. The appellate court held that the Class X sentencing enhancement provision of § 5-5-3(c)(8) did not violate defendant's rights to due process of law and trial by jury as guaranteed by the United States Constitution, or defendant's right to trial by jury as guaranteed by Ill. Const. art. I, § 13, and the trial court did not violate defendant's rights by sentencing defendant as a Class X offender without requiring the State to obtain a jury verdict finding that defendant had prior convictions which allowed defendant to be sentenced under § 5-5-3(c)(8).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1538 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth Edison Co. v. People ex rel. Coffman


No. 2-02-0342


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


338 Ill. App. 3d 623; 788 N.E.2d 364; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 457; 273 Ill. Dec. 55



April 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 16, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County. Nos. 98--TX--12, 99--TX--29, 00--TX--25. Honorable John E. Payne, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three consolidated cases, appellant property owner filed complaints against appellee county treasurer, objecting to real estate taxes levied against its property, and objecting to the issuance of certain general obligation bonds. The Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of the county treasurer and denied cross-motions for summary judgment filed by the property owner. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owner challenged general obligation bonds used by a forest preserve district to build a golf course. The property owner argued that the forest preserve district was required to submit the bonds in a referendum before the bonds were lawfully issued. The appellate court found that, by its ordinances, the forest preserve district pledged future general obligation bonds as a revenue source by which to fund the alternate bonds. The language of 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 350/3(l) (2000) encompassed the issuance of general obligation bonds to provide such a revenue source for the alternate bonds. The use of the general obligation bonds to provide a revenue source for the alternate bonds was specified in the enabling ordinance for each bond issue as well as authorized under the Debt Reform Act, 30 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 350/1 et seq. (2000). Because the bonds were plainly "revenue sources," they were properly issued. 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 805/13 (1996) required a referendum only if the aggregate indebtedness exceeded 0.3 percent of the assessed valuation of the taxable property in the district. The indebtedness did not exceed that value.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1539 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mitchell C. (In re Jamarqon C.)


Nos. 2-02-0991 & 2-02-1009 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


338 Ill. App. 3d 639; 788 N.E.2d 344; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 441; 273 Ill. Dec. 35



April 7, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 16, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 01-JA-234. Honorable Patrick L. Heaslip, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought to terminate the parental rights of respondents, the father and the mother, to their son. At the hearing the father's attorney requested a continuance. The request was denied. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) entered an order terminating respondents' parental rights. Respondents' appeals were consolidated for review.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court's failure to grant his motion for a continuance jeopardized his right to a fair trial and his ability to defend against the State's allegations. The appellate court concluded that since the father failed to demonstrate how he could have undermined the overwhelming evidence demonstrating a lack of reasonable interest in the child, the trial court properly found that he was unfit under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(m) (2000). The mother argued that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 50/1(D)(t) (2000), the statutory provision under which she was adjudicated unfit, was unconstitutional because it did not necessitate that the unfitness finding be by clear and convincing evidence. The appellate court noted that the fact that the mother gave birth to a child with drugs in his body who was subsequently adjudicated neglected marked the staring point of determining if the mother was unfit. The appellate court found that the State was required to prove that the mother failed to take advantage of drug treatment by clear and convincing evidence; thus, the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The order terminating respondents' parental rights was affirmed.

 

1540 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Evelyn S. (In re Evelyn S.)


NO. 5-01-0240


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 1096; 788 N.E.2d 310; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 404; 273 Ill. Dec. 1



April 1, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Evelyn S. (In re Evelyn S.), 213 Ill. 2d 559, 2005 Ill. LEXIS 25 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 01-MH-62. Honorable Ralph J. Mendelsohn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Madison County (Illinois), entered an order that found that respondent, an allegedly mentally ill person, was subject to the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication after she was found unfit to stand trial and was admitted to a mental health facility. She appealed. The Attorney General intervened, and both the State and Attorney General filed motions to dismiss her appeal.


OVERVIEW: The allegedly mentally ill person was charged with first-degree murder. However, she was found unfit to stand trial. She was admitted to a mental health facility. The State petitioned for the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication. The trial court granted her motion for continuance, but learned at its next hearing that no attorney had appeared on her behalf. The trial court then told her that her choices regarding representation were to accept her appointed attorney's continued representation or to represent herself. She chose to represent herself. The trial court made only a minimal inquiry into whether she had the capacity to waive her right to counsel. The trial court then heard evidence and found her to be a person subject to the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication. After she appealed, the appellate court found that the appeal was moot since she had been found fit to stand trial. It also found that the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/1-101 et seq., applied to her case, and that the trial court erred in not adequately inquiring into whether she had the capacity to waive her right to counsel.


OUTCOME: The State and the Attorney General's motions to dismiss the allegedly mentally ill person's appeal were denied and the trial court's order finding her to be a person subject to the involuntary administration of psychotropic medication was reversed.

Town of Cicero v. Ill. Ass'n, IAFF Local 717


No. 1-01-3931


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


338 Ill. App. 3d 364; 788 N.E.2d 286; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 389; 272 Ill. Dec. 982; 173 L.R.R.M. 2037



March 31, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 19, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CH 17698. Honorable Nancy J. Arnold, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court reversed; arbitral opinion and award affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a judgment that vacated and remanded an arbitral award in appellant firefighters' union's favor after the firefighters' union requested that its collective bargaining agreement with appellee town be relaxed regarding the town's requirement that municipal employees live within the town's municipal boundaries and the town sought to keep that requirement. The firefighters' union appealed.


OVERVIEW: A firefighters' union and a town disagreed on a proposal to eliminate the town's residency requirement that all municipal employees live within its boundaries. Eventually, the firefighters' union invoked its right to arbitrate that issue and made a last proposal that outlined specific residency boundaries beyond the town's boundaries. The arbitrator conducted evidentiary hearings and considered the eight interest arbitration factors set forth in 5 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 315/14(h). It then adopted the firefighters' union's last proposal. The town rejected the award. The arbitrator reaffirmed it. The town petitioned for review. The trial court vacated the arbitral award and remanded the case. After the firefighters' union appealed, the appellate court found the arbitrator had the authority to hear the dispute because the residency issue was a mandatory collective bargaining subject. It also found that the relevant factors allowed the arbitrator to consider the firefighters' "liberty interests" implicated by the residency requirement, that the arbitrator considered the mandatory arbitration factors, and that the law containing the arbitration factors was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision vacating and remanding the arbitral award in the firefighters' union's favor was reversed, and the arbitral opinion and award were affirmed.

 

1542 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Ford Motor Co. v. Motor Vehicle Review Bd.


No. 1-01-2475


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


338 Ill. App. 3d 880; 788 N.E.2d 187; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 354; 272 Ill. Dec. 883



March 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 19, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff auto manufacturer appealed from a judgment on administrative review by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that upheld a decision of defendant Illinois Motor Vehicle Review Board that the manufacturer terminated its dealership agreement with defendant dealer without good cause.


OVERVIEW: The agreement between the manufacturer and the dealer predated the enactment of the amended version of the Illinois Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 710/1 et seq. (2000), which applied specific standards to dealership agreements in determining whether such agreements were fairly administered and properly protected dealers in Illinois. Because the mediation provision in the dealership agreement provided far less protection to the dealer than the Act did, the appellate court looked to whether the standards could be applied retroactively. Since the standards in question had already been determined by the highest court of Illinois not to be applicable retroactively, the appellate court endorsed the decision of the motor vehicle review agency to look instead to whether good cause existed for the termination under a standard of commercial reasonableness, since a good cause standard had applied under pre-existing law, and the powers ordinarily delegated to Illinois agencies included the power to make determinations of that type.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v B.T. (In re D.T.)


No. 1-01-2410


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


338 Ill. App. 3d 133; 788 N.E.2d 133; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 347; 272 Ill. Dec. 829



March 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 19, 2003.
Appeal granted by People v. Brenda T. (In re D.T.), 205 Ill. 2d 583, 803 N.E.2d 482, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1432, 281 Ill. Dec. 78 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Brenda T. (In re D.T.), 212 Ill. 2d 347, 818 N.E.2d 1214, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1617, 289 Ill. Dec. 11 (Ill., Oct. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 JA 00402. Honorable Mark Lopez, Judge Presiding.
In re D.T., 312 Ill. App. 3d 1195, 769 N.E.2d 567, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1864, 264 Ill. Dec. 65 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), found that respondent mother was an unfit parent for failing to protect her son from certain abuse. After a best interest hearing, the trial court entered a judgment that terminated the mother's parental rights to her son. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: A four-year-old boy had several bruises on his face, multiple cuts and bruises on his arm, and various scratches on his back. Also, his scrotum was abnormally swollen. That injury was caused by repetitive blunt blows to the scrotum. The State petitioned to terminate the mother's parental rights and alleged she failed to protect her son from her abusive boyfriend. The trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the mother was an unfit parent. At a hearing to determine whether termination was in the child's best interests, the mother testified she had been physically abused as a child. However, she completed domestic violence and parenting classes, and participated in therapy. One social worker testified that it would be in the child's best interests to terminate, but several other social workers disagreed with that conclusion. The trial court granted the State's petition to terminate. After that judgment was entered, the appellate court found that a preponderance of the evidence standard applied to the best interest of the child decision, and application of that standard showed the trial court's decision to terminate was against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Lucas


NO. 1-99-2623


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 342



March 26, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Different results reached on rehearing at People v. Lucas, 795 N.E.2d 767, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 905, 277 Ill. Dec. 99 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lucas, 321 Ill. App. 3d 49, 746 N.E.2d 1211, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 158, 254 Ill. Dec. 163 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a conviction against him for attempted first degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and aggravated kidnapping. Defendant was sentenced to 120 years' imprisonment based on extended terms and consecutive sentences. The matter was appealed and remanded for a new sentencing determination.


OVERVIEW: The victim tried to buy drugs from defendant but only had a small amount of money. Defendant took the money and indicated that they could smoke the drugs together. However, upon reaching a wooded area, defendant grabbed her, punched her, and sexually assaulted her. She passed out continuously from the pain and after threatening to kill her and impaling her with a tree limb, defendant left. The trial court held a hearing on aggravating and mitigating factors and then imposed the consecutive and extended term sentence based on 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(2) and 5-8-4(a) (West 1999, 1998) and on its finding that the crime was exceptionally brutal and heinous. On appeal, the matter was originally affirmed but was remanded by a higher court for resentencing in view of case precedent. The court determined that the extended term sentences had to be vacated because the enhancing elements for those sentences were not specified in the indictment and proved to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. However, there was no such requirement imposed on consecutive sentences and those were found to be constitutionally imposed pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(a) (West 1998).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the consecutive sentences, but reversed and remanded that part of the sentencing order which imposed extended terms on the charges of attempted first degree murder and aggravated criminal sexual assault.

People v. Sylvia M. (In re M.M.)


No. 2-02-0327


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 764; 786 N.E.2d 654; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 333; 272 Ill. Dec. 115



March 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 97-JA-105. Honorable Judith M. Brawka, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that appointed the foster parents as guardians and closed the juvenile case involving the placement of two minor children of respondent biological mother. The biological mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The biological mother's two minor children were found living in filthy conditions. The State alleged the children were neglected, and the biological mother so stipulated. The minors were made wards of the court. Over the next four years, social workers attempted to work with her on a plan that would result in the ultimate goal of reunification. For example, the trial court ordered therapy sessions for her in an attempt to reunify her with the minor children and allow them to return home. The effort at returning them to her home failed and it became apparent that reunification was not in their best interests. The minors were placed with foster parents. Therapists later testified that it would be in the best interests of the minors to receive permanent placements. The trial court reset the permanency goal to guardianship. It then terminated the wardship, appointed the foster parents to be the minors' guardians, and closed the juvenile case of the minors. After it ruled, the appellate court found that it had jurisdiction over the case because the trial court's judgment was a final, appealable order. It also found the judgment was not against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Gorgis


No. 1-00-3759


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 960; 787 N.E.2d 329; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 320; 272 Ill. Dec. 514



March 19, 2003, Decided  
March 19, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 29, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Gorgis, 205 Ill. 2d 607, 803 N.E.2d 490, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1722, 281 Ill. Dec. 86 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph Urso and Thomas P. Fecarotta, Jr., Judges Presiding.
People v. Negrete, 333 Ill. App. 3d 1210, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 2683 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) that convicted him on jury verdict of first-degree murder and a related charge. On appeal, he argued that his confession should have been suppressed, that voir dire should have been reopened, that a truth-in-sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(i) (West 2000), was unconstitutional, and that the trial court relied on improper sentencing factors.


OVERVIEW: Several different witnesses described the circumstances surrounding defendant's confession to commission of a gang-related drive-by shooting. The judge at the hearing on the motion to suppress found the law enforcement witnesses more credible than defendant, and the appellate court found that the determination that defendant's statement was made voluntarily was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The fact that one juror had to be excused after expressing fears of gang reprisals did not oblige the trial court to reopen voir dire to determine whether other jurors were frightened, in the absence of any other evidence indicating a problem. The truth-in-sentencing statute did not violate due process or equal protection guarantees when it made persons convicted of first-degree murder ineligible for early release, because all first-degree murderers were treated equally and the law reasonably related to the State interest in discouraging murders. Finally, although defendant failed to preserve an alleged abuse of discretion in sentencing, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's consideration of nonstatutory factors in addition to required sentencing factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
