People v. Mena


No. 1-98-1326


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


338 Ill. App. 3d 1; 787 N.E.2d 274; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 312; 272 Ill. Dec. 459



March 17, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Mena, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 540 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 17, 2003)
Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Mena, 205 Ill. 2d 622, 796 N.E.2d 1056, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1452, 277 Ill. Dec. 690 (Ill., 2003)
On reconsideration by, Substituted opinion at People v. Mena, 345 Ill. App. 3d 418, 803 N.E.2d 92, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1543, 280 Ill. Dec. 862 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Ralph Reyna, Judge Presiding.
People v. Mena, 329 Ill. App. 3d 579, 768 N.E.2d 160, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 231, 263 Ill. Dec. 400 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: On reconsideration of appellate court's prior opinion, trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and case was remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the instant court on remand from the Supreme Court of Illinois, which directed the instant court to vacate and reconsider its initial opinion that vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case for resentencing. Defendant had been convicted of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim intentionally smashed his car into defendant's car. Defendant took a jack from the trunk of his car and hit the victim over the head with it several times, killing the victim. The trial court refused defendant's request for a jury instruction on second degree murder. Because the judge found that the murder was brutal and heinous, he sentenced defendant to an extended term of 90 years in prison. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request for a second degree murder instruction. A second degree murder charge was not warranted, as defendant's brutal murder of the victim was disproportionate to the victim's provocation. Defendant's extended prison term that was imposed under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(2), 5-8-2(a)(1) (West 1996) was unconstitutional. The jury's verdict authorized the trial court to sentence defendant to a term of 20 to 60 years, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(a) (West 1996). The trial judge's imposition of an extended sentence based on the judge's findings unconstitutionally deprived defendant of the right to a jury determination of fact crucial for setting the range of appropriate sentences.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated with regard to defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. Dean (In re Dean)


No. 3-01-1034


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 610; 786 N.E.2d 633; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 315; 272 Ill. Dec. 94



March 14, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 21, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Dean, 206 Ill. 2d 628, 806 N.E.2d 1068, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2327, 282 Ill. Dec. 480 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Warren County, Illinois. No. 01--MR--2. Honorable Charles H. Wilhelm, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State petitioned to commit defendant as a "sexually violent person" under the Illinois Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (West 2000). A jury found defendant a sexually violent person. The Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Warren County, Illinois, committed defendant to the department of human services until he was no longer a sexually violent person. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Act unconstitutionally denied defendant his due process rights, as it did not require the jury to determine that he lacked control over his behavior. Defendant argued that the Act violated the holding of Kansas v. Crane, which considered a Kansas act with similar language and found that a jury was required to find that a person lacked control of his behavior in order to civilly commit the person under the Kansas act. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's reading of Crane. The appellate court noted that People v. Hancock, decided by an Illinois appellate court, did not require a separate jury determination that defendant lacked volitional control in order to commit defendant under the Act.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's determination that defendant was a sexually violent person and defendant's commitment to the department of human services until he was no longer a sexually violent person were affirmed.

People v. Fox


No. 1-01-0554


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 477; 786 N.E.2d 563; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 264; 272 Ill. Dec. 24



February 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 17, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Preston L. Bowie, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance, and sentenced him to an extended five-year prison term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver less than 10 grams after a police officer watched him transfer items to other people, and defendant dropped a plastic bag containing 24 tinfoil packets when he ran from the officer. The officer delivered the plastic bag to a laboratory for testing, and the forensic chemist who received the bag tested one of the tinfoil packets and found it contained heroin. The chemist did not test the substances in the other packets, but wrote on his report that they contained "plant material." When this error was discovered, the chemist amended his report. The appellate court held that (1) the evidence showed that the police took reasonable protective measures to ensure that the evidence recovered by the officer was the same evidence that was delivered to the chemist, and the chemist's mistake went to the weight of his testimony, not its admissibility; and (2) the trial court did not violate defendant's right to trial by jury by imposing an extended sentence on defendant, based on defendant's prior convictions, without asking a jury to find that defendant had prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1550 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCoy


No. 2-01-0603


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 518; 786 N.E.2d 1052; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 270; 272 Ill. Dec. 218



February 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 10, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. McCoy, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1151 (Ill., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 99--CF--2058. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of three counts of first-degree murder, one count of attempted first-degree murder, and one of aggravated battery with a firearm based on accountability. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) imposed a mandatory sentence of natural life under the multiple-murder provision of the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections, codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(c)(ii) (West 2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his mandatory sentence of natural life based upon accountability offended the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. Defendant argued that, when a mandatory life sentence was imposed for a conviction based upon accountability, no one assessed the seriousness of the defendant's conduct at any stage, at trial or at sentencing, because intent to promote "any offense" was sufficient for accountability. Defendant asserted that satisfying the proportionality requirement necessarily required that some human being, at some stage in the process, judge the seriousness of what the defendant did, and the likelihood of restoring him to useful citizenship. The appellate court rejected defendant's contention that the constitution was violated because the seriousness of his conduct and his rehabilitative potential were never considered during sentencing. The appellate court noted that defendant was deemed guilty as a perpetrator of the ultimate offenses since, under the common-design rule, all participants were legally accountable for the concerted acts of all participants.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

Weipert v. Ill. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation


NO. 4-01-1030


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 282; 785 N.E.2d 553; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 250; 271 Ill. Dec. 621



February 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 26, 2003.
Appeal denied by Weipert v. Ill. Dep't of Prof'l Regulation, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1326 (Ill., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 01MR404. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff private investigator appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision by defendant Illinois Department of Professional Regulation, which denied his application for Illinois private detective licensure. At issue was the constitutionality of § 75(a)(6) ( 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 446/75(a)(6) (West 2000)) of the Private Detective, Private Alarm, Private Security, and Locksmith Act of 1993.


OVERVIEW: The investigator, who was licensed in Iowa and worked as a insurance claims representative, sought licensure in Illinois. The application was denied based on the investigator's failure to meet the work experience requirement of § 75(a)(6). The investigator appealed, challenging the constitutionality of § 75(a)(6), and the trial court affirmed. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the Department did not err. The court first noted that although the investigator had forfeited his constitutional challenge by not raising it before the agency, it would relax the forfeiture requirement in the interests of justice. Section 75(a)(6) was constitutional under the "apprentice test" because there was no monopolistic right to instruct where there were alternatives to the work experience requirement and because the statute was calculated to enhance expertise. There was no due process violation because the experience requirement was a reasonable means of achieving the legislative goal of protecting the public. Finally, there was no equal protection violation because the legislature's classification regarding the types of qualifying investigative experience had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

People v. Span

Appeal denied by People v. Span, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1764 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 97--CF--200. Honorable Larry S. Vandersnick, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's sentence was modified and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County (Illinois), which, on remand, sentenced defendant to a 20-year term of imprisonment for armed violence. The sentence was to run consecutively to defendant's sentences for other crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally sentenced to 25 years in prison on the armed violence charge. The sentence was to be served consecutively to sentences defendant received for violating probation. The trial court found that the nature of the offenses and defendant's character warranted that consecutive sentences be imposed to protect the public. The sentence was remanded for resentencing, because defendant was sentenced under an unconstitutional sentencing statute. On appeal of the second sentence, defendant argued that the trial court was required to make a new finding that the public's protection required consecutive sentences. The trial court failed to articulate a sufficient rationale for the imposition of consecutive sentences. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(b) (West 2000). The record of the second hearing failed to set forth a clear basis for the trial court's belief that consecutive sentences were warranted.


OUTCOME: The sentence was modified so that the sentence for armed violence was to run concurrently with defendant's other sentences. The cause was remanded to the trial court to correct the mittimus.

People v. Mendez


No. 3-02-0446


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


336 Ill. App. 3d 935; 784 N.E.2d 425; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 169; 271 Ill. Dec. 207



February 7, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 11, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--656. Honorable J. Peter Ault, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tenth Judicial Circuit Court, Tazewell County (Illinois), entered a judgment that summarily dismissed petitioner convicted criminal's petition for postconviction relief as frivolous and patently without merit after the convicted criminal pled guilty to unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. The convicted criminal appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State charged the convicted criminal with unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. He decided to plead guilty. In the factual basis for the plea, the State asserted that an undercover police officer had arranged to purchase cocaine from him. The officer later met him. He handed the officer a bag. The officer handed him a specific sum of money. The substance in the bag was later analyzed and found to be cocaine. The trial court accepted his guilty plea. The convicted criminal asserted in his postconviction relief petition that he had been entrapped into committing the offense. He argued in support that he had no prior criminal record, he was not predisposed to committing the offense, and that an informant had approached him more than 15 times before he agreed to make the sale. He also alleged his counsel was ineffective for neither investigating nor informing him of potential defenses, including entrapment. After the trial court dismissed the petition as frivolous and patently without merit, the appellate court found he alleged the gist of a constitutional claim that his plea was involuntary because his counsel was ineffective in failing to advise him on entrapment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Miller v. Fulton County Zoning Bd. of Appeals


Nos. 3-00-0673, 3-00-1002, 3-01-0940, 3-01-0952


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


337 Ill. App. 3d 210; 785 N.E.2d 532; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 121; 271 Ill. Dec. 600



February 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 26, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Miller v. Hill, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 407 (Ill. App. Ct., Feb. 6, 2003)
Appeal denied by Miller v. Hill, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1792 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fulton County. No. 99-MR-23. Honorable Larry W. Heiser, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbors of defendant firearm range operator appealed from two judgments of the Fulton County Circuit Court (Illinois), one upholding the issuance of a conditional use permit for the firearm range by defendant zoning board and the other--a partial summary judgment--denying an injunction sought by the neighbors against the operation of the firearm range.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court, as had the trial court, reviewed the zoning board's decision under the deferential standard prescribed by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-110 (West 2000), under which the grant of a conditional use variance would be upheld if the findings on which it was based were not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Since there was plenty of evidence that the board considered neighboring landowners' interests as well as the welfare of the community as a whole in reaching its decision, the permit was upheld. The injunctive relief sought by the neighbors was unavailable to them because 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 130/5(c) (West 2000) precluded them from bringing any action in trespass or nuisance, based solely on noise concerns, against an owner or operator of a lawful firearm range. This protection extended to actions seeking injunctive relief. The statutory protection did not violate the certain remedy guarantee of Ill. Const. art. I, § 12, because an owner or operator could be held liable on other grounds, or the special legislation prohibition of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13, because it bore a rational basis to a policy of protecting such activity in rural areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both judgments.

People v. Smith


No. 1-01-2623


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 175; 785 N.E.2d 76; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 80; 271 Ill. Dec. 425



January 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 21, 2003.As Corrected February 5, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Smith, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1172 (Ill., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 86 CR 6283. Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.
People v. Bradford, 187 Ill. App. 3d 903, 543 N.E.2d 918, 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1277 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1989)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after it found petitioner guilty of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. It then imposed an enhanced sentence on him after he and the State stipulated he had prior federal court drug convictions. After the conviction and sentence were affirmed, the trial court summarily denied his postconviction petition. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After a bench trial, petitioner was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. At sentencing, he and the State stipulated that he had prior federal court drug convictions. The trial court sentenced him to 40 years in prison pursuant to an Illinois statute allowing for an enhanced sentence for conviction on a second or subsequent drug offense. His conviction and sentence were then affirmed on direct appeal. He later filed a post-conviction petition alleging that his enhanced sentence violated his constitutional rights under Apprendi. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition, concluding that the sentence fell within the recidivist exception to the Apprendi rule. After that judgment was entered, the appellate court found his sentence was proper since the prior convictions used to enhance his sentence involved a narrow exception to the general rule in Apprendi because procedural safeguards were present when those prior convictions were obtained. It also found that since the sentencing law dealt with enhancements and not the offense itself, the State was not required to present the prior convictions to a jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Turner


No. 1-00-3452


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 80; 785 N.E.2d 879; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 81; 271 Ill. Dec. 685



January 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 21, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a judgment dismissing defendant's amended petition for postconviction relief challenging his murder conviction. In doing so, the trial court did not provide defendant with an evidentiary hearing. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of murder in a jury trial. About eight years after his conviction, the Illinois Supreme Court ruled in another case that the ultimate decision on whether to tender a lesser-included offense instruction belonged to a defendant. The ruling did not cite either the United States Constitution or the Illinois Constitution. More than five years later, defendant filed an amended postconviction petition claiming the Illinois Supreme Court ruling applied to his case. The trial court dismissed his petition without an evidentiary hearing. In so doing, the trial court noted that he presided over the murder trial and would not have given an involuntary manslaughter instruction in any event. After defendant appealed, the appellate court found the petition was barred by the longest applicable limitations period and defendant could not show the delay in filing was not due to his culpable negligence. It also found that the Illinois Supreme Court ruling was not of constitutional dimension and could not be applied retroactively, and that he was not prejudiced since the trial court would not have given a lesser-included offense instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ill. State Toll Highway Auth. v. Amoco Oil Co.


No. 2-01-1201


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


336 Ill. App. 3d 300; 783 N.E.2d 658; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 21; 270 Ill. Dec. 696



January 15, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 94--MR--266. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Illinois State Toll Highway Authority (ISTHA), appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which dismissed its complaint against defendant oil companies, seeking a declaration pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/2-701(a) (West 2000) that the companies violated the terms of gas station operating agreements, and further seeking contribution for cleanup costs.


OVERVIEW: The ISTHA and the companies had agreements that allowed the companies to operate highway rest stop gas stations, for which there were underground petroleum storage tanks, pipe systems, and fuel dispensers. The ISTHA alleged that the companies caused spillage and leakage of petroleum products and that costly cleanups were required. The trial court granted the companies' motion to dismiss the complaint, and on appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that the fact that the ISTHA had potential alternative remedies through a breach of contract action did not preclude seeking a declaratory judgment. It was error to dismiss the complaint on that basis, as the wording of the Act clearly indicated that a declaratory judgment action was an alternative and acceptable procedure to pursue. The court also found that the ISTHA stated a claim for contribution, holding that there was no requirement that a claim be filed against it prior to seeking contribution, pursuant to the Illinois Joint Tortfeasor Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 100/1 et seq. (West 2000), and that it alleged continuing violations of the Environmental Act, 415 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/12(a), (d), 5/21(a), (e) (West 2000).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court order and remanded for further proceedings.

King v. N. Ind. Commuter, Trans. Dist.


No. 1-02-0598


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 52; 785 N.E.2d 35; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 18; 271 Ill. Dec. 384



January 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 21, 2003.
Appeal denied by King v. N. Ind. Commuter Transp. Dist., 2003 Ill. LEXIS 597 (Ill., Apr. 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Martin E. McDonough, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed; matter remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee injured party sued, inter alia, appellant transportation district in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for personal injuries. The trial court denied the district's motion to dismiss and certified questions for interlocutory appeal, pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was removed, in Illinois, in an inebriated state from a train operated by the transportation district, and fell from the train platform. The appellate court held the principle of comity required the courts of Illinois to give effect to the laws of Indiana. One of those laws provided that the State of Indiana, and its agents, were immune from suit outside the courts of Indiana. The transportation district was undisputedly an Indiana state agency protected by this law. It was consistent with the policies of Illinois to honor Indiana's sovereign immunity, under the circumstances of the case. This was not inconsistent with the provisions of Ill. Const. art. I, § 12, providing that every person was to find a remedy for all injuries and wrongs. This did not provide the injured party with a constitutional right to a remedy for injuries occurring in Illinois but merely expressed a philosophy. This aspirational goal was not violated by restricting the remedies available to the injured party.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

People v. Townsell


3-00-0302


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


336 Ill. App. 3d 340; 783 N.E.2d 164; 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 6; 270 Ill. Dec. 589



January 8, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Townsell, 204 Ill. 2d 680, 792 N.E.2d 312, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1137, 275 Ill. Dec. 81 (2003)
Reversed by People v. Townsell, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 669 (Ill., Apr. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 91--CF--191. Honorable Jay Hanson, Judge, Presiding.

 People v. Townsell, 328 Ill. App. 3d 616, 262 Ill. Dec. 843, 766 N.E.2d 1146, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 140 (2002).
People v. Townsell, 328 Ill. App. 3d 616, 766 N.E.2d 1146, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 140, 262 Ill. Dec. 843 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated in part; prison term modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County (Illinois) to first degree murder and was sentenced to an extended prison term. On appeal, the court held that the extended portion of defendant's sentence was unconstitutional. However, the appellate court was ordered to vacate and reconsider its judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that extension of his sentence, based on the brutal or heinous element of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (1991), was a violation. The appellate court noted that at the time of defendant's sentencing hearing, the greatest punishment the judge could impose under that statute was 60 years in prison. Thus, the prescribed statutory maximum penalty for first degree murder was a 60-year prison term. Furthermore, the magnitude of defendant's claim warranted overriding the waiver rule, and defendant's guilty plea also effected a waiver. Additionally, because para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) was valid under at least one circumstance, the void ab initio doctrine did not qualify as a waiver exception. As defendant only pleaded guilty to the offense with which he was charged, ordinary first degree murder, it was thus fundamentally unfair to sentence him for a more severe offense.


OUTCOME: The portion of the circuit court's judgment extending defendant's prison term was vacated, and his sentence was modified to 60 years.

1564 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tracy H. (In re Alexis H.)


Nos. 2-01-1251 &, 2-01-1252


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 1009; 783 N.E.2d 158; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1272; 270 Ill. Dec. 583



December 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication 31, 2003.
Appeal granted by People v. Tracy H. (In re Alexis H.), 203 Ill. 2d 546, 788 N.E.2d 728, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 484, 273 Ill. Dec. 137 (2003)
Affirmed by People v. Tracy H. (In re A.H.), 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2274 (Ill., Nov. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 97--JA--12. Honorable Peter J. Dockery, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Honorable Peter J. Dockery, Judge, Presiding. No. 97--JA--13.



DISPOSITION: Appeals were dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State petitioned the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) to terminate the parental rights of appellee parents to two children. The trial court found the parents unfit but did not find termination to be in the children's best interests and denied the petitions. The State appealed the denial of each petition, and the appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The trial court continued the children's cases for permanency hearings, under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-28 (West 2000). The appellate court held, under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/2-28(2) (West 2000), permanency hearings to review the children's dispositional orders had to be held every six months until their permanency goal was attained. All rights and obligations set forth in the trial court's permanency order had to remain open for reexamination and possible revision until the permanency goal was achieved. A "final judgment," for purposes of appellate jurisdiction, absolutely fixed the rights of the parties. The State's appeal from the denial of the termination petitions "jumped the gun" on the next review of the children's permanency goal, and the appellate court lacked jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 301, 303 to review that denial. Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 306(a)(5) allowed review of interlocutory orders regarding unemancipated minors, but the State did not file the required petition. Even if that filing was excused, the grant of an interlocutory appeal under Rule 306(a)(5) was within the appellate court's discretion, which it declined to exercise.


OUTCOME: The State's appeal was dismissed.

People v. Gilford


No. 1-01-0695


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 722; 784 N.E.2d 841; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1255; 271 Ill. Dec. 287



December 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 2003.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Gilford, 206 Ill. 2d 630, 799 N.E.2d 679, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2305, 278 Ill. Dec. 814 (2003)
On remand at, Remanded by People v. Gilford, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 956 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Sept. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 C4 41108. Honorable Themis N. Karnezis, Judge Presiding.
People v. Gilford, 305 Ill. App. 3d 1104, 756 N.E.2d 485, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 2577, 258 Ill. Dec. 503 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was vacated and case was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied his motion to dismiss the State's petition, and ordered his civil commitment as a sexually dangerous person pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/4 (West 1996) of the Illinois Sexually Dangerous Persons Act. The State filed its petition two months before defendant's trial on two charges each of sexual abuse and sexual assault was to begin.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his civil commitment as a sexually dangerous person. The State filed its petition for defendant's commitment two months prior to his trial on two counts of sexual assault and two counts of sexual abuse. Defendant asserted that Illinois Sexually Dangerous Persons Act was unconstitutional, that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was a sexually dangerous person, and that the State improperly sought civil commitment instead of proceeding to trial. The court vacated and remanded, but found the statute to be constitutional. The court held that the statute was narrowly tailored to meet the State's two goals of ensuring the safety of the public from sexual assaults, and providing care and treatment to the mentally disordered. The court held that the State failed to meet its burden of proof that defendant was a sexually dangerous person. The court noted that although defendant was diagnosed as a pedophile that diagnosis alone did not imply that defendant had serious difficulty controlling his behavior, and the State failed to provide such evidence. The court held that the State did not improperly seek defendant's civil commitment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's civil commitment and remanded the case.

 

1566 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beachem


No. 1-99-0852


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 688; 784 N.E.2d 285; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1256; 271 Ill. Dec. 67



December 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 10, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Beachem, 203 Ill. 2d 552, 788 N.E.2d 730, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 761, 273 Ill. Dec. 139 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Beachem v. Illinois, 157 L. Ed. 2d 177, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5931 (U.S., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE COLLEEN MCSWEENEY-MOORE, JUDGE PRESIDING.
People v. Beachem, 317 Ill. App. 3d 693, 740 N.E.2d 389, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 868, 251 Ill. Dec. 308 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: On reconsideration of appellate court's prior decision, trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, first degree murder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to an extended term of 90 years' imprisonment for the murder conviction. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Thereafter, defendant filed a pro se post-conviction petition, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that her extended term sentence was unconstitutional as a violation of Apprendi. Apprendi was decided after defendant's direct appeal and after the denial of her post-conviction petition. The appellate court held that, generally, decisions which announced "new rules" were not applied retroactively to cases pending on collateral review. However, a new rule should have been applied retroactively if it required procedures that were implicit in the concept of ordered liberty. The gravity of an Apprendi violation was within this window of retroactivity. Thus, Apprendi applied to a timely filed post-conviction petition. Defendant did not forfeit her right to review of her extended sentence since Apprendi was decided after the trial court denied her post-conviction petition. However, the trial court, before sentence was imposed, found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was eligible for the death penalty, so her sentence of 90 years was not beyond the maximum. The jury's guilty verdict was a finding that the murdered victim of the robbery was over 60, which was sufficient to permit the trial judge to sentence defendant to an extended term.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Brown


No. 1-01-2961


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 711; 784 N.E.2d 296; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1254; 271 Ill. Dec. 78



December 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court Cook County. Honorable Clayton Jay Crane and Michael B. Bolan, Judges Presiding.
People v. Brown, 312 Ill. App. 3d 1201, 769 N.E.2d 570, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1977, 264 Ill. Dec. 68 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 20, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), denied petitioner convicted killer's petition for postconviction relief after the trial court convicted the convicted killer on one-count of first-degree murder involving a drive-by shooting, and the conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant appealed the denial of his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The convicted killer was charged with first-degree murder. After a trial, he was convicted. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The convicted killer then filed an initial petition with an explanation that he was doing so in order to meet an approaching deadline. The record did not make clear whether the trial court implicitly denied the amended petition that was subsequently filed or simply refused to address it. However, the record did clearly indicate that the trial court only considered the initial petition because the trial court did not refer to exculpatory evidence referenced in the amended petition. The trial court then denied the petition. After the convicted killer appealed, the appellate court found the trial court erred in denying the petition because the amended petition alleged the gist of constitutional claims. Indeed, its allegations indicated that defense counsel provided ineffective assistance when defense counsel did not call at trial two witnesses who could have provided exculpatory testimony and did not allow the convicted killer to testify even though he told defense counsel that he wanted to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Dewan v. Ford Motor Co.


No. 1-01-3259


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1233



December 18, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Dewan v. Ford Motor Co., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1235 (Ill. App. Ct., Sept. 30, 2003)
Opinion withdrawn by Dewan v. Ford Motor Co., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1254 (Ill. App. Ct., Oct. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CH 15909. Honorable Stephen A. Schiller, Judge Presiding.
Dewan v. Ford Motor Co., 195 Ill. 2d 550, 754 N.E.2d 1284, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 577 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer of defendant automobile manufacturer appealed from orders of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissing his complaint alleging violations of various Illinois and federal consumer statutes, denying his motion to amend his complaint, and denying his motion to set dates for proceedings relating to his petition for attorneys' fees.


OVERVIEW: The customer's car had defective sensors. The manufacturer repaired them, but not until after the customer had filed suit. The appellate court held that since the customer had been forced to sue, and could therefore be said to have been a prevailing party for purposes of recovery of attorney fees, and since certain refund offers made by the manufacturer did not appear to have made the customer whole, he could still make out a cognizable claim for damages and fees against the manufacturer. It was clear from the language of an order of the trial court dismissing the customer's claim, purportedly with prejudice, that the trial court had not intended that the dismissal in fact be final. Therefore, before the dismissal of his action would be final and reviewable, the customer would have to amend his complaint again, at which point he might well avoid dismissal. Failure of the dismissal order to include Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(a) language making it appealable also precluded review, since the petition for attorney fees was still pending. Finally, the court held that eventual consideration of the customer's claims would not be precluded by either res judicata or the law of the case.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction, as premature.

Waicekauskas v. Burke


No. 1-01-3673


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 436; 784 N.E.2d 280; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1216; 271 Ill. Dec. 62



December 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 7, 2003. Released for Publication February 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Christopher J. Donnelly, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: The court declared the ordinance invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a supplemental order in petitioner ordinance violator's case that contained specific findings that respondent village's municipal parking and vehicle condition ordinance violated neither the United States nor Illinois Constitutions and, further, that it complied with Illinois statutory law regarding the availability of a hearing to contest violations. The ordinance violator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance violator was issued tickets for various violations of a village parking ordinance. The ordinance violator requested a hearing. At the hearing, he objected to the ordinance and the hearing process as violating the Due Process Clause of the Illinois and United States Constitutions. His objection was that the violation notice required to be given to an ordinance violator stated that if a person wanted to contest his ticket and was found liable, the person could expect a higher fine than the ticket's face amount. His objection was denied. A finding of liable was entered and upheld. The trial court not only upheld that ruling, but specifically found the ordinance did not violate the state or federal due process clauses and that it did not violate 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-208.3 authorizing municipalities to adopt a civil penalty system for traffic violations. After that ruling was entered, the appellate court found the ordinance violated his state and federal due process rights by subjecting him to a fine if he exercised his right to appeal. It also found the whole ordinance had to be invalidated since the notice provision was not severable.


OUTCOME: The judgment upholding the ordinance and finding it complied with Illinois statutory law was reversed after the appellate court ruled that the ordinance was unconstitutional.

Advanced Imaging Ctr. of N. Ill. Ltd. P'Ship v. Cassidy


No. 2-02-0265


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 746; 781 N.E.2d 664; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1203; 269 Ill. Dec. 867



December 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 17, 2003.
Appeal granted by Advanced Imaging Ctr. of N. Ill. v. Cassidy, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 471 (Ill., Apr. 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 00--LA--256. Honorable Michael T. Caldwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company filed a 15-count complaint against defendant partner. The partner made an election to buy the interests of third-party defendant doctor in certain jointly owned companies. The partner filed a petition to stay all counts against him. The Circuit Court of McHenry County, Illinois, denied the partner's petition. The partner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The partner and the doctor were both practicing radiologists, and were business partners in two diagnostic imaging centers, facilities that performed magnetic resonance imagings (MRIs), mammograms, ultrasounds, bone marrow density tests, and other diagnostic tests. After the 15-count complaint was filed against the partner, he brought a third-party action against the doctor, seeking contribution or indemnification against the claims. Believing that the partner wrongfully obtained money from the jointly owned companies, the doctor filed a six-count counterclaim against the partner. The partner argued that 805 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 12.56(f) (West 2001) mandated a stay of all of the doctor's claims and that the trial court had no authority to deny his petition. The appellate court held that 805 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 12.56(f) did not mandate a stay but provided that a court could grant a stay in its discretion. Contrary to the partner's contention, while the word "shall" ordinarily indicated a mandatory legislative intent, it could be construed as permissive or directive. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the partner's petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Allen


NO. 4-00-0786


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 773; 780 N.E.2d 1133; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1204; 269 Ill. Dec. 409



December 10, 2002, Decided  
December 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published January 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County No. 00CF141 Honorable Steven H. Nardulli, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) convicted defendant of aggravated unlawful restraint and aggravated kidnapping, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/10-3.1(a), 5/10-2(a)(5) (West 2000). The court denied his posttrial motion, sentenced him as a habitual criminal under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 (West 2000), and sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that a man came up behind her, put a knife to her throat, and told her to get into his truck. The appellate court found that because the evidence of the other crime (he previously sexually assaulted a woman) was admitted but was not sufficiently similar to establish modus operandi, its admission under that exception was error. The two crimes were not so distinctive as to "earmark" them as the work of a single individual. The fact the victim of the other crime was assaulted while the victim in the charged crime was unharmed was a substantial dissimilarity. Moreover, the manner in which the perpetrator approached the victims, treated the victims during the crimes, and released the victims was different. Additionally, most of the similarities were general in nature, i.e., using a knife to force an individual who was walking alone into a vehicle. The dissimilarities destroyed the effect of the similarities. However, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, as the evidence was not closely balanced. The victim identified defendant in a photographic lineup, an in-person lineup, and in court, and gave a detailed description of the truck.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Hayes


No. 1-00-3681


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 145; 782 N.E.2d 787; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1174; 270 Ill. Dec. 228



December 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Preston L. Bowie, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Sentence and plea vacated; remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of a church. The trial court sentenced defendant to serve a six-year prison term consecutively to a seven-year sentence imposed after defendant's conviction in a separate case. Defense counsel filed a motion to reconsider and modify the sentence. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that defense counsel failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d), that the trial court failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(b), and that defendant's plea was not knowing and voluntary because the trial court failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402. As to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d), the appellate court noted that compliance was not achieved and the appropriate remedy was remand for a new hearing. As for Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(b), the appellate court found that the trial court violated Rule 605 in failing to articulate the procedural steps required for defendant to appeal. Thus, defense counsel's failure to file a notice of appeal without filing a motion to withdraw defendant's guilty plea did not constitute waiver. Finally, as for Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402, the appellate court noted that during the plea of guilty the trial court failed to admonish defendant that he was eligible for consecutive sentences. Defense counsel failed to allege said error; however, the appellate court noted that the trial court's failure constituted plain error. In considering the error, the appellate court found that defendant's plea was rendered involuntary by the trial court's failure.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence and plea were vacated. The case was remanded.

ChiCorp, Inc. v. Bower


No. 1-01-2426


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 132; 782 N.E.2d 768; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1171; 270 Ill. Dec. 209



December 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, County Department, Law Division, Tax and Miscellaneous Remedies Section. Honorable John A. Ward, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff securities broker sued defendants, Illinois Department of Revenue and others, seeking the return of money paid for gains on state bonds. The complaint also alleged that certain provisions in 1996 Ill. Laws 460 were unconstitutional and void. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, County Department, Law Division, Tax and Miscellaneous Remedies Section, granted the Department's motion to dismiss. The broker appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the broker argued that its complaint was not moot because the Illinois Protest Act provided for judicial determination of the correctness of tax claims, independent of the Department's decision not to assess the tax. The Department argued that the broker's relief under the Act was limited to a determination of the proper disposition of the money in the protest fund, and because the Department had agreed to return the money, the complaint was moot. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the appellate court concluded that the complaint was moot because there was no longer an actual case or controversy existing between the parties. The appellate court noted that the parties had agreed on the disposition of the money; thus there was no question to be decided by the court. The broker also argued that the circuit court should have applied the public interest exception. The appellate court found no compelling reason to apply the exception, noting that due to the enactment of 1996 Ill. Laws 460, the questions would not likely recur.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's dismissal of the broker's complaint was affirmed.

People v. Johnson


NO. 4-01-1039


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 805; 780 N.E.2d 803; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1175; 269 Ill. Dec. 331



December 2, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 31, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 01CF711. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) granting defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment that charged him with four counts of bribery in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33-1(a) (West 2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an attorney. Defendant was accused of giving the deputy circuit clerk $ 150 if the clerk provided defendant with bond forms of those individuals arrested for the offense of driving under the influence and other traffic offenses. The clerk was not permitted to accept the money. Defendant stated that he approached the clerk to hire her to provide him with copies of bond sheets containing the names and addresses of those charged with driving under the influence. The trial court found that the bribery statute contemplated the public official's action being more than a ministerial act to which defendant was already entitled. The appellate court found that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33-1(a) (West 2000) was not unconstitutionally vague, because defendant received adequate notice of the statute's proscription. The indictment contained sufficient facts to allege bribery even if defendant paid the clerk to perform a duty that defendant was legally entitled to have performed. Defendant's claim that he lacked corrupt intent was inconsequential, because corrupt intent was not an element under § 33-1(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

People v. Abdullah

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99CF474. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery. Defendant's motion for acquittal or, in the alternative, for a new trial was denied. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) adjudged defendant a habitual criminal under the Illinois Habitual Criminal Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1 to 33B-3 (West 2000), and sentenced him to life imprisonment, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/33B-1(e) (West 2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted his motions for a directed verdict and for acquittal notwithstanding the verdict because no rational jury would have believed that the eyewitness could have identified him as the robber. In upholding the jury's verdict, the appellate court noted that there was other evidence upon which the jury could have convicted defendant, including testimony regarding his clothing, a shot gun, and a mountain bike. Defendant also argued that the trial court should have granted his motion for a new trial because he was denied a fair trial. The appellate court found that defendant suffered no prejudice as the result of testimony that defendant possessed heroin when arrested because defendant admitted that he was a user of heroin. Finally, defendant argued that the trial court erred in adjudging him a habitual offender. The appellate court found no error, noting that defendant met the requirements of the Illinois Habitual Criminal Act, thus mandating the imposition of a life sentence.

People v. Williams


No. 1-01-0794


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

November 27, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Docket Number of this Case has been Corrected December 3, 2002. Released for Publication January 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and three counts of aggravated battery with a firearm. The trial court sentenced defendant for the murder and to three consecutive prison terms for each aggravated battery with a firearm conviction. Defendant appealed his consecutive sentencing for the aggravated battery with a firearm convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fired shots at a group of people. One man died. Three other people were wounded. One victim testified she was shot in the leg. Although she did not get immediate medical attention, she later spent five or six hours at the hospital. Another victim was shot in the leg. He also did not get immediate medical attention and was released from the hospital right after his wound was cleaned. The third victim sustained a wound to her left arm requiring emergency surgery and a 19-day hospital stay. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and three counts of aggravated battery with a firearm. He was then sentenced for the murder and also given three consecutive prison terms for each aggravated battery conviction. After judgment was entered, the appellate court found that to impose consecutive sentences pursuant to the relevant sentencing statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-8-4(a) (West 1996), it had to be shown that the victims sustained "severe bodily injury." While it concluded that element was shown as to the victim with the 19-day hospital stay, it remanded the case for the trial court to hold a new sentencing hearing as to the other two victims.


OUTCOME: The consecutive sentence imposed on the aggravated battery with a firearm conviction for the victim who spent 19 days in the hospital after being shot was affirmed. The consecutive sentences imposed on those convictions regarding the other two shooting victims were vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing as to the sentences regarding the two shooting victims.

In re Marriage of Centioli


No. 1-01-2043


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), granted petitioner husband's motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action upon which relief could be granted after respondent wife sought injunctive relief to compel him to restore his estate plan to the status existing prior to his institution of dissolution of marriage proceedings and to restrain him from disposing of his property except as statutorily permitted. The wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband sought a divorce. During dissolution proceedings, he removed his wife as beneficiary of his inter vivos revocable trust. The wife then petitioned for injunctive relief to compel him to restore his estate plan to its predissolution status. She alleged the parties had created separate inter vivos revocable trusts for estate planning purposes and had designated each other as trust beneficiary upon their deaths. The trial court granted the husband's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. After judgment was entered, the appellate court found the wife was not entitled to the preliminary injunction she sought, as her allegations were insufficient to show the existence of mutual wills or a binding contract regarding revocation, a protectable right, or that he had transferred property he was not allowed to transfer.

People v. Hanks


No. 1-00-2519 and 1-00-3854 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


335 Ill. App. 3d 894; 781 N.E.2d 601; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1117; 269 Ill. Dec. 804



November 27, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Daniel J. Kelley, Judge Presiding.
People v. Hanks, 307 Ill. App. 3d 1069, 760 N.E.2d 1060, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 4326, 260 Ill. Dec. 287 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and armed robbery after a jury trial. The convictions were affirmed on appeal. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissed petitioner's pro se requests for relief pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 122-1 et seq. (West 2000), after finding the issues raised therein to be frivolous and patently without merit. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of two crimes and his request for post-conviction relief was summarily dismissed. On appeal, the court remanded with directions. The court held that the trial court erred in summarily dismissing the petition because petitioner stated a "gist" of a meritorious claim in arguing that he was denied a fair and impartial trial and that his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise that issue on appeal. Specifically, petitioner alleged he was denied a fair trial because one of the jurors worked during the same time as petitioner at a hotel when petitioner was convicted of raping a hotel guest. Petitioner's claim was not waived for failure to raise it on direct appeal because his appellate counsel's failure to raise the issue at that time was objectively unreasonable where the record demonstrated that the juror may have possessed exceptionally prejudicial information concerning the prior conviction. As such, an evidentiary hearing should have been held. The court further held that because a gist of a claim had been found to exist, the entire petition and all of the claims therein were required to be remanded to the trial court for consideration.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause to the trial court for petitioner's claim for relief to be redocketed and advanced to the second stage for the trial court to determine whether petitioner made a substantial showing of constitutional violations. The trial court was also directed to consider the allegations raised in petitioner's second postconviction petition regarding his sentence.

S. 51 Dev. Corp. v. Vega


Nos. 1-01-3251, 1-01-3255, and 1-01-3260 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


335 Ill. App. 3d 542; 781 N.E.2d 528; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1103; 269 Ill. Dec. 731



November 26, 2002, Decided  
November 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 15, 2003.
Appeal granted by Advance Am. v. Vega (In re S. 51 Dev. Corp.), 203 Ill. 2d 570, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 469 (2003)
Appeal granted by S. 51 Dev. Corp. v. Vega, 203 Ill. 2d 570, 788 N.E.2d 735, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 482, 273 Ill. Dec. 144 (2003)
Appeal dismissed by S. 51 Dev. Corp. v. Vega, 211 Ill. 2d 189, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1014 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Sophia H. Hall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant short-term lenders sued appellee director in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for declaratory judgment as to the validity of legislation amending the Illinois Consumer Installment Loan Act, 205 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 670/1 et seq. (West 2000), and certain short-term lending rules promulgated pursuant to the amendatory legislation. The trial court granted the director's motion to dismiss. The short-term lenders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The short-term lenders sought to declare the amendment to 205 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 670/22 (West 2000) of the Illinois Consumer Installment Loan Act, 205 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 670/1 et seq. (West 2000), unconstitutional and the rules promulgated thereunder by the Illinois Department of Financial Institutions void or, alternatively, invalid. On appeal, the court concluded that the amendment represented a valid delegation of legislative authority to the Department. Further, the amendment provided sufficiently intelligible standards to guide the Department's rulemaking discretion and, accordingly, was not impermissibly vague. Moreover, the promulgated rules were consistent with and did not transcend the scope of the Loan Act statutory scheme. Finally, the impact analysis by the Illinois Department of Commerce and Community Affairs was submitted within the time constraints imposed by 5 Ill. Comp. Sta. Ann. 100/5-30(c) (West 2000). Accordingly, the amendment and the rules promulgated thereunder were valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Edwards


Nos. 1-98-0444, 1-98-0445, 1-98-1928, 1-98-2095, 1-01-0497, 1-01-0779 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


337 Ill. App. 3d 912; 788 N.E.2d 35; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1111; 272 Ill. Dec. 731



November 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Edwards, 203 Ill. 2d 554, 788 N.E.2d 731, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 652, 273 Ill. Dec. 140 (2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Edwards, 788 N.E.2d 731, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 653 (Ill., 2003)
Rehearing denied by People v. Edwards, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 642 (Ill. App. Ct., Apr. 28, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Edwards, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1907 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Edwards, 803 N.E.2d 488, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1898, 281 Ill. Dec. 84 (Ill., 2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at People ex rel. Dir. of Corr. v. Edwards, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 752 (Ill. App. Ct., June 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 94 CR 16717. The Honorable Marcus R. Salone, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments on jury verdict of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting them (after trials before two different juries) of criminal drug conspiracy. They argued primarily that their indictment had been duplicitous and that the nonconsensual eavesdropping orders used to gather evidence were constitutional. They also challenged certain evidentiary rulings and the length of their sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested for criminal drug conspiracy in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 570/405.1 (West 2000) after a long investigation during which police gathered evidence via electronic eavesdropping pursuant to warrants obtained in accordance with 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. art. 5/108B (West 2000) as well as from pen registers that recorded numbers called from the phones they used. The appellate court held, first, that the indictment was not duplicitous. Although many acts were alleged, they were all allegedly committed in furtherance of a single conspiracy, and that conspiracy was the crime of which they were convicted. The statutory procedures, which were followed nearly to the letter, assured that the issuance of warrants for electronic surveillance did not violate the protections of the Fourth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. Pen registers were not searches within the Fourth Amendment's definition, although they were possible breaches of privacy rights protected by the state provision. Defendants lacked standing to challenge them, however, because they had no reasonable expectation of privacy in phones they did not own.


OUTCOME: The court corrected an error in the mittimus for one defendant, but otherwise affirmed the judgments in all respects.

Fabiano v. City of Palos Hills


No. 1-00-1266


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


336 Ill. App. 3d 635; 784 N.E.2d 258; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1099; 271 Ill. Dec. 40



November 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 5, 2003. Released for Publication March 10, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Fabiano v. City of Palo Hills, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1387 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 25, 2002)
Appeal denied by Fabiano v. City of Palos Hills, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1269 (Ill., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 L 6149. The Honorable Randye A. Kogan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), granted summary judgment to defendants, a city, a police chief, and two police officers, after plaintiff day care owner sued them alleging malicious prosecution and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims, and her spouse sought loss of consortium damages. It also denied the day care owner and spouse's motion to compel discovery of police department personnel files. The day care owner and spouse appealed.


OVERVIEW: The day care owner operated two day care centers. A child alleged that the day care owner had sexually assaulted her. An investigation ensued. At least three other children alleged the day care owner sexually abused them. She was indicted for the aggravated criminal sexual assaults of the four children. She was tried for assaulting the first child. The jury returned a not guilty verdict. The State nol-prossed the remaining indictments. She then sued the police chief and two police officers for malicious prosecution and for violating her civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The spouse filed a loss of consortium claim. The city was also joined as a defendant. After the trial court granted the police chief, police officers, and city's summary judgment motion on all the claims, the appellate court found that they did not show the absence of any of the malicious prosecution elements or that they were entitled to immunity and, thus, the trier of fact needed to hear the case. However, it also found that denial of the day care owner's and spouse's motion to compel seeking police department personnel files was proper, as the request was an unwarranted "fishing expedition."


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city, the police chief, and the two police officers was reversed. The judgment denying the day care owner and spouse's motion to compel discovery was affirmed. Also, the case was ordered to be remanded so that it could proceed to trial.

Lyon v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


NO. 4-01-0760


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS FOURTH DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 376; 780 N.E.2d 748; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1071; 269 Ill. Dec. 276



November 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 7, 2003, Reported at: 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 8.
Rehearing denied by Lyon v. Ill. Dep't Children & Family Serv., 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 8 (Ill. App. Ct., Jan. 7, 2003)
Modified and rehearing denied by, 01/07/2003
Appeal granted by Lyon v. Ill. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 203 Ill. 2d 549, 788 N.E.2d 729, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 483, 273 Ill. Dec. 138 (2003)
Affirmed by Lyon v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 361 (Ill., Mar. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 01MR226. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff choir director, pursuant to 325 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7.16, sued defendants Department of Children and Family Services, its Director, and an administrative law judge, claiming error in the Department's refusal to remove from its central register an "indicated" report listing him as a child molester. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) reversed the department's decision. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on a student's charge that the choir director sexually molested her, the Department filed an "indicated" report of abuse. It denied the choir director's request for expungement. He requested a hearing, and the Department was ordered to give him copies of its investigative file. After the hearing, the "indicated" finding was upheld. The trial court reversed due to the Department's untimely production of portions of a police report. The instant court disagreed, because the choir director had not shown prejudice from his late receipt of the report, but affirmed on other grounds. The instant court held the Department could file an "indicated" report on the basis of "credible evidence," rather than a preponderance of the evidence, without violating the choir director's right to due process. However, having done so, it was obliged to strictly comply with its statutory and regulatory deadlines for processing the administrative appeal. The Department missed the 90-day deadline to issue its decision, and the Director missed the 45-day deadline to issue his opinion. By failing to meet statutory and regulatory deadlines, the Department violated the choir director's right to due process.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

City of Urbana v. Andrew N.B.


NO. 4-01-0773


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 180; 780 N.E.2d 765; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1077; 269 Ill. Dec. 293



November 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 31, 2002.
Appeal denied by City of Urbana v. Andrew N.B., 203 Ill. 2d 571, 788 N.E.2d 735, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 543, 273 Ill. Dec. 144 (2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by City of Urbana v. Andrew N.B., 2004 Ill. LEXIS 990 (Ill., June 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 01OV640. Honorable Jeffrey B. Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed from his conviction of theft by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), after being charged with violation of a city ordinance. Defendant violated two of the conditions of his supervision for theft, was found in indirect criminal contempt, and was sentenced to 12 months of probation, 180 days of detention, eight days to be served immediately; both the contempt conviction and sentence were also appealed.


OVERVIEW: The proceedings were not conducted under the Juvenile Court Act, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-1 et seq. Defendant contended that § 5-125, codified at 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-125 (West 2000), which permitted a prosecution under a city ordinance without the procedural safeguards provided for in the Act, violated his rights to equal protection and due process. The appellate court found that § 5-125 was constitutional. There was a reasonable purpose for the statute, so there was no equal protection violation. Further, the juvenile received due process even though the trial court did not appoint counsel for the theft charge, as he was not imprisoned for it. Counsel was appointed for the contempt charge. The sentence for criminal contempt was not an abuse of discretion. The juvenile could avoid imprisonment for all but eight days of the sentence by obeying the trial court's probationary order that he comply with the requirements that the law and society imposed on 13-year-olds. The trial court had jurisdiction in the contempt proceedings as the juvenile had not completed his supervision for the theft. The contempt charge did not have to be filed as a separate proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

People v. Swanson


No. 2-01-0591


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 117; 780 N.E.2d 342; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1073; 269 Ill. Dec. 157



November 15, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 13, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Swanson, 206 Ill. 2d 641, 806 N.E.2d 1072, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2323, 282 Ill. Dec. 484 (2003)
Related proceeding at Swanson v. Liberty Healthcare Corp., 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16053 (C.D. Ill., Feb. 6, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99--MR--688. Honorable Edward R. Duncan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State petitioned the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) to find defendant to be a sexually violent person, pursuant to the provisions of the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (West 1998). The trial court granted the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Sexual offender commitment laws had to require proof of a person's serious difficulty in controlling behavior. The appellate court held, though the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 et seq. (West 1998), did not explicitly mandate a finding as to an offender's self-control ability, the State had to prove the offender's mental disorder affecting the ability to control conduct. No other findings of an offender's inability to control conduct were required. Defendant was not discharged from the Illinois Department of Corrections until released from mandatory supervision, so the State complied with the provision in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/15(b)(2) (West 1998) that it file a commitment petition within 90 days of his discharge by filing before the end of his incarceration for a second conviction, after mandatory supervision. Admitting hearsay an expert did not rely on in forming an opinion was harmless error, given other evidence. Not objecting to the results of a penile plethysmograph, not shown to have general scientific acceptance, did not prejudice defendant, given other evidence, so ineffective assistance of counsel was not shown.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Chi. Limousine Serv. v. City of Chicago


No. 1-00-4149


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


335 Ill. App. 3d 489; 781 N.E.2d 421; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1052; 269 Ill. Dec. 624



November 12, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 21, 2002. Released for Publication January 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CH 12428. Honorable Paul P. Biebel, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limousine service corporation appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its breach of contract and promissory estoppel claims in an action against defendants, a city and related entities, which was related to livery licenses issued by the city during a certain period. The corporation did not appeal the dismissal of four additional counts in its complaint.


OVERVIEW: The city had an ordinance that regulated the issuance of livery licenses and limited the number of licenses available. The ordinance was amended many times and ultimately the cap on licenses was lifted. Nine years after the termination of the cap, the corporation instituted an action that alleged multiple claims and the trial court dismissed each claim. On the corporation's appeal from the dismissal of its contract and estoppel claims, the court affirmed. The court first held that the corporation's action was not time-barred under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/8-101 (West 2000) because that statute did not apply to contract claims. No contract was formed between the parties because the ordinance was not a unilateral offer that the corporation accepted by obtaining livery licenses. The city did not promise to limit the number of licenses issued, nor did it direct the ordinance at any particular organization. As there was no contract, it followed that there was no breach. The corporation's promissory estoppel claim was properly dismissed because the ordinance was not a promise purporting to be directed to the corporation and, further, estoppel against public bodies was extremely rare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.
