People v. Lewis


No. 1-01-3760


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 993; 779 N.E.2d 490; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1042; 268 Ill. Dec. 876



November 8, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Lewis, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1880 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stuart E. Palmer, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lewis, 317 Ill. App. 3d 1157, 783 N.E.2d 238, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 3200, 270 Ill. Dec. 663 (Ill. App. Ct., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered an open plea of guilty to two counts of first-degree murder. Following an earlier sentencing and remand, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had beaten a five-year-old child over two days, and left him alone to die. In the first appeal, defendant's sentence was vacated since the statute under which he was sentenced was unconstitutional. On remand, defendant did not move to withdraw his guilty plea. The parties stipulated to the evidence presented at the first sentencing hearing. On appeal, defendant argued that the prior decision required the trial court to conduct a full resentencing hearing. The appellate court ruled that the trial court's conduct of the resentencing hearing on remand was proper. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(b) provided for a discretionary, not mandatory, life imprisonment where a trial court found, inter alia, that the murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous or wanton cruelty. The life sentence was supported by factors including, but not limited to, the unprovoked and senseless nature of the attack, the number of wounds inflicted, the extent of the injury inflicted, the prolonged nature of the offense, the conduct devoid of mercy or compassion, the amount of force used, the repeated gratuitous violence, and the mental anguish of the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. C.T.S.


No. 3-01-0227


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 167; 779 N.E.2d 1148; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1047; 269 Ill. Dec. 113



November 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 00-JD-153. Honorable Chris L. Frederickson Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a trial in absentia, the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois), found defendant, a minor, delinquent for having committed unlawful possession of a motor vehicle, in violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/4-103(a)(1) (West 2000), and residential burglary, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/19-3(a) (West 2000). The trial court sentenced defendant in absentia. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of a motor vehicle and residential burglary. The trial court appointed counsel for defendant and informed her she could be tried in absentia if she failed to appear for trial. Defendant denied the burglary charge, and the matter was set for trial on that charge. Defendant failed to appear for trial and the trial court tried defendant in absentia, and adjudicated her delinquent. The court scheduled sentencing for a later date, but defendant failed to appear for sentencing and the court sentenced her in absentia. The appellate court held that (1) the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/1-1 et seq. (West 2000), required that minors receive, at a minimum, the same procedural rights as adults; (2) 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/113-4(e) (West 2000) required trial courts to inform adult defendants that they could be tried in absentia; (3) sentencing was an aspect of trial and the trial court informed defendant she could be sentenced in absentia when it informed her she could be tried in absentia; and (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by trying or sentencing defendant in absentia.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jose Z. (In re Alicia Z.)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 97--JA--0080. Honorable Judith M. Brawka, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 2-01-1465 was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Trial court's judgment appealed from in appeal Nos. 2-02-0395 and 2-02-0505 was reversed and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed from a decision by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) denying his motion to modify guardianship and custody of his children. In a separate appeal, the father and appellant Illinois Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) transferring guardianship of the children from DCFS to foster parents.


OVERVIEW: The father contended that the appellate court had jurisdiction to review the order denying his motion to modify guardianship and custody pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 301, 304(a), 306(a)(5). In dismissing the appeal, the appellate court concluded that it lacked jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 301 and 304, and would not entertain the appeal under Ill. Sup. Ct. In the father's appeal, he argued that the trial court should have granted him immediate guardianship and custody of the minors because, inter alia, the trial court's finding that a placement with foster parents was in the minors' best interest was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The appellate court agreed with this argument and reversed the transfer.


OUTCOME: The father's appeal from denial of his motion to modify guardianship was dismissed. The trial court's order transferring guardianship was reversed and the case was remanded.

People v. Lundy


Nos. 1-01-1295 & 1-01-2443 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 819; 779 N.E.2d 404; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1002; 268 Ill. Dec. 790



November 4, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 98 CR 9709 & 00 CR 17110.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's convictions and sentences vacated in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting him in separate proceedings of two counts each of drug possession and drug possession with intent to deliver and sentencing him, in a single proceeding, to consecutive sentences on the two pairs of counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for possession of drugs; two years later he was arrested for possession with intent to deliver. He was tried on the latter charges first, convicted on both sets of counts, and sentenced in a single proceeding, with an enhanced sentence because of his prior felony convictions, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (West 1998). He successfully challenged the simple possession convictions on grounds of insufficiency of evidence, because the State had simply failed to establish chain of custody at all, so there was no reason to suppose the plastic packets mentioned by the arresting officer had anything to do with the drugs identified by the State's expert. Defendant's argument that his convictions of possession with intent to deliver were causally related to counsel's ineffective assistance was meritless, however, because it was clear that any motions to quash his arrest or suppress the evidence seized would have been futile. Finally, the imposition of an enhanced sentence did not violate the Apprendi rule.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the convictions and sentences for possession but affirmed the convictions and sentences for possession with intent to deliver.

Graham v. Reid


No. 1-02-1827


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 1017; 779 N.E.2d 391; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 995; 268 Ill. Dec. 777



November 1, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable RAYMOND JAGIELSKI, Judge Presiding.
Graham v. Reid, 332 Ill. App. 3d 1132, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1786 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a losing political candidate, filed an action pursuant to 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-63 (West 1998) against respondents, the winning candidate, two other candidates, a county clerk, the chairman of a county canvassing board, and others, contesting the results of a primary election. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declared the primary election void and ordered a new election, and the winning candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two candidates who received the most number of votes in a primary election each received 6,934 votes, and pursuant to 10 Ill. Comp Stat. Ann. 5/22-4 (West 1998), the state board of elections broke the tie by lot. The losing candidate filed an action contesting the election and a trial court ordered election authorities to conduct a recount. During the recount, ballots cast in 1 of the 119 precincts where voting occurred could not be located, and the losing candidate also claimed that voters in other precincts did not have their votes counted because they were given the wrong ballot. The trial court considered this evidence and ordered a new election. The appellate court held that (1) the United States Supreme Court's Bush decision did not require that anytime a recount was ordered and ballots were missing, a new election must be held; (2) the returns provided by election officials were prima facie evidence of the election results; (3) the errors alleged were garden variety election irregularities that did not rise to the level of a constitutional violation under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; and (4) the trial court erred by ordering a new election.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, vacated the trial court's order requiring a new election, and remanded the case with directions that the trial court complete the process of recounting the votes.

Wright v. Bd. of Educ.


1-01-2348


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


335 Ill. App. 3d 948; 781 N.E.2d 386; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 997; 269 Ill. Dec. 589



November 1, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 15, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 L 11894. Honorable Mary Mulhern, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parent filed a personal injury action against defendant Board of Education of the City of Chicago (Illinois), alleging that she was injured because the Board failed to warn her of a dangerous condition on its property and violated the Cook County (Illinois) Building Ordinance and the Chicago (Illinois) Municipal Code. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the action and the parent appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a parent was leaving a school where she had gone to register her children, she missed a step that was outside a door leading out of the school, stepped onto the ground at a level lower than the step, and fractured her ankle. The parent claimed that she fell because the step was not 10 inches wide, the placement of a desk by the door interfered with egress, the step had no handrail, and the Board failed to warn her about the danger. The Board filed a motion for summary judgment, arguing that the parent's lawsuit was time-barred by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214(b) (West 1998), the statute of repose for construction. The appellate court held that the Illinois Premises Liability Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 130/1 et seq. (West 1998), did not impose a duty on the Board to change the step as construction standards changed, the Board could rely on 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/13-214(b) (West 1998) to defend the parent's action, and the parent's action was time-barred under § 13-214(b) because it was filed more than 10 years after the step was constructed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Kastman


No. 2-00-1425


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


335 Ill. App. 3d 87; 779 N.E.2d 333; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 988; 268 Ill. Dec. 719



October 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 6, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Kastman, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2322 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 93-CM-4621. Honorable Donald H. Geiger, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Kastman, 309 Ill. App. 3d 516, 722 N.E.2d 1202, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 4, 243 Ill. Dec. 133 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was adjudicated a sexually dangerous person. Years later, appellant filed an application for recovery, pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 205/9 (West 1998), in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois). The trial court denied the application. Appellant timely sought review following the trial court's denial of his posttrial motion.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the application because the psychiatrist, the warden, and the social worker who signed appellant's psychologist report believed that appellant was still sexually dangerous, and the trial court found appellant's testimony did not overcome that factor. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred when it placed the burden of proof on appellant to show that he was no longer sexually dangerous. The burden of proof belonged on the State to show beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant remained sexually dangerous. Additionally, the appellate court found that (1) the psychologist who signed the report was not required to hold a license; (2) because the psychiatrist received no remuneration for his services other than his salary and because his socio-psychiatric reports were prepared solely on behalf of the corrections department, he was exempt from the statutory licensing requirement; (3) the trial court, upon a challenge, had to ensure that the psychologist and the sociologist preparing the socio-psychiatric report were qualified to prepare the report; and (4) the Illinois Sexually Dangerous Persons Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich


No. 2-00-0943


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 488; 778 N.E.2d 750; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 970; 268 Ill. Dec. 484



October 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 22, 2002.
Appeal granted by Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 202 Ill. 2d 672, 787 N.E.2d 174, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 202, 272 Ill. Dec. 359 (2003)
Reversed by Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 356 (Ill., Feb. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rule 23 Order of June 27, 2002, Withdrawn October 21, 2002. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98--MR--75. Honorable John R. Goshgarian, Judge, Presiding.
Vill. of Lake Villa v. Stokovich, 800 N.E.2d 889, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 3918, 279 Ill. Dec. 601 (Ill. App. Ct., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Village of Lake Villa (Illinois) filed an action, pursuant to 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-31-1 (West 1996) and the Lake Villa Village Code § 8-4-1 (1994), against defendants, a trustee and a property owner, seeking an order authorizing demolition of a building and fines for alleged violations of the Lake Villa Village Code tit. 8. The Circuit Court of Lake County(Illinois) entered an order of demolition, and the defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Village officials posted notice on a building indicating that it was unsafe, abandoned, dilapidated, and animal infested. Three and a half months later, the village's attorney sent the property owners a letter stating that the building was in a dangerous and unsafe condition and had to be demolished within 30 days. When the owner did not demolish the building, the village filed suit, pursuant to § 11-31-1 of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-31-1 (West 1996), seeking an order authorizing demolition. On appeal from a trial court's judgment authorizing demolition, the appellate court held that § 11-31-1 was unconstitutional to the extent it authorized the village to demolish privately-owned buildings or to require a person or entity that owned private property to demolish a building without giving the owner the option of repairing the building within a reasonable period of time.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded with directions that the trial court allow defendants a reasonable period of time in which to make repairs to their building before it ordered demolition.

 

1594 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Callahan


NO. 4-99-1043


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 636; 778 N.E.2d 737; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1069; 268 Ill. Dec. 471



October 18, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 12, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Callahan, 202 Ill. 2d 677, 787 N.E.2d 175, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 271, 272 Ill. Dec. 360 (Feb. 5, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Callahan, 204 Ill. 2d 666, 792 N.E.2d 309, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1111, 275 Ill. Dec. 78 (June 4, 2003)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Callahan, 2017 IL App (4th) 150576-U, 2017 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2242 (Nov. 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Jersey County. No. 97CF147. Honorable Ronald F. Robinson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, as modified, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Jersey County (Illinois) of first degree murder and four counts of armed violence. He was sentenced to a term of natural life imprisonment for the murder conviction and 30 years for each conviction for armed violence, to be served consecutively to each other and to the sentence of natural life. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defense counsel did not object to armed violence charges filed on the eve of the trial of murder and attempted murder. The appellate court held the armed violence charges were not included offenses of attempted murder as they contained elements not required for an attempted murder conviction. Under the charging-instrument approach, it did not matter if the additional elements were at issue at trial. Defense counsel was ineffective for not moving to dismiss the armed violence charges on speedy-trial grounds; since dismissal would have been granted and defendant would not have been convicted of these charges, he proved prejudice. Given the overwhelming evidence of defendant's voluntary and willful actions, defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to tender a recklessness instruction along with an involuntary manslaughter instruction. The case did not hinge on defendant's mental state. The trial court's finding that defendant's behavior was exceptionally brutal and indicative of wanton cruelty had to be charged and submitted to the jury; since it was not, defendant's life sentence had to be modified to the statutory maximum for first degree murder, which was 60 years.


OUTCOME: Defendant's armed violence convictions were reversed, and his life sentence was reduced to 60 years. His first degree murder conviction was affirmed.

People v. Singmouangthong


No. 2-01-0751


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 542; 778 N.E.2d 390; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 971; 268 Ill. Dec. 404



October 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 99--CF--2915. Honorable Rosemary Collins, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) of reckless homicide. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(b) (West 1998), a defendant under the influence of alcohol at the time of a reckless homicide was presumed reckless unless disproved by contrary evidence. The appellate court held this provision unconstitutionally compelled the jury to find defendant was reckless and shifted the burden to him to prove otherwise. It was severable from the rest of the reckless homicide statute as it was adopted at a different time, the rest of the statute could operate without it, and it was not so intertwined with the rest of the statute that the legislature intended the statute to stand or fall as a whole. The trial court's exclusion of defendant's character evidence was harmless as his offer of proof was vague and the State had ample contradictory evidence. Defendant's requested use of charts during closing to show that subtracting 30 from 59.75 yielded 29.75 was unnecessary. His proposed instruction that excessive speed alone did not prove recklessness was correctly refused as it was misleading in that it did not convey a proper analysis of applicable law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1596 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beronich


No. 2-01-0665


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 536; 778 N.E.2d 385; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 933; 268 Ill. Dec. 399



October 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 90--CF--516. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for murder and other offenses. Defendant entered a negotiated guilty plea. The circuit court sentenced defendant to 50 years' imprisonment. Defendant's post-conviction petition was dismissed. Defendant's second amended petition for post-conviction relief was denied by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that his guilty plea to first-degree murder was involuntary because the court admonished him that he was eligible for an extended-term sentence but the extended-term sentencing statute was later rendered unconstitutional by Apprendi. In affirming defendant's conviction, the appellate court noted that the trial court admonishment that defendant was eligible for extended-term sentences was true under the then-existing law and remained true. Thus, the appellate court concluded that defendant's argument reduced to one that, had he known that he had the right to have a jury, rather than the trial court, decide whether his conduct was brutal and heinous, he would have rejected the State's plea offer and insisted on going to trial. On that argument, the appellate court held that defendant's plea was voluntary in light of law that existed when the plea was entered into. The appellate court noted that the voluntary plea could not be invalidated by late changes in the law.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's second amended post-conviction petition was affirmed.

 

1597 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barwig


NO. 5-01-0356


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 738; 778 N.E.2d 350; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 927; 268 Ill. Dec. 364



October 9, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. Nos. 01-DT-55, 01-DT-56, 01-TR-887, & 01-TR-888. Honorable Leo T. Desmond, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited for, inter alia, driving while under the influence of alcohol and driving while having a blood alcohol concentration in excess of .08. Defendant petitioned to rescind his statutory summary suspension and alleged that 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/7-4-8 (West 2000) was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) denied defendant's petition and declined to find a constitutional violation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the circuit court erred in denying his petition to rescind his statutory summary suspension. Defendant claimed that because the officer failed to log the purported test or tests in the official records of the sheriff's department, the tests were inadmissible hearsay. In affirming the circuit court's judgment, the appellate court concluded that Ind. Admin. Code tit. 77, § 510.20 (1999) contained no requirement that the breath test be listed in a logbook to be accurate or trustworthy. In addition, defendant failed to show to that the test was not preformed in accordance with the regulations. Defendant also claimed that he made out a prima facie case for recission because the officer left the room during the 20-minute observation period in violation of Ind. Admin. Code tit. 778 § 510.60(a)(1) (1999). The appellate court found that even if the officer left the room, he observed defendant the entire time required, though glass. Finally, defendant argued that the statutory police district was unconstitutional. The appellate court disagreed, noting that defendant's right as a voter was not extinguished by the legislature's creation of a police district.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's denial of defendant's petition to rescind his statutory summary suspension and his constitutional challenge was affirmed.

People v. Thoennes


NO. 4-00-0776


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


334 Ill. App. 3d 320; 777 N.E.2d 1075; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 938; 268 Ill. Dec. 152



October 9, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 6, 2002. Application for Rehearing Denied October 9, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 1056.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 99CF1482. Honorable Donald D. Bernardi, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, McLean County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of the offense of false personation of a peace officer in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/32-5.1 (West 1998). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A woman and her friend were driving in a vehicle. They noticed two males in a different car driving next to them. Upon approaching a set of railroad tracks, the other car swerved in front of the woman's vehicle. The woman had to brake hard" The woman then followed the other car to get a license plate number. Both vehicles stopped in a residential neighborhood. The passenger of the car, identified as defendant, exited the vehicle and came up to the woman's window. An angry conversation took place. After telling defendant and the other car's driver that she wanted the license plate number, the woman said that defendant stated he was a police officer. The woman did not believe the two males were police officers. The other car's driver entered his car and pulled out what appeared to be a badge. Defendant was arrested. He was then found guilty in a jury trial of false personation of a peace officer in violation of § 32-5.1. After a judgment of conviction was entered against him, the appellate court found that the statute was not unconstitutional as it violated neither his substantive due process rights nor sufficiently chilled free speech.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jones


No. 1-00-3941


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 420; 778 N.E.2d 234; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 902; 268 Ill. Dec. 248



September 30, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Criminal Division Honorable John J. Divane, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of telephone harassment. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Criminal Division (Illinois), sentenced defendant to two years' conditional discharge with a mental health examination, and defendant was ordered not have any unlawful contact with her former attorney. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was based on telephone contact she had with the attorney representing her in a civil action. On appeal, defendant contended that she was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the State failed to prove that she made the telephone call for the specific purpose of making a threat. The appellate court noted first that defendant's intent should be measured at the time she placed the call to the attorney. Thus, the appellate court concluded that, based upon the totality of the surrounding circumstances, and the reasonable inferences that could be drawn therefrom, the evidence supported the finding that defendant intended to threaten the attorney at the time the call was placed. Under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 135/1-1(2) (West 2000), the court was not required to consider whether defendant's threat was reasonable, but, rather, whether her subsequent conduct was evidence of her intent at the time she placed the phone call.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for telephone harassment was affirmed.

 

1600 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. Ill. Int'l Port Dist.


No. 1-01-0488


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 462; 778 N.E.2d 705; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 909; 268 Ill. Dec. 439



September 30, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph N. Casciato, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sued appellee port district, and others, in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) regarding the decedent's death after falling from the port district's dock. The trial court dismissed the widow's complaint, and she appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent worked on a dock maintained by the port district, from which he fell into a river and drowned. The appellate court held the port district was immune from liability for the fall, under 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/3-110 (West 2000), because its authority and responsibility did not extend to the river. It was a creature of statutes, rules and regulations which defined its operational parameters. Its responsibility did not extend beyond the maintenance of port, harbor, and water and land terminal facilities to control of the river in which the decedent drowned. The decedent was not a third party beneficiary of the license agreement between his employer and the port district, which required the port district to maintain the dock from which he fell, as that agreement made no mention of him or any longshoreman. 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 10/3-110 (West 2000) did not violate the Illinois Constitution's special legislation clause, as it treated all municipalities near the water in the same manner, so the trial court did not abuse its discretion in declining to allow the widow to amend her complaint to include that argument.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.
